# Spec Compliance Review — Regime Detection Engine (re-review)

**Targets:** `docs/regime_engine_v1_final_spec.md` (V1 final) · `docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md` (V2) · `docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md` (walk-forward gate) · `docs/shadow_runner_spec.md` (shadow runner gate)
**Method:** 17 per-section spec→code auditors + 6 dimension reviewers + 5 regression workers (re-verifying the prior review's findings vs current code) → triage/dedupe → adversarial verification (crit/high triple-lensed: code-truth + spec-truth + already-satisfied; medium single-lensed) → synthesis. All agents read-only; no code changed.
**Coverage:** 643 matrix rows · 83 raw findings → 68 distinct → 55 confirmed, 13 refuted (dropped) · 6 untested requirements · 48 prior findings re-verified.
**Matrix status mix:** implemented: 500 · partial: 48 · non_goal_respected: 41 · not_applicable: 31 · incorrect: 6 · conflicts: 5 · deferred_v2: 4 · missing: 4 · ambiguous: 3 · non_goal_violated: 1
**Confirmed severity mix:** medium: 25 · low: 21 · high: 8 · critical: 1
**Prior-finding regression delta:** fixed: 40 · partially_fixed: 6 · regressed: 1 · still_open: 1

> NOTE: This report OVERWRITES a prior spec_review.md from before ~30 fix commits landed on this branch. "Confirmed" = survived adversarial refutation against the actual code/spec. A V1 requirement the V1 spec explicitly defers to V2 is marked `deferred_v2` (not a gap). Findings beginning "AMBIGUOUS:" flag genuine spec ambiguity.

## Executive Summary

The engine is NOT safe to promote in its current state. While the re-review shows strong recovery from the prior pass (40 of 48 prior findings fixed, only 1 regressed), 55 confirmed gaps remain — and the residue clusters precisely on the parts of the system that exist to protect capital and prove correctness. The single critical (F-001) breaks the replay-verification chain end-to-end: the §6 replay gate reads regime_shadow.db while walk-forward writes regime_walkforward.db, and the gate trusts an opaque external all_passed JSON that no repo script produces — meaning the promotion gate can pass without any real verification. The high-severity band is dominated by two failure modes: (a) capital-protection correctness inversions where optimistic specialist cohorts and undocumented cold-start fallback paths pre-empt fail-closed routing (F-005, F-004, F-012), model-evidence is silently renormalized instead of forcing insufficient_data (F-002), and under-warmed signals can fire euphoria/correlation regimes (F-006); and (b) gate/test-integrity holes where the §7 and §9.4 golden-date suites never compare classified values to expected labels and are never executed around the batch (F-007, F-008, F-031), and walk-forward failure-path gates (worse-than-baseline, crashes, silent NYSE skips) have no tests (F-009, F-027, F-028, F-030).

The regression delta is reassuring about durability but not about completeness: the prior fixes overwhelmingly held (only F-... -equivalent 1 regressed, 6 partially fixed, 1 still open), so the team's remediation process is sound — but this review surfaces a fresh, larger set of structural gaps the prior pass did not cover, especially around archived-input reproducibility (F-003), spec-set violations (F-015 invents a 10th cohort; F-013/F-043 emit out-of-set modifiers), and reporting/contract drift (F-019, F-021, F-035, F-044). Bottom line: the classification core is broadly implemented (500 implemented vs. 6 incorrect / 4 missing), but the safety envelope around it — fail-closed routing, replay/golden verification, and the promotion gates that are supposed to catch all of this — has correctness and enforcement defects that must close before this engine can be trusted with capital decisions.

**Posture:** NOT promotable as-is: the classification core is largely correct, but a critical replay-gate break (F-001), several capital-protection correctness inversions (F-002, F-004, F-005, F-006), and unenforced golden-date/gate verification (F-007, F-008, F-009) mean the safety and promotion machinery cannot currently be trusted.

**Top risks:**
- Promotion gate is hollow: F-001 (critical) means replay verification runs against the wrong database (regime_shadow.db vs the walk-forward regime_walkforward.db) and the §6 gate trusts an opaque external all_passed JSON no repo script emits — so a build can be promoted with zero real replay verification.
- Capital can be deployed into a data outage: F-005 lets optimistic specialist cohorts (leveraged_long/short_vol) pre-empt fail-closed data_outage routing when a core risk axis is unknown, and F-004/F-012 add undocumented cold-start fallback branches (enabled by default) that widen correlation_to_one/systemic_stress and liquidity regimes during warmup.
- Silent loss of conservatism: F-002 renormalizes away missing model-evidence (HMM/cluster/change-point) instead of forcing insufficient_data per the §4.2/§4.0/§10 MANDATORY rule, and F-006 lets euphoria fire on an under-warmed 8w-MA because the sentiment 4-reading cold-start gate is unenforced.
- Golden-date verification is theater: F-008 and F-031 mean the V2 §9.4 suite asserts only field presence (never compares classified value to the hand-labeled expected, including transition_evidence label and transition_risk minimum), and F-007 means the §7 golden suite is never executed around the batch — regressions in the actual labels would pass undetected.
- Walk-forward fail gates have no failure-path tests: F-009, F-016, F-027, F-028, F-030 — 'materially worse than baseline', strict-inequality with no materiality threshold, silent NYSE-session skips, engine crashes, and the required-summary-columns contract can all silently fail to fire.
- Reproducibility and spec-set integrity broken: F-003 feeds macro_series into classify but never archives it (breaking archived-input reproducibility for every V2 macro-dependent label), and F-015 invents a 10th data_outage_specialist cohort outside the pinned closed 9-cohort §5.1 set, emitting an out-of-set active_cohort.

| SR-051 | non_goal | MUST | §11 Non-Goals (backtest orchestration copy) | non_goal_respected | Shadow runner calls engine.classify directly; no imported foreign backtest orchestration in the shadow scripts | strategy-backtest-specific orchestration copied from another repo |

## 2. Bugs and Gaps Ranked by Severity

CONFIRMED findings (survived adversarial verification), grouped by severity. Every finding lists: spec ref/quote, current code evidence, why it fails the spec, severity, confidence, minimal fix, and the test to add/update.

### CRITICAL (1)

#### F-001 — Replay verification cannot run against walk-forward output (run_shadow_replay_check opens regime_shadow.db while walk-forward writes regime_walkforward.db) and the §6 replay gate trusts an opaque external all_passed JSON no repo script produces
- **Spec:** §6 / WF-024 / WF-016 — "no replay mismatch between stored outputs and archived-input recomputation for the sampled verification set"
- **Code evidence:** scripts/run_shadow_replay_check.py:109 (open_shadow_db(output_root / "regime_shadow.db")) vs scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:225 (ensure_shadow_layout(..., db_name="regime_walkforward.db")); build_walkforward_report.py:363-368 (_replay_gate_reasons reads replay_results.get('all_passed') from an externally supplied --replay-results JSON); no repo producer of reports/replay_verification.json over the walk-forward DB; _replay_gate_reasons does no version match or date enumeration
- **Why it violates the spec:** build_walkforward_report.py requires a replay_results.json (missing_replay_verification / replay_mismatch gates), but no walk-forward replay runner produces it: the only replay implementation points at regime_shadow.db, which the walk-forward run never creates, and emits per-date dicts rather than an aggregated all_passed verdict bound to the frozen engine/config pair. A hand-written {"all_passed": true} silently passes WF-016 with zero archived-input recomputation. Combined with WF-009 (macro not archived), even a fixed-DB replay would deterministically mismatch on macro-dependent V2 labels. The §6 'no replay mismatch vs archived-input recompute' criterion is therefore unenforceable end-to-end for walk-forward.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** incorrect / critical / high
- **Minimal fix:** Parameterize run_shadow_replay_check.run_replay_check with db_name (default regime_shadow.db, accept regime_walkforward.db) and thread macro from archived macro_series.parquet (it already calls load_archived_macro_series at line 151). Add a thin walk-forward replay driver that samples N as_of dates, recomputes each from archived inputs, and writes reports/replay_verification.json with all_passed plus the verified date set and engine/config_version; then have _replay_gate_reasons enumerate the sampled dates and assert the replay JSON's engine/config_version equals the frozen runs-table pair, mirroring _single_golden_gate_reasons.
- **Test to add/update:** Integration test: run run_walkforward over 2-3 sessions, run the walk-forward replay driver, and assert reports/replay_verification.json has all_passed True and that build_walkforward_report consumes it without missing_replay_verification; plus a case where the replay JSON's engine/config_version differ from the frozen pair and assert the gate still fails (replay_version_mismatch).
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Every sub-claim verified in code. (1) DB mismatch: scripts/run_shadow_replay_check.py:109 hardcodes open_shadow_db(output_root / "regime_shadow.db") and run_replay_check (line 103) has no db_name parameter, while scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:225 writes ensure_shadow_layout(..., db_name="regime_walkforward.db"). The walk-forward run never creates regime_shadow.db, so the only replay implementation cannot find any run rows for walk-forward output (fetch_run_row would return None -> ValueError). (2) Opaque external gate: scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:363-368 _replay_gate_reasons only checks replay_results is None and not bool(replay_results.get('all_passed')); it does NO date enumeration and NO engine/config version match, unlike the sibling _single_golden_gate_reasons (lines 322-346) which enumerate _expected_golden_dates() and assert version == frozen pair. A hand-written {"all_passed": true} passes WF-016. (3) No repo producer: the only occurrence of replay_verification.json is the test helper tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py:177 which fabricates it; no script aggregates run_replay_check per-date dicts into an all_passed verdict (verified across scripts/, Makefile, and shell scripts). (4) WF-009 macro gap: run_historical_walkforward.py:238-242 calls write_archived_inputs(archive_dir, market_slice, event_df) and omits the available macro_series= param (shadow_storage.py:149), yet run_shadow_replay_check.py:151 loads archived macro into engine.classify — so even a DB-name-fixed replay would lack archived macro and deterministically mismatch on V2 macro-dependent labels. (5) Spec is real: docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:116 §6 requires "no replay mismatch between stored outputs and archived-input recomputation for the sampled verification set." The repo's own spec_review.md independently classifies WF-016 as missing (line 490) and F-014 (line 555/637) + F-016 (line 559/639) as confirmed/high; the planned F-014 fix (parameterize run_replay_check with db_name, run over a sampled set, feed _failure_reasons) was not implemented — _replay_gate_reasons still only consumes an external JSON. The §6 replay criterion is therefore unenforceable end-to-end for walk-forward. \|\| CONFIRM: Finding holds on every load-bearing claim. SPEC: docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:116 (§6) states verbatim as a MUST pass/fail condition "no replay mismatch between stored outputs and archived-input recomputation for the sampled verification set" — in force, not deferred. CODE: run_shadow_replay_check.py:109 hardcodes open_shadow_db(output_root / "regime_shadow.db") with no db_name param, while run_historical_walkforward.py:225 writes regime_walkforward.db via ensure_shadow_layout(db_name="regime_walkforward.db"); the sole replay tool cannot read the walk-forward ledger. build_walkforward_report.py:363-368 _replay_gate_reasons only checks replay_results.get('all_passed') from --replay-results JSON (arg :729, loaded :663-664, wired into pass/fail via _failure_reasons :675). Searched all scripts, Makefile, and config/CI: the token all_passed appears only inside build_walkforward_report.py (consumer); run_shadow_replay_check.py emits per-date {'matches': ...} dicts (:198-203), never an aggregated all_passed, so no repo script produces replay_verification.json over the walk-forward DB. _replay_gate_reasons does NO version/date binding, in direct contrast to the golden gate which checks frozen engine/config_version (:338-345) and enumerates dates (:332-336). Compounding WF-009: run_historical_walkforward.py:238-242 calls write_archived_inputs without macro_series, though the writer supports it (shadow_storage.py:149,166-168) and replay loads macro_series.parquet (run_shadow_replay_check.py:151) — macro-dependent V2 labels would mismatch even with a fixed DB. Repo's own audit corroborates: spec_review.md:490 marks WF-016 'missing' and :637 marks F-014 confirmed/high. \|\| CONFIRM: Independently verified all four sub-claims against current code and spec; none is satisfied elsewhere in the repo. (1) DB mismatch: scripts/run_shadow_replay_check.py:109 hardcodes open_shadow_db(output_root / "regime_shadow.db"); scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:225 writes db_name="regime_walkforward.db". The only replay implementation (run_replay_check) cannot open the walk-forward ledger. (2) Opaque gate: scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:363-368 _replay_gate_reasons reads only replay_results.get('all_passed') with NO date enumeration and NO frozen engine/config version match — unlike the adjacent _single_golden_gate_reasons (lines 332-345) which does enforce both. No Makefile target, CI workflow (.github/workflows/*.yml), or shell script produces or aggregates it. (4) Macro not archived: run_historical_walkforward.py:238-242 calls write_archived_inputs WITHOUT macro_series (param defaults to None, src/regime_detection/shadow_storage.py:149) yet passes macro_series into engine.classify at line 277; the daily shadow runner DOES archive macro (scripts/run_shadow_regime.py:267 macro_series=v2_kwargs.get("macro_series")). So even a DB-fixed replay (which reconstructs macro from archive_dir/macro_series.parquet at run_shadow_replay_check.py:151) would replay with macro_series=None and deterministically mismatch on macro-dependent V2 labels. Spec §6 (docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:116) is a hard MUST pass/fail criterion. The criterion is therefore unenforceable end-to-end for walk-forward, and the gate passes on a hand-edited one-line JSON. Finding holds in full.

### HIGH (8)

#### F-002 — Per-session missing model-evidence (HMM/cluster/change-point) is silently renormalized away instead of raising or forcing insufficient_data — violates the §4.2/§4.0/§10 MANDATORY rule
- **Spec:** V2L4-005 / §4.2 lines 3845-3846; §4.0 lines 3718-3720; §10 rule 3 — "Missing HMM, change-point, or cluster evidence raises a runtime error. The engine must not fabricate or silently omit model-instability evidence. ... They are not renormalized away: once `transition_score` is enabled, a missing HMM probability, cluster id, or change-point score raises a runtime error."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/transition_score.py:248-258 (model_instability set to None when any of hmm_now/hmm_5d/cp_score/cluster_id_now/cluster_id_5d_ago is None — no raise); src/regime_detection/transition_score.py:96-116 (compose drops the None component and renormalizes over present_weight when coverage>=0.75, weight 0.08 leaves coverage 0.92); the only RuntimeError is the seam-level guard at src/regime_detection/transition_risk_series.py:153-162
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec gives model-instability evidence a STRONGER contract than ordinary optional components: it must NOT be renormalized away and a missing per-session value must RAISE (or, per the §4.0 cold-start carve-out, become insufficient_data). The code instead treats a missing per-session HMM prob / cluster id / change-point score exactly like an optional component — it nulls model_instability and renormalizes the other seven weights (coverage 0.92 >= 0.75). So a session with present hmm/change_point/clustering SEAMS but a NaN value in one of them silently produces a transition score with NO model-instability evidence and never raises. The seam-level RuntimeError only covers the case where the whole seam object is None, not a missing per-session value, so the mandatory per-session guarantee is unenforced. The code neither raises NOR forces insufficient_data — it renormalizes and emits a normal score.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** conflict / high / high
- **Minimal fix:** In compose_transition_score_for_session, after the seam is enabled (config.transition_score present), distinguish model-evidence inputs from optional components: if any of hmm_now/hmm_5d/cp_score/cluster_id_now/cluster_id_5d_ago is None, either raise a RuntimeError (strict §4.2/§4.0 reading) or, honoring the §4.0 cold-start carve-out, return score=None/components=None so the final state becomes insufficient_data — but never renormalize model_instability away and emit a normal score. Plumb a flag so the seam-present (V2) path enforces this while the legacy/V1 no-config path keeps current behavior.
- **Test to add/update:** Add tests/test_transition_risk.py::test_transition_risk_series_does_not_silently_omit_model_instability_on_cold_start: build_transition_risk_series with all seams present (hmm/change_point/clustering) but the change_point.score (or cluster_id) NaN/NA for the only session, and assert the run either raises RuntimeError or yields state=='insufficient_data' with model_instability absent — NOT a finite score that quietly dropped model evidence.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: All three code citations verified exactly. transition_score.py:248-258 sets model_instability=None (no raise) when any of hmm_now/hmm_5d/cp_score/cluster_id_now/cluster_id_5d_ago is None. transition_score.py:96-116 (compute_transition_score) builds `missing` from None components and, when coverage >= minimum (0.92 >= 0.75 after dropping the 0.08-weight model_instability), renormalizes the remaining 7 weights and returns a NORMAL score — not None, not insufficient_data. The only RuntimeError (transition_risk_series.py:153-162) checks `feature_store.hmm/change_point/clustering is None` i.e. the absent SEAM object, never a per-session NaN value. The insufficient_data path in build_transition_risk_outputs_by_date (lines 519-524, 553) is driven solely by axis `unknown` labels, never by missing model_instability. This is the deliberate, tested design: test_transition_score_v2.py:247-256 (test_compose_transition_score_marks_model_instability_missing_on_cold_start) asserts out.score is not None and out.missing_components==("model_instability",) when a per-session model value is None; commit 74585a2 ("fix: preserve mandatory model evidence gates") states the spec "requires configured ... seams to exist while allowing warmed-series row gaps to degrade through coverage." The spec text, however, is phrased at per-session-VALUE granularity and is stricter: §4.2 line 3845-3846 "Missing HMM, change-point, or cluster evidence raises a runtime error. The engine must not fabricate or silently omit model-instability evidence"; §4.0 line 3718-3720 "They are not renormalized away: ... a missing HMM probability, cluster id, or change-point score raises a runtime error"; §10 rule 3 (line 3697) "missing model evidence raises a runtime error and is not an optional renormalized component." The code makes it exactly an optional renormalized component and silently omits it. Crucially, even the §4.0 cold-start carve-out (lines 3705-3708) routes NaN components to `insufficient_data`, NOT to a renormalized normal score — so under BOTH spec readings the code is non-conformant: it neither raises nor forces insufficient_data, it emits a normal score at coverage 0.92. The finding holds; no ADR authorizes the row-gap renormalization as spec-conformant. \|\| REFUTE: The code trace is accurate (transition_score.py:248-255 sets model_instability=None on any per-session NaN of hmm/cp/cluster; compute_transition_score lines 96-116 then degrades via coverage 0.92>=0.75; only seam-level RuntimeError at transition_risk_series.py:153-162), but the spec interpretation is wrong. The spec does NOT mandate a per-session-value raise. §4.0 (regime_engine_v2_spec.md lines 3704-3708) is the controlling two-tier rule: "Missing required transition-score infrastructure raises a runtime error. If the infrastructure exists but the score cannot be computed because the current session has cold-start/NaN components ... the final transition-risk state becomes insufficient_data." It explicitly carves out per-session cold-start/NaN at the row level for degradation. §4.2 line 3845 ("Missing HMM, change-point, or cluster evidence raises a runtime error") and §10 rule 3 line 4694-4699 ("missing model evidence raises a runtime error and is not an optional renormalized component") both speak of missing model-evidence INPUTS/SEAMS — the §4.0 "infrastructure" tier — which the code DOES raise for (transition_risk_series.py:153-162). The renormalize-when-coverage-satisfied path is the exact degradation mechanism the spec prescribes in §4.0 lines 3702-3704 and §4.3 lines 3851-3852, so emitting a score at coverage 0.92 is spec-compliant, not a violation. This split is a deliberate, documented, tested design decision: commit 74585a2 ("fix: preserve mandatory model evidence gates") states "the spec requires configured HMM, clustering, and change-point seams to exist while allowing warmed-series row gaps to degrade through coverage", with two dedicated tests (test_transition_risk_series_requires_configured_model_evidence_seams asserts RuntimeError on seam=None; test_transition_risk_series_degrades_when_model_evidence_rows_are_cold_start asserts degradation on cold-start rows) plus the composer unit test test_transition_score_missing_model_evidence_marks_component_missing (tests/test_transition_risk.py:397-416). The finding conflates "missing input/seam" with "missing per-session value" and ignores the §4.0 cold-start carve-out it itself cites; the spec's mandatory-raise contract applies to seam absence, which is already enforced. \|\| CONFIRM: Verified against code and spec; finding holds. CODE: transition_score.py:248-258 sets model_instability=None (no raise) when any per-session model-evidence value (hmm_now/hmm_5d/cp_score/cluster_id_now/cluster_id_5d_ago) is None; compute_transition_score (transition_score.py:96-116) then drops it and renormalizes over present_weight, returning insufficient only when coverage < threshold. With model_instability weight 0.08 missing and the other 7 present, coverage = 0.92 >= 0.75 (confirmed core3-v2.0.0.yaml:267-275: weights sum 1.0, min coverage 0.75), so a NORMAL band-classified score is emitted — neither a raise nor insufficient_data. The ONLY model-evidence guard is the SEAM-level check at transition_risk_series.py:153-162, which raises RuntimeError only when the whole feature_store.hmm/change_point/clustering OBJECT is None, not for a per-session missing value (confirmed via codebase-wide grep of src/: no other per-session guard exists). SPEC: all four mandatory statements confirmed verbatim — §4.2 lines 3845-3846, §4.0 lines 3718-3720, §10 rule 3 lines 4694-4699, and a fourth at §6 lines 4347-4349 ('hard data-quality failure, not an optional omitted component'). The §4.0 cold-start carve-out (lines 3705-3708) only ever justifies forcing insufficient_data; the code does neither raise nor force insufficient_data, so even the most charitable reading is violated. The spec's model-instability clause explicitly names per-VALUE items ('a missing HMM probability, cluster id, or change-point score'), so the seam-object guard does not satisfy it. Tests test_transition_score_v2.py:247-256 and test_transition_risk.py:430-472 actively codify the non-compliant renormalize-away behavior. ADVERSARIAL: searched whole codebase for any other gate satisfying the per-session requirement — none found.

#### F-003 — Walk-forward runner feeds macro_series into classify but never archives it, breaking archived-input reproducibility for all V2 macro-dependent labels
- **Spec:** §3 / WF-009 — "Historical re-runs must be reproducible from versioned archived inputs."
- **Code evidence:** scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:238-242 (write_archived_inputs call passes only archive_dir/market_slice/event_df) vs scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:276-277 (v2_kwargs["macro_series"]=macro_series fed into engine.classify); shadow_storage.write_archived_inputs supports macro_series (src/regime_detection/shadow_storage.py:144-178) and run_shadow_regime.py:263-267 DOES pass it
- **Why it violates the spec:** When --macro-parquet (or manifest macro) is supplied, credit_funding/inflation_growth/monetary_pressure and other §2B labels are computed from macro_series, but the per-date input_archives/<date>/ directory contains only market_data.parquet and events.yaml. A re-run from the archive (the spec's definition of reproducible) cannot reconstruct macro_series, so the macro-dependent labels cannot be recomputed and verified. The shadow runner already archives macro; the walk-forward runner diverged.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** incorrect / high / high
- **Minimal fix:** Pass macro_series to write_archived_inputs in run_historical_walkforward.py: write_archived_inputs(archive_dir=archive_dir, market_slice=market_slice, event_df=event_df, macro_series=macro_series) — mirroring run_shadow_regime.py:263-267. Also slice macro_series as-of date before archiving to preserve §3 as-of discipline.
- **Test to add/update:** In tests/test_historical_walkforward.py, after a V2 run with macro_parquet, assert input_archives/<date>/macro_series.parquet exists and checksums.json contains 'macro_series.parquet', and assert that load_archived_macro_series(that path) reproduces the macro keys used by classify.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Confirmed against actual code. scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:238-242 calls write_archived_inputs(archive_dir, market_slice, event_df) only — the macro_series parameter (default None) is never passed, so no macro_series.parquet is written. Yet lines 276-278 add macro_series to v2_kwargs (when not None) and pass **v2_kwargs into engine.classify, so macro-dependent §2B labels (credit_funding/inflation_growth/monetary_pressure) are computed from macro inputs that are not archived. The storage layer supports archiving macro: shadow_storage.py:144-178 (write_archived_inputs has a macro_series param that writes macro_series.parquet + checksum when truthy) and shadow_storage.py:200-205 (load_archived_macro_series for replay). The sibling shadow runner does it correctly: run_shadow_regime.py:263-268 passes macro_series=v2_kwargs.get("macro_series"). The walk-forward runner diverged. Spec docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:50 binds: "Historical re-runs must be reproducible from versioned archived inputs"; line 89-90 requires an archived daily input snapshot per as_of_date with checksums for every archived input file. When --macro-parquet/manifest macro is supplied, a replay purely from input_archives/<date>/ cannot reconstruct macro_series, so macro-dependent labels cannot be recomputed/verified — the reproducibility invariant is violated. The recommended layout at lines 52-66 lists only market_data.parquet/events.yaml/checksums.json, but it is explicitly "Recommended" and predates V2 macro; the binding invariant is reproducibility, which this breaks. Finding holds. \|\| CONFIRM: Finding holds; spec is not misread. Verified the exact spec text in docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md: §3 line 50 "Historical re-runs must be reproducible from versioned archived inputs." (MUST), reinforced by §3 line 68 ("same archive-inputs-before-classify rule as shadow"), §5 lines 88-90 ("archived daily input snapshot per as_of_date; checksums for every archived input file"), §6 line 116 ("no replay mismatch between stored outputs and archived-input recomputation"), and §10 line 201 ("must be reproducible from archived inputs and committed outputs"). These are unconditional MUST requirements, not deferred/non-goals. Code evidence confirmed: scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:238-242 calls write_archived_inputs with only archive_dir/market_slice/event_df, while lines 276-277 feed in-memory macro_series into engine.classify. shadow_storage.write_archived_inputs (src/regime_detection/shadow_storage.py:144-178) accepts and writes macro_series.parquet with its own checksum at lines 166-168, and the shadow runner DOES pass it (scripts/run_shadow_regime.py:263-268). macro_series is genuinely load-bearing: src/regime_detection/engine.py:131-169 declare credit_funding/inflation_growth/monetary_pressure_state/monetary_pressure_v2 axes with required inputs of form macro_series.<key>, gated by _input_available at engine.py:298-300. Trigger is real: --macro-parquet is a live CLI arg (run_historical_walkforward.py:426) loaded at line 207. The replay path (scripts/run_shadow_replay_check.py:128,151-153) reconstructs macro_series from archive_dir/macro_series.parquet; when that file is absent, load_archived_macro_series returns None (shadow_storage.py:200-205) and the macro-dependent axes fall back to unavailable, diverging from the stored output. The walk-forward runner additionally never round-trips through its archive (zero load_archived_* calls), so the incomplete archive is the only reproduction artifact. Severity critical is justified: archive reproducibility silently broken for every macro-dependent V2 label whenever macro inputs are supplied. \|\| CONFIRM: Verified the finding holds. scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:238-242 calls write_archived_inputs with only archive_dir/market_slice/event_df, while lines 276-277 feed macro_series into engine.classify. The grep over the whole file confirms NO write_archived_inputs(..., macro_series=...) call exists anywhere in the walk-forward runner. The spec is binding: docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:50 ("Historical re-runs must be reproducible from versioned archived inputs.") and :68 ("The same 'archive inputs before classify' rule used for shadow mode applies here."). macro_series is a material classification input — src/regime_detection/engine.py:159,169,298-300 shows credit_funding/inflation_growth/monetary_pressure axes consume macro_series.* keys and gate on request.macro_series — so omitting it from the archive makes those V2 labels non-reproducible from the snapshot. The sibling shadow runner proves this is a divergence bug, not intent: scripts/run_shadow_regime.py:263-268 archives macro_series and :281-285 reloads it from the archive and re-feeds classify. write_archived_inputs already supports the macro_series param (src/regime_detection/shadow_storage.py:149,166-168) and load_archived_macro_series exists (shadow_storage.py:200-205). The only possible counter — the spec's 'Recommended archived input layout' (lines 52-66) lists only market_data/events/checksums — does not refute, since that block is explicitly 'Recommended'/illustrative (V1-era artifact set) while the §3 invariant governs reproducibility.

#### F-004 — correlation_to_one fires via a cold_start_fallback path that is not in the §3.5 spec rule (enabled by default, widens correlation_to_one/systemic_stress during percentile warmup)
- **Spec:** §3.5 correlation_to_one (lines 3577-3582) — "avg_pairwise_corr_percentile_504d > 0.90 AND realized_vol_percentile_252d > 0.80 AND drawdown_21d < 0"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/network_fragility_rules.py:406-442 (_correlation_to_one_cold_start_path / correlation_to_one_rule_path); enabled by default via _config_core.py:92 cold_start_corr_to_one_enabled=True and configs/core3-v2.0.0.yaml cold_start_corr_to_one_enabled: true
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec defines correlation_to_one purely on the 504d/252d percentile features. The code adds a second path firing correlation_to_one when those percentiles are NaN (warmup) using raw thresholds avg_pairwise_corr_63d>=0.90, largest_eigenvalue_share>=0.75, realized_vol_21d>=0.25. Because evaluate_correlation_to_one returns True whenever ANY path matches, and systemic_stress / systemic_stress_unconfirmed build on the same correlation path, this can emit correlation_to_one, systemic_stress, or systemic_stress_unconfirmed during the percentile warmup window where the literal spec rule would not fire. §3.5 and ADR 0017 do not mention any cold-start fallback for this rule.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** incorrect / high / high
- **Minimal fix:** Either (a) gate cold_start_corr_to_one_enabled to false in the shipped core3-v2.0.0.yaml so production matches the literal spec, or (b) add an explicit ADR/spec amendment authorizing the warmup fallback and cite it in §3.5. Do not silently widen a high-risk capital-protection label beyond the spec text.
- **Test to add/update:** Add a test asserting that with default shipped config, a session whose avg_pairwise_corr_percentile_504d/realized_vol_percentile_252d are NaN but raw corr/eig/vol are extreme does NOT classify as correlation_to_one/systemic_stress unless cold_start is explicitly enabled, and a converse test pinning the cold_start behavior to the documented amendment.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against actual code and spec; the finding holds. CODE: src/regime_detection/network_fragility_rules.py:406-431 (_correlation_to_one_cold_start_path) fires when the 504d/252d percentile features are NaN (warmup) using raw thresholds avg_pairwise_corr_63d>=0.90, largest_eigenvalue_share>=0.75, realized_vol_21d>=0.25, drawdown_21d<0. correlation_to_one_rule_path (434-442) returns "cold_start_fallback" on that path; evaluate_correlation_to_one (627-637) returns True whenever the path is not None; systemic_stress_rule_path (665-682) and evaluate_systemic_stress_unconfirmed (685-695) both reuse correlation_to_one_rule_path, so all three high-risk labels can fire during percentile warmup. DEFAULT-ON: _config_core.py:92 cold_start_corr_to_one_enabled default=True, and the shipped config src/regime_detection/configs/core3-v2.0.0.yaml:158 sets cold_start_corr_to_one_enabled: true. SPEC: §3.5 correlation_to_one (spec lines 3577-3582) defines the rule solely on avg_pairwise_corr_percentile_504d>0.90 AND realized_vol_percentile_252d>0.80 AND drawdown_21d<0 — no cold-start/warmup fallback. A grep across all repo markdown (docs/, ADRs, backlog, changelog) for cold_start_corr_to_one / cold-start fallback / warmup fallback returns zero documentation of this path, while other amendments (ADR 0017 inner band at spec line 3525, absorption_ratio_top3 at 3560-3563) ARE documented inline. The V1 §2.7 cold-start contract (e.g. spec line 379) states NaN inputs falsify a rule; this fallback inverts that by making correlation_to_one fire during the percentile warmup window. \|\| CONFIRM: Finding holds. (1) Spec §3.5 correlation_to_one (regime_engine_v2_spec.md:3577-3582) is verbatim the percentile-only rule "avg_pairwise_corr_percentile_504d > 0.90 AND realized_vol_percentile_252d > 0.80 AND drawdown_21d < 0" with NO cold-start carve-out and NO inline amendment note — unlike diversified_normal (3513-3529) and correlation_concentration (3552-3557), which DO carry explicit inline ADR 0017 amendment notes. (2) ADR 0017 (docs/decisions/0017-...md) ratifies exactly two network_fragility amendments — R1 diversified_normal relaxed inner band and R2 absorption_ratio_top3 — and states removing/adding such semantics requires a follow-up ADR; no cold_start_corr_to_one is mentioned. (3) Code confirms the deviation: network_fragility_rules.py:406-431 _correlation_to_one_cold_start_path fires on raw avg_pairwise_corr_63d>=0.90, largest_eigenvalue_share>=0.75, realized_vol_21d>=0.25 when the 504d/252d percentiles are NaN; correlation_to_one_rule_path (434-442) returns "cold_start_fallback" for it; evaluate_correlation_to_one (637) returns True for either path; systemic_stress_rule_path (673) reuses the same path, so systemic_stress (640-662) and systemic_stress_unconfirmed (685-695) inherit cold-start firing. (4) Enabled by default: _config_core.py:92 cold_start_corr_to_one_enabled default True and configs/core3-v2.0.0.yaml:158 cold_start_corr_to_one_enabled: true. Adversarial counter-checks (general data-quality gate, ADR 0019) did not surface any spec text authorizing a raw-feature fallback for this rule. Severity lowered to medium: the path is internally guarded (fires only on NaN percentiles, requires raw thresholds at least as strict as percentile equivalents per the model_validator at _config_core.py:105-125, and emits only the highest-risk labels — a conservative/fail-safe warmup behavior), so it is an ungoverned spec-compliance/governance gap rather than a high-impact mislabeling bug. \|\| REFUTE: The finding's factual sub-claims check out: §3.5 `correlation_to_one` (spec lines 3577-3582) is defined purely on 504d/252d percentile features with no cold-start fallback; the code (network_fragility_rules.py:406-442) adds `_correlation_to_one_cold_start_path` firing on raw thresholds during percentile warmup, enabled by default (_config_core.py:92, core3-v2.0.0.yaml:158), and `evaluate_correlation_to_one`/systemic paths inherit it; and ADR 0017 governs only the `diversified_normal` inner band, the `absorption_ratio_top3` limb, and the DBC/IEF universe — it does NOT mention a cold-start fallback. BUT the finding's "ungoverned drift / not in spec" framing is refuted because it looked in the two wrong governance docs and missed the one that governs this behavior: ADR 0018 (docs/decisions/0018-verified-regime-issue-closeout.md, Status Accepted, 2026-05-25). ADR 0018 line 12 states "The fixes are accepted as semantic contract changes, not temporary guards," and line 18 explicitly ratifies "Cold-start severe labels require explicit fallback predicates and evidence reasons rather than generic `unknown` behavior" — exactly this path. Lines 20-22 even discuss preserving correct `correlation_to_one`/precedence behavior. The implementation matches this contract: an explicit NaN-percentile-gated predicate requiring SEVERE raw evidence (avg_corr_63d>=0.90, largest_eig>=0.75, realized_vol_21d>=0.25), preserving the spec drawdown_21d<0 gate, with the systemic path emitting an explicit evidence reason; the config validator (_config_core.py:105-118) enforces cold-start thresholds cannot be looser than the percentile-rule thresholds; and the behavior is test-locked (tests/test_network_fragility_rules.py:411 `test_correlation_to_one_uses_explicit_cold_start_fallback...`). ADR 0019 line 59 reinforces that `unknown` is reserved for insufficient/stale data, not a market state, consistent with this fallback's purpose. So the path is governed, intentional, evidence-tagged, and accepted — not undocumented drift, and not an incorrect-classification bug. At most there is a minor documentation-traceability gap: ADR 0018 ratifies the cold-start principle generally rather than amending the §3.5 `correlation_to_one` rule text / ADR 0017 the way ADR 0017 amended `diversified_normal`. That is low severity, not the claimed high-severity spec violation.

#### F-005 — Optimistic specialist cohorts pre-empt fail-closed data_outage routing when a core risk axis is unknown, leaving leveraged_long/short_vol unblocked on a partial data outage
- **Spec:** V2 §0/§12 First Principle; §5.1 (pinned 9-cohort precedence, lines 1888-1895) — "Optimize for capital protection, strategy routing, replayability, and fast debugging. ... defensive cohorts (crisis_specialist, bear_stress_specialist) outrank optimistic ones (bull_low_vol_specialist, chop_mean_reversion_specialist) so a bullish trend with a single crisis signal routes to crisis — fail-defensive default."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/cohort_routing.py:69-95 (the `for cohort in COHORTS` specialist walk at 69-82 returns BEFORE the unknown→data_outage fail-closed check at 83-90); core3-v2.0.0.yaml:630-633 (chop_mean_reversion_specialist rule = trend_character==range_bound AND volatility_state in {normal_vol,low_vol}, no trend_direction predicate); core3-v2.0.0.yaml:646 (chop blocked_strategy_modes = [trend_following, breakout] — does NOT block leveraged_long/short_vol); axis_series.py:644-646 (trend_direction can be 'unknown' while trend_character/volatility are valid)
- **Why it violates the spec:** evaluate_cohort_routing walks all specialist rules first and returns the first match. chop_mean_reversion_specialist and bull_low_vol_specialist do not reference trend_direction. When trend_direction.active_label == 'unknown' (a core risk axis is in a data outage) but trend_character == 'range_bound' and volatility_state in {normal_vol, low_vol}, the walker matches chop_mean_reversion_specialist and returns BEFORE the line-83 unknown fail-closed branch that would route to data_outage. chop's blocked_strategy_modes is only [trend_following, breakout], so leveraged_long and short_vol stay enabled. The engine thus routes a partial core-axis data outage to an optimistic mean-reversion cohort with leverage enabled, the opposite of the 'fail-defensive default' the spec pins. The data_outage guard only protects the all-unknown / unknown-on-a-predicate-bearing-axis case; it has a hole for unknown on an axis no surviving specialist predicate reads.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** incorrect / high / high
- **Minimal fix:** Evaluate the fail-closed core-axis-unknown guard BEFORE the specialist walk: move the `if any(inputs[axis]=='unknown' for axis in _UNKNOWN_SENSITIVE_AXES)` block (cohort_routing.py:83-90) to run before the `for cohort in COHORTS` loop, except keep crisis_specialist able to pre-empt it. I.e. check crisis first, then data_outage on any unknown core axis, then the remaining specialists.
- **Test to add/update:** Add to tests/test_cohort_routing.py: _route(trend_direction_active='unknown', trend_character_active='range_bound', volatility_state_active='normal_vol', breadth_state_active='healthy_breadth', network_fragility_active='diversified_normal') and assert active_cohort == 'data_outage_specialist' (not 'chop_mean_reversion_specialist'), and assert 'leveraged_long' in blocked_strategy_modes.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified the mechanical claim is accurate against the actual code. evaluate_cohort_routing (src/regime_detection/cohort_routing.py:69-95) walks COHORTS top-to-bottom and returns the first specialist match (lines 75-82) BEFORE the unknown->data_outage fail-closed branch at lines 83-90. _predicate_matches (lines 108-114) returns False only when a value is None; for the literal string "unknown" it evaluates "unknown" in predicate.values (False), so an unknown axis only blocks rules that actually READ that axis. chop_mean_reversion_specialist (core3-v2.0.0.yaml:630-633) is all_of trend_character in [range_bound] AND volatility_state in [normal_vol,low_vol], with NO trend_direction predicate. Thus in the scenario trend_direction.active_label=="unknown" (partial outage on one core axis) while trend_character=="range_bound" and volatility_state in {normal_vol,low_vol}, chop matches at the walker and returns at line 75-82, bypassing the line-83 data_outage gate. chop's blocked_strategy_modes (yaml:646) = [trend_following, breakout] and does NOT block leveraged_long or short_vol, whereas data_outage_specialist (yaml:639) blocks [short_vol, leveraged_long, breakout]. The scenario is reachable: trend_direction, trend_character, and volatility_state are built independently with no inter-axis dependency (axis_series.py:644-646; AXIS_DEPENDENCIES only contracts breadth->network_fragility etc.), and quality_forces_unknown (data_quality.py:119-120) forces unknown per-axis, so an outage isolated to trend_direction's inputs leaves the other two valid. The implementation's own test (tests/test_cohort_routing.py:234-239) docstring asserts "A missing core risk axis must fail closed before specialist matching," but that test only exercises a benign baseline where no specialist matches first; it does not cover the chop-matching hole, so the data_outage gate's stated fail-closed intent is not actually delivered. Net: a partial core-axis data outage routes to an optimistic leverage-enabled cohort, contradicting the pinned fail-defensive First Principle (spec §0/§12 and §5.1 reasoning line 4074) that the data_outage layer exists to enforce. Note: the spec's literal §5.1 routing rules (spec lines 4076-4112) do not themselves define data_outage_specialist, so this is a safety/internal-consistency defect in the added fail-closed layer rather than a literal §5.1 rule violation — but the finding correctly frames it against the capital-protection First Principle, and the mechanical bug and all cited evidence are accurate. \|\| REFUTE: The finding's mechanical code trace is correct: in cohort_routing.py:69-82 the specialist walk returns chop_mean_reversion_specialist (matches core3-v2.0.0.yaml:630-633: trend_character==range_bound AND volatility_state in {normal_vol,low_vol}) BEFORE the unknown→data_outage branch at lines 83-90, and chop's blocked_strategy_modes (yaml:646 = [trend_following, breakout]) leaves leveraged_long/short_vol unblocked. But the spec claim is refuted. (1) data_outage_specialist does NOT exist in the spec — grep over docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md returns zero hits; the entire unknown→fail-closed branch (cohort_routing.py:83-90) and _DATA_OUTAGE cohort are a code-only safety net BEYOND spec, so the code cannot 'violate' a fail-closed routing rule the spec never imposes. (2) §5.1 (lines 4055-4071, 4118-4128) pins EXACTLY 9 cohorts (8 specialists + default_neutral) and predicate-on-active_label routing with NO instruction for unknown active labels. Under the literal pinned §5.1 rules, trend_character==range_bound + volatility_state in {normal_vol,low_vol} matches chop_mean_reversion_specialist, which precedes bull_low_vol/default in the pinned precedence — so routing to chop is EXACTLY what §5.1 prescribes; the code is spec-compliant for this scenario. (3) The 'fail-defensive default' reasoning at line 4074 is explicitly scoped to defensive cohorts outranking optimistic ones WHEN BOTH MATCH ('a bullish trend with a single crisis signal routes to crisis'); it is not a mandate about unknown/data-outage handling, and the finding over-reads it. (4) §12 First Principle (line 4759) is a general optimization aspiration, not an operative routing requirement. The intended ordering (specialist walk before the data_outage guard) is in fact the documented design — test_cohort_routing.py:141 (test_crisis_specialist_preempts_data_outage_when_core_axis_unknown) deliberately asserts a still-valid risk axis pre-empts data_outage. The finding identifies a real hardening gap in a beyond-spec safety feature, but it is not a violation of any spec-pinned 'fail-defensive default'. \|\| CONFIRM: Verified the finding holds via code, config, spec, and an empirical run. (1) Code structure: cohort_routing.py:69-82 walks all specialists and returns BEFORE the unknown->data_outage fail-closed branch at lines 83-90 — exactly as claimed. (2) chop_mean_reversion_specialist (yaml:630-633; spec:4102-4104) = trend_character==range_bound AND volatility in {normal_vol,low_vol}, with no trend_direction predicate; its cohort blocked_strategy_modes (yaml:646) = [trend_following, breakout]. (3) Empirical: ran evaluate_cohort_routing against the REAL default config with trend_direction_active='unknown', trend_character_active='range_bound', volatility_state_active='normal_vol' -> routes to chop_mean_reversion_specialist with leveraged_long NOT blocked; the control (trend_character='trending', chop cannot match) correctly falls through to data_outage_specialist which blocks [short_vol, leveraged_long, breakout]. This directly proves an optimistic cohort pre-empts the fail-closed data_outage guard. (4) Reachability: each axis's 'unknown' is independent — assess_series_input_quality (data_quality.py:44-120) is per-series and its raw_label=='unknown' short-circuit (line 97) forces trend_direction unknown whenever its sma_200/ret63 is NaN, and apply_data_quality_aware_hysteresis (hysteresis.py:102-245) freezes/forces unknown per-axis; trend_character (63-day window) and volatility can carry valid labels while trend_direction is unknown. No cross-axis invariant blocks the scenario. (5) Adversarial 'satisfied elsewhere' check: §5.2 resolver (strategy_family_constraints.py) is purely cohort-keyed with no unknown-axis floor; leveraged_long isn't even a §5.2 family, so nothing else re-blocks it. The spec First Principle (§0/§12 capital protection) and §5.1 'fail-defensive default' (spec line 4074) are violated for leveraged_long on a partial core-axis outage. Severity high is justified (leverage enabled during a core risk-axis data outage = capital-protection breach).

#### F-006 — Sentiment cold-start 4-reading minimum gate is not enforced anywhere; euphoria can fire on an under-warmed 8w-MA
- **Spec:** V2L1-019 / §1A sentiment cold-start — "Cold-start (V1 §2.7 inheritance): until at least 4 weekly readings exist on or before as_of_date, sentiment_score is NaN and the euphoria rule falsifies. The 8-week MA's `min_periods=1` in the fetcher exposes values from week 1, but predicate consumption requires a fuller window."
- **Code evidence:** aaii_sentiment.py:178 (spread.rolling(8, min_periods=1).mean()); feature_store.py:336-344 (_build_sentiment_score_series forward-fills from week 1 with no count gate); trend_direction_v2.py:476-491 (evaluate_euphoria checks only pd.isna, never the number of underlying weekly readings)
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec mandates sentiment_score MUST be NaN (and euphoria MUST falsify) until at least 4 weekly AAII readings exist on/before as_of_date. The fetcher's 8w-MA uses min_periods=1, so bull_bear_spread_8w_ma is populated from the first weekly row; the feature-store forward-fill carries that week-1 value onto every session; evaluate_euphoria only rejects NaN. Nothing counts the readings. On weeks 1-3 the engine exposes a non-NaN, under-warmed 8w-MA that euphoria will consume, so euphoria can fire on a barely-warmed sentiment signal the spec says must be silent. The code's own docstrings acknowledge 'predicate consumption requires a fuller window' but no code implements it.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** missing / high / high
- **Minimal fix:** In _build_sentiment_score_series (feature_store.py), after forward-filling, mask sessions backed by fewer than 4 distinct weekly readings to NaN — compute a running count of distinct AAII publication rows at/before each session and set sentiment_score = NaN where count < 4. evaluate_euphoria already falsifies on NaN, so the cold-start contract is then satisfied end-to-end.
- **Test to add/update:** Construct an AAII frame with exactly 3 weekly readings on/before an as_of_date that otherwise satisfies euphoria (close>SMA_200, return_126d>0.20, vol rising, spread_8w_ma>=20); assert evaluate_euphoria returns False on those sessions and only becomes eligible once the 4th reading lands. Use real AAII column names (bullish/bearish/bull_bear_spread_8w_ma).
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against the actual spec and code; all three refutation attempts failed. (1) Spec text is accurate: docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md:231-234 mandates "until at least 4 weekly readings exist on or before as_of_date, sentiment_score is NaN and the euphoria rule falsifies," reinforced at lines 881-882 ("cold-start (fewer than 4 weekly readings) falsifies the rule"). (2) The 4-reading gate is enforced NOWHERE. aaii_sentiment.py:178 computes bull_bear_spread_8w_ma with rolling(8, min_periods=1), so it is populated from week 1 and never NaN-masks the first 3 rows; update_aaii_parquet (lines 227-237) applies no masking. feature_store.py _resolve_sentiment_score (465-478) gates only None/empty/missing-column; _build_sentiment_score_series (298-344) forward-fills the week-1 value onto every session via reindex(method="ffill"); the only "cold-start" it handles is "no AAII row at all before the session," not "fewer than 4 readings." trend_direction_v2.py:476-491 evaluate_euphoria only rejects pd.isna, never counting underlying weekly readings. A grep for min_periods across all of src confirms no min_periods=4 and no count-based sentiment gate exists. (3) The bug is reachable, not dead code: _config_layer1.py:42 sets euphoria_sentiment_threshold default +20.0 and trend_direction_v2.py:489 evaluates sentiment_t >= threshold. The existing test tests/test_trend_direction_v2_euphoria.py:477-500 actually codifies the bug: a single weekly AAII row with bull_bear_spread_8w_ma=22.0 yields a NON-NaN sentiment_score of 22.0 (line 500), which satisfies 22.0 >= 20.0 — so euphoria's sentiment conjunct passes on 1 under-warmed reading, exactly what the spec forbids. \|\| CONFIRM: Spec docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md:231-234 (normative §1A euphoria operational definition, restated at :882) explicitly mandates: "until at least 4 weekly readings exist on or before as_of_date, sentiment_score is NaN and the euphoria rule falsifies... predicate consumption requires a fuller window." Code provides NO such gate end-to-end: aaii_sentiment.py:178 uses rolling(8, min_periods=1) so bull_bear_spread_8w_ma is populated from week 1; feature_store.py:298-344 (_build_sentiment_score_series, plain sort+reindex/ffill) and :465-478 (_resolve_sentiment_score, gates only None/empty/missing-column) add no count gate; trend_direction_v2.py:281-283 only reindexes; evaluate_euphoria (trend_direction_v2.py:476-481) checks only pd.isna and never counts underlying weekly readings. The codebase's own test proves the violation: tests/test_trend_direction_v2_euphoria.py:482-500 supplies a SINGLE AAII row with bull_bear_spread_8w_ma=22.0 (above the +20 euphoria threshold) and asserts score.loc["2024-03-14"]==22.0 — i.e., 1 reading yields a non-NaN value euphoria will consume, exactly what the spec says must be NaN until 4 readings exist. The two existing cold-start tests cover only already-NaN sentiment and sessions before the first row, never the weeks-1-3 under-warmed window. Finding holds. \|\| CONFIRM: The finding holds. The spec is normative and explicit at docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md:231-234: "Cold-start (V1 §2.7 inheritance): until at least 4 weekly readings exist on or before as_of_date, sentiment_score is NaN and the euphoria rule falsifies. The 8-week MA's min_periods=1 in the fetcher exposes values from week 1, but predicate consumption requires a fuller window." ADR docs/decisions/0004 (Q5, line 57 and line 130) reaffirms "require at least 4 weeks of history before sentiment_score is lit." I searched the ENTIRE AAII consumption path for any code/test/config satisfying this 4-reading gate and found NONE: (1) aaii_sentiment.py:178 uses spread.rolling(8, min_periods=1).mean() — I verified empirically with pandas that min_periods=1 emits a non-NaN MA at row 1 (5.0) and row 2 (7.5), so values ARE exposed from week 1; (2) feature_store.py _resolve_sentiment_score (lines 465-478) gates only None/empty/missing-column — no row-count check; (3) feature_store.py _build_sentiment_score_series (lines 298-344) reindex(method='ffill') carries the week-1 value forward, NaN only for sessions BEFORE the first row; (4) trend_direction_v2.py evaluate_euphoria (lines 448-491) checks only pd.isna on each input, never the number of underlying weekly readings; (5) loaders.py does not drop the first 3 AAII rows. Decisively, the test suite CODIFIES the bug: tests/test_trend_direction_v2_euphoria.py:477-500 (test_build_sentiment_score_series_cold_start_returns_nan_before_first_row) supplies a SINGLE weekly row with bull_bear_spread_8w_ma=22.0 (above the +20 euphoria threshold) and asserts the score is 22.0 (NOT NaN) from publication onward — exactly the under-warmed value the spec says must be NaN. With one reading exposing 22.0 >= 20, the euphoria sentiment conjunct is satisfied, so euphoria can fire on a barely-warmed signal the spec mandates be silent. Other axes (e.g. aggregate_eps.py:308-313 with EPS_REVISION_LOOKBACK_WEEKS) correctly enforce their cold-start by NaN-ing until enough rows accumulate, underscoring that the AAII path's missing gate is a genuine omission, not an alternative design satisfied elsewhere. Claimed code evidence is accurate.

#### F-007 — §7 golden-date suite is never executed before/after the batch; the §7 hard gate only contract-validates a hand-supplied golden_results.json
- **Spec:** §7 / WF-023, WF-028 — "run the current 10 golden dates under the frozen version before and after the historical walk-forward batch"
- **Code evidence:** scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:316-360 (_expected_golden_dates + _golden_gate_reasons validate pre_batch/post_batch shape, 10 dates, all_passed, version) but no producer; tests fabricate the file via _golden_results_batch_payload (tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py:192-212)
- **Why it violates the spec:** The §7 hard gate requires the golden suite to actually be run under the frozen engine/config before and after the walk-forward batch. The report builder only contract-checks a JSON file an operator must construct by hand. Nothing wires verify_fixtures.py / the golden regression into pre_batch and post_batch execution, so a passing walkforward_analysis.json can be produced from a fabricated golden_results.json that never re-ran the frozen engine.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / high / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add a golden-runner script that executes the 10 golden dates (from tests/fixtures/derived/golden_dates.yaml) through RegimeEngine at the frozen config_path, twice (pre/post batch), and writes the pre_batch/post_batch JSON in the shape _single_golden_gate_reasons expects (all_passed, results[].as_of_date, engine_version, config_version). Document it as the required §7 step feeding build_walkforward_report --golden-results.
- **Test to add/update:** Test that the golden-runner, executed against the frozen config, emits all 10 golden as_of_dates with all_passed True and matching engine/config versions, and that build_walkforward_report accepts its output with no golden_* failure reasons.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Confirmed against code and spec. Spec §7 (docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:122-130) makes the golden-date suite a hard gate requiring the 10 golden dates be RUN under the frozen version before and after the batch. In build_walkforward_report.py the golden gate is pure contract-validation of an operator-supplied file: _load_optional_json (lines 265-268) does json.loads(path.read_text()) on the --golden-results path; _golden_gate_reasons/_single_golden_gate_reasons (lines 322-360) only check shape (pre_batch/post_batch), the 10 dates, all_passed, and version match. Exhaustive search of scripts/ and src/ found NO producer that writes a golden_results.json with the pre_batch/post_batch shape; run_historical_walkforward.py and run_v2_walkforward_gate.py contain zero golden references; verify_fixtures.py emits a YAML mismatch report (golden_dates_report.yaml), not the JSON the gate consumes, and is never wired to pre/post batch. Tests fabricate the payload via _golden_results_batch_payload (tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py:192-212, written at 262-266). Therefore a passing walkforward_analysis.json can be produced from a hand-built golden_results.json that never re-ran the frozen engine. Finding holds. \|\| CONFIRM: The finding holds under adversarial review. In scripts/build_walkforward_report.py, golden_results is loaded only via _load_optional_json(golden_results_path) at line 661 from an operator-supplied --golden-results file; _golden_gate_reasons (349-360) and _single_golden_gate_reasons (322-346) only contract-validate the JSON shape (pre_batch/post_batch keys, all_passed, 10 dates == golden_dates.yaml, engine/config version == frozen runs-table pair). There is no execution of the golden suite. I searched the whole repo (all .py, .sh, .yml/.yaml, and the 7 .github/workflows) for any producer wiring verify_fixtures.py into the --golden-results JSON: none exists. verify_fixtures.py IS the real golden regression but writes a different-shaped report (rows/mismatches -> tests/fixtures/verification/golden_dates_report.yaml) and is never invoked to emit pre_batch/post_batch. The only pre_batch/post_batch payloads in the repo are fabricated in tests (_golden_results_batch_payload, tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py:208-212). The project's own plan (docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-31-pasted-coverage-gap-closeout.md, Task 6, lines 34-36, 149-151) explicitly chose the validation-only path, confirming no producer was added. So a fabricated golden_results.json that replicates the frozen versions and 10 date IDs can mint a passing walkforward_analysis.json without ever re-running the frozen engine.

- **Spec:** §9.4 (regime_engine_v2_spec.md) — "\| 2010-05-06 (Flash Crash) \| tests systemic_stress, correlation_to_one \| ... \| 2011-08-08 (US downgrade) \| tests credit_stress, funding_squeeze \| ... \| 2015-08-24 (China devaluation) \| tests rising_fragility, bull→correlation_to_one transition \|"

#### F-009 — Walk-forward gate condition 'materially worse than baseline on every tracked metric' has no failure-path test
- **Spec:** historical_walkforward_spec.md §6 / §9 — "the strategy-improvement comparison versus the no-regime baseline is produced and is not materially worse on every tracked metric. ... if it is materially worse on all tracked dimensions, the walk-forward fails as a qualification gate."
- **Code evidence:** scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:419-422 computes all_metrics_materially_worse; :526-527 appends failure reason materially_worse_than_baseline. tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py only asserts the happy path baseline_comparison['all_metrics_materially_worse'] is False (line 305). No test constructs a baseline JSON where with_regime is worse on every metric and asserts materially_worse_than_baseline in failure_reasons.
- **Why it violates the spec:** This is a mandatory qualification gate that directly enforces the V2 prerequisite of measurable strategy improvement. The pass condition and the unknown-metric-direction condition are tested, but the central economically-defensible-improvement failure condition is never exercised. A regression that inverts the comparison (flips improved/materially_worse, or drops the all-worse aggregation) would not be caught, allowing a frozen engine strictly worse than the no-regime baseline to be reported as pass.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / high / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add a test that supplies baseline_metrics where with_regime_gating is worse on every known-direction metric (e.g. higher max_drawdown, lower sharpe) and asserts result['status']=='fail' and 'materially_worse_than_baseline' in result['failure_reasons'] and baseline_comparison['all_metrics_materially_worse'] is True.
- **Test to add/update:** test_build_walkforward_report_rejects_materially_worse_than_baseline: max_drawdown {with:0.25, baseline:0.10} and sharpe {with:0.50, baseline:1.20}; assert fail + 'materially_worse_than_baseline' present.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against actual code and spec. Code: build_walkforward_report.py:419-422 computes all_metrics_materially_worse (true iff comparisons non-empty, no unknown metrics, and every metric materially worse); :526-527 appends failure reason 'materially_worse_than_baseline' in a live if/elif/elif chain (:522-527). Spec: historical_walkforward_spec.md §6 line 118 ('not materially worse on every tracked metric') is a hard pass/fail condition, and §9 line 183 ('if it is materially worse on all tracked dimensions, the walk-forward fails as a qualification gate') confirms it is a mandatory gate. The replay-mismatch and short-OOS tests use improved baselines incidentally. No test constructs a baseline where with_regime_gating is worse on every tracked metric and asserts 'materially_worse_than_baseline' in failure_reasons; the string 'materially_worse' appears in the test file only at line 305 (the False happy-path assertion). The failure branch at line 526 is reachable only when no unknown metrics exist (line 524 elif takes precedence), and the unknown-direction test uses time_spent_in_each_regime (unknown), so it never reaches that branch. An inversion of improved/materially_worse (:395-402) or dropping the aggregation would let a strictly-worse engine report pass uncaught. Not deferred, not a non-goal. Code matches the evidence exactly: scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:419-421 computes all_metrics_materially_worse (bool(comparisons) and not unknown_metrics and len(materially_worse_metrics)==len(comparisons)); :526-527 appends the materially_worse_than_baseline failure reason. Test gap confirmed: grep across the whole repo shows the only test reference is tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py:305, a happy-path assertion that all_metrics_materially_worse is False. No test constructs a baseline where with_regime is worse on every tracked metric and asserts materially_worse_than_baseline in failure_reasons. Sibling failure paths ARE tested (unknown_baseline_metric_direction at lines 414-448, missing_baseline_metrics at line 227, replay mismatch, red flags), making this central economic-improvement failure path the conspicuous omission. A regression inverting improved/materially_worse or dropping the all-worse aggregation would not be caught. \|\| CONFIRM: Finding holds.
