### MEDIUM (25)

#### F-010 — NFCI weekly and first-release CPI are reindexed onto the SPY trading-day index WITHOUT method='ffill' before ffill, silently dropping any observation whose stamp falls on a non-NYSE date
- **Spec:** v2 §1A lines 226-229 (weekly→daily alignment) / §2C lines 3232-3233 (NFCI weekly→daily forward-fill) — "row with publication_date <= as_of_date (forward-fill from publication date; NEVER consult a future-dated reading)."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/credit_funding.py:331 nfci_w = nfci_weekly.reindex(spy_index).astype(float); :389 nfci_daily_carried = nfci_w.ffill(); src/regime_detection/inflation_growth.py:237-238 first_release = first_release_cpi.reindex(session_index).astype(float).ffill(). Leak-safe pattern: feature_store.py:344 aligned.reindex(session_index, method='ffill') (AAII) and inflation_growth.py:395-396 eps_revision_sorted.reindex(spy_index, method='ffill') (EPS)
- **Why it violates the spec:** AAII and EPS correctly use reindex(index, method='ffill'), carrying the latest observation with date <= each session regardless of whether the source stamp is a trading day. NFCI (week-ending Fridays) and first-release CPI (keyed by release date) instead reindex onto spy_index FIRST (no method), landing values only on exact-match dates and producing NaN otherwise, then ffill. When a weekly NFCI stamp or a CPI release date falls on a NYSE-closed day (e.g. Good Friday), that observation is dropped and the prior reading is carried — the latest-on-or-before reading is not honored. The carry is leak-SAFE (never future) but silently discards the most recent reading on off-calendar stamps, diverging from 'latest reading with date <= as_of'.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** edge_case / medium / medium
- **Minimal fix:** Use reindex(spy_index, method='ffill') for nfci_weekly (credit_funding.py:331) and for first_release_cpi/latest_cpi (inflation_growth.py:237-238, 335), matching the AAII/EPS pattern, so a weekly/release stamp on a non-NYSE date still forward-fills the latest value <= each session.
- **Test to add/update:** tests/test_credit_funding.py / tests/test_inflation_growth.py: build an NFCI (and CPI first-release) series whose latest observation date is a non-NYSE business day (e.g. Good Friday) and assert the following SPY session reads that latest value, not the prior week/month's value.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified the finding holds. credit_funding.py:331 (`nfci_w = nfci_weekly.reindex(spy_index).astype(float)`) + :389 (`nfci_daily_carried = nfci_w.ffill()`) and inflation_growth.py:237-238 (`latest_cpi.reindex(session_index).astype(float).ffill()` / `first_release_cpi.reindex(session_index).astype(float).ffill()`) both reindex onto the SPY session calendar with NO method, then ffill. The sibling leak-safe paths do use method='ffill': feature_store.py:344 (AAII `aligned.reindex(session_index, method='ffill')`) and inflation_growth.py:395-396 (EPS `eps_revision_sorted.reindex(spy_index, method='ffill')`) — finding's comparators are accurate. Empirically reproduced the divergence: on a realistic full-2024 NYSE calendar with NFCI week-ending-Friday stamps, Good Friday (2024-03-29) is both a NYSE holiday and an NFCI week-ending Friday; `reindex().ffill()` drops that observation and carries the stale 03-22 reading across sessions 04-01..04-04, whereas `reindex(method='ffill')` correctly carries the 03-29 reading forward — 4 session rows differ. Data keys confirm exposure: loaders.py:556-559 keys first-release CPI by raw BLS `realtime_start` (release date, not a trading calendar; code comment lines 546-547 states intent is 'keyed by release date and then forward-filled onto trading sessions'), and feature_store.py:887 pulls raw FRED weekly NFCI (week-ending Fridays) with no business-day snap. Spec §1A lines 226-229 ('the value carried by the latest AAII row with publication_date <= as_of_date; forward-fill from publication date') and §2C lines 3212-3213 ('nfci_weekly_carried = forward_fill(nfci_weekly, to_daily=True)', carry forward via last-known-value) both require latest-on-or-before semantics, which Pattern A violates on off-calendar stamps. The carry remains leak-SAFE (never future) but silently discards the most-recent reading whose stamp lands on a NYSE-closed day, diverging from spec and from the AAII/EPS code paths.

#### F-011 — §6.8 / §6.6 index_distance_from_63d_high uses min_periods=63, spec mandates min_periods=50, masking ~13 warm-up sessions to unknown
- **Spec:** §6.8 ETF Proxy Formulas (line 741; identical pin §6.6 line 700) / V1L1-036 — "index_distance_from_63d_high = SPY_close / SPY_close.rolling(63, min_periods=50).max() - 1"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/breadth_state.py:70 — idx_dist = spy_close / spy_close.rolling(63, min_periods=63).max() - 1
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec pins min_periods=50 inside the 63-session rolling max, so a partial window is allowed to emit a value once 50 sessions are present. The code hardcodes min_periods=63, requiring the FULL window before index_distance_from_63d_high becomes non-NaN. Because this feature is part of the `valid` mask (breadth_state.py:110) and the divergent_fragile predicate (line 112), the code's stricter warm-up suppresses ALL breadth labels (forcing `unknown`) for sessions 50-62 the spec would classify, shifting divergent_fragile/weak_breadth/healthy_breadth firing for those dates. test_breadth_state.py:98-105 pins this divergent behavior (62 sessions → all NaN).
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** incorrect / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Change breadth_state.py:70 to spy_close.rolling(63, min_periods=50).max() to match §6.8/§6.6, and update test_breadth_state.py:98-105 to assert the first non-NaN value appears at session index 49 (50th session). Verify the §6.6 PIT formula uses the same min_periods=50 for consistency.
- **Test to add/update:** test_index_distance_from_63d_high_emits_at_50_sessions: build SPY of exactly 50-60 sessions, assert index_distance_from_63d_high.iloc[49] (or position 55) is non-NaN and equals close/max(close[0..t]) - 1, and iloc[:49] all NaN (current code wrongly leaves these NaN through 63).
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified all claims directly. (1) Code: src/regime_detection/breadth_state.py:70 reads `idx_dist = spy_close / spy_close.rolling(63, min_periods=63).max() - 1` — uses min_periods=63 as claimed. (2) Spec: docs/regime_engine_v1_final_spec.md:741 (§6.8 ETF Proxy Formulas, the section compute_features actually implements) reads `index_distance_from_63d_high = SPY_close / SPY_close.rolling(63, min_periods=50).max() - 1`, and the identical §6.6 PIT pin at line 700 also mandates min_periods=50. The code's min_periods=63 contradicts the spec-pinned min_periods=50. (3) Downstream impact confirmed: build_raw_outputs (breadth_state.py:110) folds `idx_dist.isna()` into the `valid` mask, and line 112 uses idx_dist in the divergent_fragile predicate; with min_periods=63, sessions 50-62 (~13 warm-up sessions) have NaN idx_dist, forcing valid=False → label "unknown" (line 118), which axis_builders/breadth.py:167-176 maps to insufficient_history. Under min_periods=50 those sessions would classify. (4) The function is live (imported by axis_builders/breadth.py and feature_store.py as compute_breadth_features), not dead code. (5) test_breadth_state.py:98-105 (test_index_distance_from_63d_high_requires_full_window) pins the divergent behavior: 62 sessions -> isna().all(), which would fail under the spec's min_periods=50 (session 50 onward would be non-NaN). The finding is accurate on code, spec, mechanism, and the enforcing test.

#### F-012 — liquidity_gap_behavior adds an undocumented cold-start raw-level fallback branch (enabled by default) not in the §1E spec rule
- **Spec:** V2L1-052 / §1E liquidity_gap_behavior — "liquidity_gap_behavior:   gap_frequency_20d percentile_252d > 0.75   AND intraday_range_percentile_252d > 0.75"
- **Code evidence:** volume_liquidity_rules.py:107-130 liquidity_gap_rule_path: after the spec percentile branch, when percentile history is unavailable it returns 'cold_start_fallback' if gap_frequency_20d >= cold_start_liquidity_gap_frequency_20d_min (0.30) AND intraday_range >= cold_start_liquidity_gap_intraday_range_min (0.04); enabled by default (_config_layer1.py:229 cold_start_liquidity_gap_enabled default True)
- **Why it violates the spec:** §1E defines liquidity_gap_behavior solely as the conjunction of two 252d-percentile strict->0.75 tests. The implementation, enabled by default, fires the label via a second path using RAW gap_frequency_20d/intraday_range thresholds (0.30/0.04) while the 252d percentile is warming up. Per the §1E cold-start contract every other rule treats NaN percentile inputs as fall-through to unknown; this fallback instead emits the risk-rank-2 liquidity_gap_behavior label on sessions the spec rule cannot evaluate, changing which sessions carry an elevated-risk volume/liquidity label.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** incorrect / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Default cold_start_liquidity_gap_enabled to False so the shipped behavior matches the spec rule exactly, or gate the fallback behind an explicitly-opt-in non-default config and document it as an engine extension beyond §1E. The spec percentile branch already matches §1E and should remain the only default path.
- **Test to add/update:** Build inputs where gap_frequency_percentile_252d and intraday_range_percentile_252d are NaN but raw gap_frequency_20d=0.35 and intraday_range=0.05; with default config assert evaluate_liquidity_gap_behavior is False (currently returns True via the fallback). Also assert the percentile branch still fires at percentile>0.75.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Finding HOLDS. Code at volume_liquidity_rules.py:107-130 (liquidity_gap_rule_path) returns 'cold_start_fallback' when both 252d percentiles are NaN and raw gap_frequency_20d >= 0.30 AND intraday_range >= 0.04; this path is enabled by default via cold_start_liquidity_gap_enabled (Field default=True) at _config_layer1.py:229, with thresholds at lines 230-233. evaluate_liquidity_gap_behavior (line 175) returns True whenever this path is non-None, so the fallback emits the risk-rank-2 liquidity_gap_behavior label. The spec §1E (docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md:419-423) defines liquidity_gap_behavior SOLELY as 'gap_frequency_20d percentile_252d > 0.75 AND intraday_range_percentile_252d > 0.75'. The authoritative Implementation Ambiguity Log entry #40 'fully resolved' status (lines 1034-1048) describes the implementation as the spec predicate with 'NaN in either input falsifies the rule per V1 §2.7' and documents NO raw-level fallback. A grep of the spec for 0.30/0.04/raw/fallback found no sanction of a raw-threshold liquidity_gap cold-start path (the 0.30 literals all belong to avg_pairwise_corr_percentile_504d). The §10 ABSOLUTE RULE (line 4683) forbids inventing logic when the spec is silent. One inaccuracy in the finding: the why_violates claim that 'every other rule treats NaN percentile inputs as fall-through to unknown' is an overstatement — the same cold_start_fallback pattern also exists in network_fragility_rules.py (lines 410-441) and credit_funding.py. This does not refute the finding; it shows the spec-silent fallback is a broader undocumented pattern. Core claim is accurate.

#### F-013 — recovery_attempt modifier sets leverage_allowed=false, a field not in the §10.4 recovery_attempt modifier set
- **Spec:** §10.4 recovery_attempt — "`recovery_attempt` — when `transition_risk.state = recovery_attempt`: { "position_size_multiplier": 0.5, "allow_trend_following": true, "allow_buy_dip": true, "require_breadth_confirmation": true, "allow_leverage_expansion": false }"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/strategy_response.py:135-142 (line 139 `leverage_allowed = False`)
- **Why it violates the spec:** The §10.4 recovery_attempt modifier JSON enumerates exactly five overridden fields and does NOT include `leverage_allowed`. The base/default_neutral value (§10.1) is `leverage_allowed: true`. The code mutates `leverage_allowed = False` inside the recovery_attempt branch, so the emitted response for a recovery_attempt regime carries leverage_allowed=false instead of the spec-implied true. The companion test (tests/test_transition_and_strategy.py:127-128) asserts leverage_allowed is False, locking in the off-spec behavior. §10.4 also says the V2 spec governs V2-owned states, so this MAY be intentional V2 hardening, but it diverges from the literal V1 §10.4 modifier JSON.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** incorrect / medium / medium
- **Minimal fix:** Remove line 139 (`leverage_allowed = False`) from the recovery_attempt branch so the modifier mutates only the five fields the §10.4 JSON lists, leaving leverage_allowed at its default_neutral value of true; if the stricter behavior is intended, reconcile the spec JSON to include leverage_allowed. Update the test assertion accordingly.
- **Test to add/update:** Add test_strategy_response_recovery_attempt_matches_spec_modifier_fields asserting that for transition_risk_state='recovery_attempt' (with a non-bull/non-chop axis combination) the response equals default_neutral with exactly position_size_multiplier=0.5, allow_trend_following=True, allow_buy_dip=True, require_breadth_confirmation=True, allow_leverage_expansion=False and leverage_allowed=True (default unchanged).
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against the authoritative spec and code. §10.4 recovery_attempt modifier JSON (docs/regime_engine_v1_final_spec.md:1107-1116) enumerates exactly five fields — position_size_multiplier, allow_trend_following, allow_buy_dip, require_breadth_confirmation, allow_leverage_expansion — and does NOT include leverage_allowed. §10.1 base (line 1014) sets leverage_allowed: true, and §10.4 (line 1054) states modifiers are "layered on default_neutral" with only conflicting (i.e., enumerated) fields overridden, so the spec-implied leverage_allowed for recovery_attempt is true. The code at src/regime_detection/strategy_response.py:135-142 sets leverage_allowed = False on line 139 inside the recovery_attempt branch (an extra field not in the §10.4 set), and the function constructs StrategyResponse directly from these locals (lines 221-240), so the emitted response carries leverage_allowed=false. The test at tests/test_transition_and_strategy.py:128 asserts leverage_allowed is False, locking in the divergence. All three citations (spec quote, code line 139, test line 128) are accurate. Note: this branch is not exercised by the V1 frozen byte-contract (frozen fixtures show leverage_allowed: true only for non-recovery_attempt regimes), so it does not break frozen replay, but it does diverge from the literal V1 §10.4 modifier set. The finding holds.

#### F-014 — Shadow runner does not accumulate the six §10 strategy success metrics required for the V2 strategy-improvement prerequisite
- **Spec:** SR-046 / SR-047 (§10 L194-203) — "Track at minimum: strategy return, max drawdown, Sharpe, false switch rate, average detection lag, wrong-environment trades avoided ... the prerequisite is not satisfied until those metrics exist in a reproducible report."
- **Code evidence:** No shadow script (run_shadow_regime.py, run_shadow_replay_check.py, run_shadow_deadman_check.py, run_v2_shadow_ab_gate.py) computes these metrics. Grep for false_switch/detection_lag/max_drawdown/sharpe/wrong-environment in the shadow files returns nothing; comparison.py:118 only references a §9.3 A/B per-day label diff and is not wired to regime_shadow.db.
- **Why it violates the spec:** The shadow run is told it 'should also accumulate the evidence needed for the separate V2 prerequisite of measurable strategy improvement', and the prerequisite is explicitly unsatisfied until the six metrics exist in a reproducible report. The shadow outputs are classification-only JSON; none of the six metrics is produced or persisted, so the V2 strategy-improvement prerequisite cannot be met from shadow artifacts.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** missing / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add a reproducible shadow metrics report (e.g. a reports/ artifact or a metrics table) that, from the ledger + a no-regime baseline, computes strategy return, max drawdown, Sharpe, false switch rate, average detection lag, and wrong-environment trades avoided; or explicitly document where outside this repo the reproducible report is generated and link it from the shadow runner.
- **Test to add/update:** A test that runs a small multi-session shadow ledger through the metrics reporter and asserts all six §10 metric keys are present and deterministically reproduced on a re-run.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against verbatim spec and code. docs/shadow_runner_spec.md §10 (L190-203) requires the forward shadow run to accumulate six strategy success metrics (strategy return, max drawdown, Sharpe, false switch rate, average detection lag, wrong-environment trades avoided) and states "the prerequisite is not satisfied until those metrics exist in a reproducible report"; docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md §0 L17 makes "measurable strategy improvement vs no-regime baseline" a distinct V2 activation prerequisite. I read all four shadow scripts: scripts/run_shadow_regime.py:191-199,303-311 emits classification-only JSON (model_dump + v2_dependency_payload_contracts + rule_provenance); scripts/run_v2_shadow_ab_gate.py:284-354 emits a §9.3 label-disagreement markdown only; scripts/run_shadow_replay_check.py does byte-equality replay only; scripts/run_shadow_deadman_check.py + src/regime_detection/shadow_qualification.py:62-134 evaluate only the operational 252-session window. None compute or persist any of the six metrics. src/regime_detection/comparison.py:43-62 (StrategyMetrics) holds only four of the six metrics and its docstring (L54-57) states "The engine itself never computes these — they come from the strategy eval layer downstream"; comparison.py is imported only by tests/test_v2_comparison.py (grep confirmed), never by any shadow script or regime_shadow.db. ADR docs/decisions/0020-v2-prerequisite-and-shadow-scope.md (same review date) addresses F-019..F-053 but contains no decision waiving or relocating the §10 metrics-accumulation requirement, so it is not satisfied elsewhere. The finding's evidence is accurate and the gap is real.

#### F-015 — data_outage_specialist is a 10th cohort outside the spec's pinned closed 9-cohort §5.1 set (forbidden invention; emits out-of-set active_cohort)
- **Spec:** V2 §5.1 (Ambiguity Log resolution lines 1888-1895; cohort list 4055-4072); §10 ABSOLUTE RULE line 4683 — "§5.1 cohort routing pinned: 9 cohorts (8 specialist + default_neutral fallback). ... ABSOLUTE RULE: When the spec is ambiguous or silent, stop and ask. Do not invent. ... Forbidden V2 inventions ... New regime labels not in this spec"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/cohort_routing.py:35 (_DATA_OUTAGE = 'data_outage_specialist'), 83-90 (returns AgentRouting(active_cohort=_DATA_OUTAGE, ...) when any of _UNKNOWN_SENSITIVE_AXES is 'unknown'); core3-v2.0.0.yaml:639 (blocked_strategy_modes entry). No routing_rules entry; no §5.1 list, Ambiguity Log entry, or ADR contains data_outage_specialist.
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec pins exactly 9 cohorts (8 specialists + default_neutral) as a closed set and forbids inventing states/labels not in the spec; default_neutral is the universal fallback when no specialist matches. cohort_routing.py emits a 10th active_cohort value, data_outage_specialist, that no §5.1 list contains, leaking an out-of-closed-set label to downstream agent-routing consumers keyed to the 9-cohort enum and silently changing routing semantics (it blocks short_vol/leveraged_long/breakout vs default_neutral's empty blocklist). The spec-faithful fail-closed behavior under the pinned set is default_neutral (or a spec amendment), not minting a new cohort name. (The prior crisis-pre-emption concern is resolved because the COHORTS loop runs crisis first.)
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** non_goal_violation / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Either (a) raise a spec amendment / Ambiguity-Log item to add data_outage_specialist to the pinned §5.1 set before code emits it, or (b) keep the fail-closed posture but express it within the spec vocabulary — route to default_neutral while surfacing the outage through classification_coverage.safe_for_downstream / classification_status. Do not emit an out-of-set active_cohort string.
- **Test to add/update:** Add a test asserting that every active_cohort the router can return is a member of the spec-pinned closed COHORTS tuple (the 9 §5.1 cohorts) — i.e. with a sensitive axis 'unknown' and no specialist match, active_cohort == 'default_neutral' and blocked_strategy_modes == [] — so an out-of-spec cohort name fails CI until the spec is amended. (The existing test pinning the invented behavior must be replaced.)
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against actual code and spec. cohort_routing.py:35 defines _DATA_OUTAGE = "data_outage_specialist" and lines 83-90 return AgentRouting(active_cohort=_DATA_OUTAGE, ...) whenever any of _UNKNOWN_SENSITIVE_AXES (trend_direction, trend_character, volatility_state, breadth_state, network_fragility) equals "unknown". The spec pins a CLOSED 9-cohort set: §5.1 line 1888 ("9 cohorts (8 specialist + default_neutral fallback)"), cohort list lines 4055-4064 (default_neutral is "the fallback when no specialist rule matches"), and routing rules lines 4079-4112 list only the 8 specialists plus default_neutral with NO data_outage entry. §10 ABSOLUTE RULE line 4683 ("When the spec is ambiguous or silent, stop and ask. Do not invent.") and the Forbidden V2 inventions list line 4727 ("New regime labels not in this spec") prohibit this. Grep across docs/ found zero references to data_outage anywhere in the spec, and there is no docs/adr/ directory at all — confirming no Ambiguity Log or ADR sanctions this 10th cohort. The YAML config core3-v2.0.0.yaml:639 has data_outage_specialist only under blocked_strategy_modes (["short_vol","leveraged_long","breakout"]) with NO routing_rules entry, exactly as the finding states. Under the spec-faithful walker, unknown axis labels match no specialist (the YAML predicate value-lists at lines 610-637 never include "unknown"), so the correct fail-defensive result is default_neutral (empty blocklist), not a minted data_outage_specialist that silently blocks three strategy modes. The finding's acknowledgment that crisis pre-emption is NOT an issue is also correct: the COHORTS loop (lines 69-82) runs crisis_specialist first and only breaks at _FALLBACK, so the unknown short-circuit at line 83 executes only after no specialist matched (confirmed by tests/test_cohort_routing.py:141). The finding accurately describes real code behavior and a genuine non-goal/spec violation.

#### F-016 — §8.x 'materially worse on every tracked metric' uses strict inequality with no materiality threshold, so a baseline that ties on one metric and is worse everywhere else escapes the fail gate
- **Spec:** §9 / WF-026, WF-041 — "if it is materially worse on all tracked dimensions, the walk-forward fails as a qualification gate"
- **Code evidence:** scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:395-422 — improved/materially_worse use strict with_regime < baseline / > baseline; all_metrics_materially_worse requires len(materially_worse_metrics)==len(comparisons); a metric where with_regime==baseline is neither improved nor materially_worse
- **Why it violates the spec:** Two gaps: (1) there is no 'material' magnitude threshold — any infinitesimal delta flips a metric to improved or worse, so 'materially' in the spec is not modeled; (2) the all-worse fail condition is defeated by a single exact tie (a tie metric is excluded from materially_worse_metrics, making the count mismatch len(comparisons)), so an engine worse on every non-tied metric and merely equal on one passes the gate. The spec intent (fail when no material benefit anywhere) is not faithfully enforced.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Introduce an epsilon/material-delta threshold per metric for 'improved' and 'materially_worse', and treat ties (within epsilon) as non-improving so they cannot rescue an otherwise all-worse run; require at least one materially-improved dimension rather than only failing on unanimous strict worseness.
- **Test to add/update:** Test a baseline payload where with_regime ties baseline on sharpe and is strictly worse on max_drawdown/false_switch_rate/hit_rate, and assert status fail (currently it would pass).
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:395-422 and docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:118,181-183. Both claimed gaps hold. (1) Materiality threshold: lines 395-402 use pure strict inequality (with_regime > baseline / < baseline) with no magnitude threshold, so any infinitesimal delta flips a metric to improved or materially_worse — the spec word "materially" (lines 118, 183) is not modeled. (2) Tie defeats the all-worse fail gate: a metric where with_regime == baseline is neither improved nor materially_worse (it fails both strict comparisons at 396-401), so it is excluded from materially_worse_metrics yet still added unconditionally to comparisons (407-413). all_metrics_materially_worse (419-421) requires len(materially_worse_metrics) == len(comparisons), which a single exact tie breaks, yielding False. Lines 526-527 show this is the ONLY baseline fail gate, and improved_metrics (computed at 404/416) is never used to enforce the spec's pass-interpretation requirement (lines 181-182) of "clear benefit on at least one material dimension." So an engine equal on one metric and worse on every other metric demonstrates zero benefit yet passes the qualification gate. tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py:270-312 only covers the all-improved case; the tie edge is untested. Cited evidence is accurate.

#### F-017 — Dead-man monitor reports interior 252-window gaps but never alerts/fails on them (status='ok', exit code 0)
- **Spec:** SR-045 / SR-023 (§9 L185-188) — "A separate monitor checks the next morning that the previous NYSE session produced a runs row. ... No silent gaps are allowed in the qualifying window."
- **Code evidence:** scripts/run_shadow_deadman_check.py:47-62 (returns status='ok' whenever fetch_run_row for the immediate previous session is not None, attaching the qualification dict but never escalating) and :99 (main() returns 1 only when result['status']=='alert'); src/regime_detection/shadow_qualification.py:106-109 surfaces 'missing_session_gap' for interior gaps but only inside the returned payload
- **Why it violates the spec:** The whole-window contiguity scan now exists (evaluate_shadow_qualification scans 252 expected NYSE sessions backward and flags missing_session_gap / non_success_run), closing the original 'no scan at all' gap. But the deadman's alert status and exit code key only off the single immediately-previous session. Empirically: with an interior window session dropped while the immediate-previous session is present, run_deadman_check returns status='ok', qualification.qualifies=False, blocking_reasons=['missing_session_gap','insufficient_consecutive_sessions'], exit code 0. An automated monitor consuming the exit code therefore treats a window with a silent interior gap as healthy — contrary to 'No silent gaps are allowed in the qualifying window.'
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** In run_deadman_check, after computing qualification in the present-previous-session branch, escalate to a non-ok signal when qualification['qualifies'] is False and a contiguity reason is present ('missing_session_gap' or 'non_success_run' in blocking_reasons): return a distinct status (e.g. 'window_gap') and make main() return nonzero for it, and optionally insert an incident with breaks_qualification=True for the earliest gap date.
- **Test to add/update:** In tests/test_shadow_deadman_check.py add a test that records 252 sessions minus one interior session (immediate-previous present), runs run_deadman_check for the day after the last session, and asserts the monitor surfaces the interior gap as a failing signal (non-ok status / main() nonzero) rather than status='ok' with exit code 0.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against the actual code and spec. scripts/run_shadow_deadman_check.py:47-62: when fetch_run_row for the immediate-previous NYSE session is non-None, run_deadman_check enters `if run_row is not None:` and returns status="ok" UNCONDITIONALLY, attaching the qualification dict but never inspecting qualification["qualifies"] or ["blocking_reasons"]. Line 99: main() returns `1 if result["status"] == "alert" else 0`, so status="ok" yields exit code 0. src/regime_detection/shadow_qualification.py:106-109: an interior 252-window session with no runs row sets status=None and appends "missing_session_gap", breaking the scan and yielding qualifies=False — but this lives only in the returned payload. Empirical claim confirmed by reading code: interior gap + present immediate-previous session => status="ok", qualifies=False, blocking_reasons includes "missing_session_gap"/"insufficient_consecutive_sessions", exit 0. The spec (docs/shadow_runner_spec.md:188) states the invariant "No silent gaps are allowed in the qualifying window." (a MUST per spec_review.md SR-023). So an automated monitor keying off the exit code treats a silently-gapped window as healthy, contradicting the invariant. tests/test_shadow_deadman_check.py:143-166 only asserts the qualification counter is reported, never that an interior gap escalates to alert/non-zero exit — confirming the design treats it as informational telemetry only. spec_review.md:526-527 independently marks SR-022/SR-023 as "partial". Caveat (severity, not existence): the §9 "Minimum behavior" bullets literally require alerting only for the immediate-previous session, which the code does handle (lines 64-78); under nominal daily operation each new gap is caught the next morning, so interior gaps imply a previously-missed/ignored alert. Detection exists; only escalation at the alert/exit-code boundary is missing.

#### F-018 — No automated detection that a classification/threshold/config change occurred during the window — window-restart depends on a human inserting an incident
- **Spec:** SR-032 / SR-033 (§6 L147-149) — "Any classification bug fix or threshold/config change is qualification-breaking and restarts the 252-session window. ... Every qualification-breaking change must be recorded in incidents with breaks_qualification=true."
- **Code evidence:** shadow_qualification.py:53-59 _breaking_incident_dates reads incidents where breaks_qualification=1 and :95-101 resets the consecutive count when one falls in the window. But nothing detects a config/threshold change: insert_incident (shadow_storage.py:377) is only called by the replay check and the deadman monitor. A silent config edit that changes labels produces NO incident on its own.
- **Why it violates the spec:** The window-restart machinery is correct given an incident, but the spec makes recording the incident mandatory for any classification/threshold/config change, and the system provides no detector or guard. config_version is captured per run and the qualification query is keyed on (engine_version,config_version), so a config change that bumps config_version naturally starts a fresh series — but a classification logic change that does NOT bump engine_version/config_version would silently continue the same window with no incident and no break, defeating the freeze policy.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / medium / medium
- **Minimal fix:** At minimum, have run_shadow_regime record the engine_version+config_version (and ideally a config content hash) and fail-fast or auto-insert a breaks_qualification incident when the active version/hash differs from the version/hash that started the current consecutive window; document that any classification logic change must bump engine_version.
- **Test to add/update:** A qualification test where mid-window the engine_version (or a config hash) changes without an incident, asserting the consecutive counter does not silently span the change (either resets or a breaking incident is auto-recorded).
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against actual code and spec. Spec shadow_runner_spec.md §6 L147-149 reads exactly as quoted: "Any classification bug fix or threshold/config change is qualification-breaking and restarts the 252-session window... Every qualification-breaking change must be recorded in incidents with breaks_qualification=true." This is mandatory.  The code provides NO automated detector for a classification/threshold/config change. insert_incident (shadow_storage.py:377) has exactly two production callers, both verified by grep: run_shadow_replay_check.py:188 (fires only on a spot-check replay output MISMATCH, and §7 L153/L157 makes replay a separate, manually-selected, non-per-session process) and run_shadow_deadman_check.py:65 (fires only on a MISSING runs row). Neither detects a config/logic edit.  The qualification series is keyed on (engine_version, config_version) (shadow_qualification.py:23-50). Crucially, neither identifier is content-derived: config_version is a hand-set Literal["core3-v1.0.0","core3-v2.0.0"] (config.py:109), and engine_version() is derived from the hardcoded __version__="2.0.0" string (versioning.py:8-9, __init__.py:5), NOT from a hash of the classification logic. So an operator can edit an actual threshold value in the YAML or change classifier logic in source WITHOUT changing either string; _breaking_incident_dates (shadow_qualification.py:53-59) then finds no incident and evaluate_shadow_qualification (95-118) keeps counting straight through the change. The finding's partial-mitigation caveat (a change that DOES bump the version naturally starts a fresh series) is also accurate. Cited file:line evidence is correct.

#### F-019 — §5 'every output artifact must preserve run timestamp and input archive path' is not satisfied by the per-date JSON or the CSV summary
- **Spec:** §5 / WF-018 / WF-010 — "Every output artifact must preserve: engine_version, config_version, as_of_date, run timestamp, input archive path"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/wire_models.py:38-40 (RegimeOutput has engine_version/config_version/as_of_date only — no run_timestamp, no input_archive_path); scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:293-333 summary_rows include input_archive_path but no run_timestamp column; build_walkforward_report.py:111-121 _load_runs_from_db SELECT omits run_timestamp; :287-313 _per_date_provenance emits no timestamp; shadow_storage.py:48 runs.run_timestamp NOT NULL is stored but never read back
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec says EVERY output artifact preserves all five fields. The immutable per-date JSON (RegimeOutput) carries no run timestamp and no input archive path; the walkforward_summary.csv carries input_archive_path but not run_timestamp; the aggregate report never surfaces the run_timestamp the engine records in the DB. Only the SQLite runs row carries all five. So provenance is split across the DB/checksums sidecar and the run-timestamp half is not surfaced per-artifact, weakening the per-artifact reproducibility the spec demands.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add run_timestamp to the _load_runs_from_db SELECT and to each _per_date_provenance row and to the summary CSV row dict (run_timestamp is already computed at run_historical_walkforward.py:231); either embed run_timestamp/input_archive_path in the per-date JSON sidecar or document that the DB runs row is the canonical per-artifact provenance and reference its run_id from the JSON.
- **Test to add/update:** Assert walkforward_summary.csv contains a non-null run_timestamp column for every row, and that payload['per_date_provenance'][0] contains a non-null run_timestamp tying each as_of_date to a run_timestamp.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against actual code and spec. Spec §5 (docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:94-100) states "Every output artifact must preserve: engine_version, config_version, as_of_date, run timestamp, input archive path," and the immutable per-date JSON is an explicitly listed required artifact (line 88). The cited evidence is accurate: (1) wire_models.py:38-41 RegimeOutput exposes only engine_version/config_version/as_of_date/market — no run_timestamp, no input_archive_path; (2) run_historical_walkforward.py:231 generates run_timestamp but it flows only into insert_run_row (DB); the CSV summary_rows (293-333) include input_archive_path but no run_timestamp, and REQUIRED_SUMMARY_COLUMNS (build_walkforward_report.py:44-56) omits it; (3) build_walkforward_report.py:117 _load_runs_from_db SELECT omits run_timestamp, and _per_date_provenance (287-313) emits engine_version/config_version/input_archive_path/output_path but no run timestamp; (4) shadow_storage.py:48 runs.run_timestamp is NOT NULL and written (line 225) but fetch_run_row SELECTs (331-348) never read it back. _write_output_json (run_historical_walkforward.py:96-97) writes only the model payload with no provenance sidecar, so the per-date JSON carries neither run timestamp nor input archive path. The repo's own spec_review.md independently marks this exact item WF-010/F-056 as 'partial' with identical evidence and the same suggested fix (sidecar provenance file). The finding holds.

#### F-020 — NaN-leakage gate only scans numeric/JSON-float NaN and never asserts string labels stay within the unknown/insufficient_history contract
- **Spec:** §6 / WF-022 — "no NaN leakage beyond the explicit V1 unknown / insufficient_history contract"
- **Code evidence:** scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:217-240 _nan_leakage iterates only numeric summary columns (is_numeric_dtype) and JSON float('nan') paths; no check that label columns are restricted to valid labels plus {unknown, insufficient_history}
- **Why it violates the spec:** The criterion explicitly frames the allowed NaN/empty contract as the V1 'unknown'/'insufficient_history' labels. The implementation only catches float NaN in numeric cells and JSON floats. A label column that silently emits an empty/None/null string or an out-of-contract sentinel is not validated against the allowed set, so a degraded label outside the {unknown, insufficient_history} contract would pass the gate.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / medium / medium
- **Minimal fix:** Add an explicit label-contract check: for each LABEL_COLUMN in success rows, assert values are non-empty and any 'no-data' value is one of the allowed contract labels (unknown / insufficient_history), flagging anything else as nan_leakage/contract_violation.
- **Test to add/update:** Test that a success row whose volatility_state_active is empty/'' or an unexpected sentinel is flagged (status fail), while 'unknown' and 'insufficient_history' are accepted.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against the actual code and spec. Spec §6 (docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:114): "no NaN leakage beyond the explicit V1 `unknown` / `insufficient_history` contract" — the contract is fundamentally about label values surfacing missing/degraded data as the strings unknown/insufficient_history rather than as raw NaN. The implementation in scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:217-240 (_nan_leakage) does exactly what the finding claims: (1) lines 221-225 iterate summary columns but skip any column where `not pd.api.types.is_numeric_dtype(...)`, so the string label columns (trend_direction_active, trend_character_active, volatility_state_active, breadth_state_active, transition_risk_state — defined lines 21-27) are skipped entirely; (2) lines 227-239 + _json_nan_paths (lines 200-214) flag only `float('nan')` in JSON outputs. There is no validation that label columns are restricted to valid labels plus {unknown, insufficient_history}. Label columns are populated from output.<axis>.active_label / transition_risk.state (run_historical_walkforward.py:302-316), which are typed `str \| None` upstream, so a None/empty/out-of-contract label is possible. I empirically confirmed: a DataFrame with None in trend_direction_active and '' in transition_risk_state yields object dtype, is_numeric_dtype=False, and the summary loop flags ONLY the numeric transition_risk_score NaN — both label cells leak through undetected. The existing tests (tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py:586-631) only assert detection of numeric/JSON-float NaN (summary.transition_risk_score, output.transition_risk.score); none cover label-column contract validation. The cited evidence (lines 217-240) is accurate. The gap is real but bounded (defense-in-depth; partial overlapping coverage from §8 long_unknown_run / label_dominance red flags at lines 432-458), so medium severity / partial category stands.

#### F-021 — Walk-forward report omits Section 10 data-source/archive-policy, incidents/anomalies/reruns, and transition-risk evidence values
- **Spec:** WF-028 (§10 Report Contents) — "The final historical walk-forward report should contain: ... 3. data source and archive policy; ... 6. transition and false-switch summaries, including transition-risk score, primary drivers, triggered rules, data-quality status, and axis-switch counts; ... 8. incidents, anomalies, and reruns;"
- **Code evidence:** scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:533-642 (_build_markdown emits Frozen Version, Missing Sessions, NaN Leakage, Red Flags, Replay Verification, Per-Date Provenance, Label Distributions, Series Summaries, Golden Results, Baseline Comparison only); :21-27 (LABEL_COLUMNS excludes transition_risk_score/primary_drivers/triggered_rules/data_quality_status/axis_switch columns); grep for 'data source\|archive policy\|incident\|anomal\|rerun' returns no matches
- **Why it violates the spec:** REQUIRED_SUMMARY_COLUMNS validates the transition-risk evidence columns exist in the CSV, but the rendered markdown never prints their values; series_summaries only covers LABEL_COLUMNS (switch/false-switch counts), so §10 item 6's score/primary_drivers/triggered_rules/data_quality_status/axis-switch counts are absent from the report. There is also no Data Source & Archive Policy section (item 3) and no Incidents/Anomalies/Reruns section (item 8), even though the shadow_storage incidents table and checksums.json archive sidecars exist to source them.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** In _build_markdown add (a) a 'Data Source & Archive Policy' section sourced from the archive dir / checksums.json, (b) an 'Incidents / Anomalies / Reruns' section (explicit empty-list when none), and (c) a transition-risk evidence section rendering per-date or aggregated transition_risk_score/primary_drivers/triggered_rules/data_quality_status/axis_switch_count from the summary CSV.
- **Test to add/update:** Extend tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py to assert the generated walkforward_report.md contains '## Data Source', '## Incidents', and a transition-risk evidence section that prints transition_risk_score and axis-switch counts from the realistic 252-row summary fixture.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against actual code and spec. Spec §10 (docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:185-199) requires the report to contain, verbatim: item 3 "data source and archive policy"; item 6 "transition and false-switch summaries, including transition-risk score, primary drivers, triggered rules, data-quality status, and axis-switch counts"; item 8 "incidents, anomalies, and reruns". The spec quote in the finding is exact.  _build_markdown (scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:533-642) emits only these sections: header (status/engine/config/session counts), Failure Reasons, Frozen Version, Missing Sessions, NaN Leakage, Red Flags, Replay Verification, Per-Date Provenance, Label Distributions, Series Summaries, Golden Results, Baseline Comparison.  Item 6: _series_summaries (line 243-262) and _label_distribution (line 137-145) iterate LABEL_COLUMNS (lines 21-27), which contains only the five *_active/_state columns. The transition-risk evidence columns (transition_risk_score, transition_risk_primary_drivers, transition_risk_triggered_rules, transition_risk_data_quality_status, transition_risk_axis_switch_count, transition_risk_recent_axis_switch_count) appear ONLY in REQUIRED_SUMMARY_COLUMNS (lines 49-54), which is used solely by _missing_summary_columns (line 108) to validate column EXISTENCE — their VALUES are never rendered to markdown. The runner does write these values (run_historical_walkforward.py:317-327), so the data exists but is dropped from the report.  Item 3: grep confirms no "data source"/"archive policy" string anywhere in the script. Per-Date Provenance does emit input_archive_path per date (partial), but no data-source/archive-policy section.  Item 8: grep confirms no "incident"/"anomal"/"rerun" string. _load_runs_from_db (line 117) queries only the runs table, never the incidents table that exists in shadow_storage.py:72. No incidents/anomalies/reruns section is produced.  The cited code_evidence (build_walkforward_report.py:533-642 and :21-27) is accurate. WF-028 is a SHOULD requirement (spec_review.md:502), and the omitted §10 content is sourceable from existing artifacts (summary CSV columns, incidents table, checksums.json sidecars at shadow_storage.py:155). Finding holds.

#### F-022 — §9.1 performance-gate evaluator (evaluate_v2_gate) is unwired — no shipping/promotion path consumes it
- **Spec:** §9.1 — "V2 components that don't beat V1 on at least one metric must not ship. Log the failure, document why, move on."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/comparison.py:75-114 evaluate_v2_gate returns a GateResult but a repo-wide grep for evaluate_v2_gate/GateResult/StrategyMetrics outside comparison.py and its test finds zero references; the module docstring (comparison.py:14-15) claims consumption by the walk-forward runner but no runner imports it
- **Why it violates the spec:** §9.1 is a gating requirement ('must not ship'). The code provides a pure comparator with unit tests, but nothing in the engine, runner, or promotion path actually calls evaluate_v2_gate to block a non-beating V2 component, nor does anything 'log the failure'. The 'must not ship' enforcement is documentation-only; the function is scaffolding. (The §9.3 shadow-qualification path is a separate mechanism and does not invoke the §9.1 metric gate.)
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Wire evaluate_v2_gate into the walk-forward/promotion runner so a failing GateResult blocks promotion and logs the failure with the v1/v2 metrics, or explicitly document in the module that this is an offline analysis helper not an enforcement gate.
- **Test to add/update:** Add an integration test that runs the walk-forward runner with a V2 candidate that loses on all four metrics and asserts the run records a non-promotion + logs the failure (proving the gate is actually consulted).
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against actual code and spec. evaluate_v2_gate (src/regime_detection/comparison.py:75-114) returns a GateResult but has zero call sites outside comparison.py and tests/test_v2_comparison.py — confirmed by grep for evaluate_v2_gate/GateResult/StrategyMetrics across all .py files. The module docstring (comparison.py:14-15) claims evaluate_v2_gate is 'consumed by the walk-forward runner', but the actual runner scripts/run_v2_walkforward_gate.py imports only V2_GATE_METRIC_NAMES (line 34) — a names tuple used solely to print the metric list into a markdown report (line 352) — and never imports/calls evaluate_v2_gate, StrategyMetrics, or GateResult. The runner's own docstring (lines 10-14) and output artifact docs/verification/v2_walkforward_perf_gate.md:55-59 explicitly state the strategy-PnL metrics (drawdown/sharpe/false-switch that the gate evaluates) are computed downstream/'operator concerns when v2 outputs route into a backtester' — i.e. nothing populates StrategyMetrics, so the gate can never fire, nothing blocks a non-beating V2 component, and nothing 'logs the failure'. Spec §9.1 (docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md:4625-4633) is a gating requirement: 'V2 components that don't beat V1 on at least one metric must not ship. Log the failure, document why, move on.' The §9.3 shadow path (spec:4641-4645, served by compute_v1_v2_diff) is a separate mechanism that does not invoke the §9.1 metric gate, as the finding correctly notes. The 'must not ship' enforcement is documentation-only; evaluate_v2_gate is scaffolding. Finding holds.

#### F-023 — §12.4/§13.18 V2-scaffolding block check is scoped to 7 V1-contract files and does not cover all V1-owned modules
- **Spec:** §12.4 / §13.18 — "V1 must include a CI or pre-commit check that fails on V2 scaffolding/imports, including HMM libraries, macro fetchers, correlation/eigenvalue modules beyond schema needs, ORCA/SRR, Hurst, efficiency ratio, weighted transition score, and `crash_condition`."
- **Code evidence:** tests/test_source_hygiene.py:15-66 (V1_CONTRACT_GUARD_PATHS is 7 files; FORBIDDEN patterns block GaussianHMM/hmm/GMM/ORCA/SRR/hurst/efficiency_ratio/eigenvalue/weighted_transition_score/crash_condition only within those paths); pyproject.toml:20 (hmmlearn==0.3.3 is a runtime dependency); .pre-commit-config.yaml:1-32 (no V2-scaffold grep hook)
- **Why it violates the spec:** In the unified V1+V2 branch a literal repo-wide block is impossible, so the guard is narrowed to the 7 V1-contract modules. This is the correct adaptation under §14.3 and IS enforced every commit via pytest. The remaining gap vs the literal spec: it does not cover all V1 modules, only the 7 enumerated contract paths, so a stray HMM import in another nominally-V1 module would not be caught.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / medium / medium
- **Minimal fix:** Document (in spec or test) the V1-contract-path scoping rationale tied to §14.3, and expand V1_CONTRACT_GUARD_PATHS to cover every V1-owned module (or invert to an allowlist of V2-owned modules) so a V2 import sneaking into any non-allowlisted V1 file is caught.
- **Test to add/update:** Add a test that enumerates all src/regime_detection V1-owned modules (those not in the V2 module set named in §14.3) and asserts none import hmmlearn/sklearn.mixture/macro fetchers, so the guard does not silently miss a newly added V1 file.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: All cited evidence is accurate. tests/test_source_hygiene.py:15-23 defines V1_CONTRACT_GUARD_PATHS as exactly 7 files (trend_direction, trend_character, volatility_state, breadth_state, event_calendar, strategy_response, legacy_v1_wire). The forbidden-token scan (FORBIDDEN_V1_CONTRACT_SCAFFOLDING_PATTERNS blocking GaussianHMM/hmm/GMM/ORCA/SRR/hurst/efficiency_ratio/eigenvalue/weighted_transition_score/crash_condition) only runs over those 7 paths (test function lines 54-66). pyproject.toml:20 confirms hmmlearn==0.3.3 is a runtime dependency. .pre-commit-config.yaml:1-32 has no V2-scaffold grep hook (only black/deptry/cubic/codex). The literal spec requirement is §12.4 of docs/regime_engine_v1_final_spec.md line 1447 ('V1 must include a CI or pre-commit check that fails on V2 scaffolding/imports, including HMM libraries...'), quoted verbatim in the finding. The gap is demonstrably real: this is a unified V1+V2 branch where a repo-wide literal block is impossible (hmm_state.py is an explicit 'v2 §6.1' module importing hmmlearn.GaussianHMM; credit_funding.py/inflation_growth.py are 'v2 §2C/§2B' axis modules), so the 7-path scoping is the correct §14.3 adaptation. But timeline.py — a V1 orchestrator NOT in the guard list — carries extensive GaussianHMM/hmm wiring (lines 53-57, 133-137, 209-242, 271-448), and HMM imports also live in unguarded clustering.py and _config_evidence_strategy.py. So a stray V2-scaffold reference in a V1-owned module outside the 7 contract paths would not be caught, exactly as the finding states. The '§13.18' portion of spec_ref does not exist as a spec header (a finding-ID artifact), but this does not undermine the substantive §12.4-grounded finding.

#### F-024 — No direct test for the §2C effective-resolver same-risk-rank 'confirmed' path
- **Spec:** V2L2B-032 / §2C effective resolver lines 3329-3330 — "OAS and proxy classified with the same risk rank → use OAS and mark agreement_status=confirmed"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/axis_builders/credit_funding.py:435-442 (oas_rank == proxy_rank branch → source_used=oas_confirmed, agreement_status=confirmed); tests/test_credit_funding_axis_engine.py:440-496 cover divergent + proxy_fallback but no same-rank confirmed case
- **Why it violates the spec:** The resolver's same-risk-rank branch (return OAS, agreement_status=confirmed) is a distinct load-bearing outcome of the spec's five-way resolver contract. Tests assert the divergent path, the proxy-fallback path, and evidence typing, but none constructs an OAS and proxy that classify to the same risk rank to assert agreement_status=='confirmed' and source_used=='oas_confirmed' with the OAS label chosen. A regression that flipped this branch (e.g. always returning proxy on equality, or mislabeling agreement_status) would pass the existing suite.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** None to production code; the branch is correct on read (credit_funding.py:435-442).
- **Test to add/update:** test_effective_credit_funding_marks_confirmed_when_oas_and_proxy_same_rank: build oas=_credit_output(label='credit_calm') and proxy=_credit_output(label='credit_recovery') (both risk_rank 0), resolve, and assert effective.active_label=='credit_calm', evidence['agreement_status']=='confirmed', evidence['source_used']=='oas_confirmed'.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Spec docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md:3329-3330 specifies the same-risk-rank contract verbatim ("OAS and proxy classified with the same risk rank → use OAS and mark agreement_status=confirmed"). Code credit_funding.py:435-442 implements it as a distinct branch (oas_rank==proxy_rank → chosen=oas, source_used="oas_confirmed", agreement_status="confirmed"). I checked every test invocation of resolve_credit_funding_effective_output (tests/test_credit_funding_axis_engine.py:447, 472, 491, 520, 580): they assert only proxy_higher_risk/divergent and proxy_fallback — none builds OAS+proxy at the same rank to assert the confirmed outcome. The nearest candidate (test_credit_funding_axis_engine.py:879-884) uses a real fixture where both are credit_calm (same rank, hits the confirmed branch) but asserts agreement_status in {"confirmed","divergent"} — it accepts either, and never pins source_used=="oas_confirmed" or that the OAS label was chosen, so a regression flipping the branch to divergent or returning proxy would still pass. The Layer2 test (tests/test_layer2_audit.py:139-169) hand-feeds source_used="oas_confirmed" as input to the summary aggregator and never calls the resolver, so it cannot catch a resolver regression. The test gap is real as described.

#### F-025 — classify_series multi-day byte-identity contract has no test (only a trivial single-day case is covered)
- **Spec:** V1 final spec §2.1 (classify_series V1.1 helper) — "It is a thin wrapper over `classify_window`; each row is byte-identical to the corresponding `classify(as_of_date)` output."
- **Code evidence:** tests/test_classify_series.py:61-85 (test_classify_series_agrees_with_pointwise_classify) calls classify_series with start_date==end_date==date(2024,1,10) (a 1-session window); engine.py:446-466 classify_series passes lookback_days=len(window_sessions) into classify_window, whereas engine.py:377-400 classify always uses lookback_days=1
- **Why it violates the spec:** The load-bearing byte-identity guarantee is between a per-row label in a MULTI-day window (lookback_days=N>1) and the pointwise classify(as_of_date) for that day. The only agreement test uses a single-session window, so both sides run lookback_days=1 and the assertion passes trivially. The path that could actually diverge — classify_series over a multi-day window vs classify for each interior day — is never exercised. A regression in slice sizing, v2 model-fit windowing, or per-day evidence alignment would change interior-day labels without any test catching it.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add a test that calls classify_series over a multi-session window (e.g. [2024-01-03, 2024-01-12]) and, for every emitted as_of_date, asserts each of the five axis columns equals RegimeEngine().classify(as_of_date=that_day, ...) active_label/state — i.e. loop the existing single-day assertion across all interior sessions.
- **Test to add/update:** test_classify_series_agrees_with_pointwise_classify_multi_day: classify_series over a >=5-session NYSE window; for each row, build the pointwise classify(as_of_date) and assert trend_direction/trend_character/volatility_state/breadth_state == active_label and transition_risk == .state, proving byte-identity holds when lookback_days>1.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against the actual code and spec. (1) Spec contract is verbatim: docs/regime_engine_v1_final_spec.md:155 states classify_series "is a thin wrapper over classify_window; each row is byte-identical to the corresponding classify(as_of_date) output" — a genuine load-bearing requirement, not a paraphrase. (2) engine.py:381 — classify() hardcodes lookback_days=1. (3) engine.py:449 — classify_series passes lookback_days=len(window_sessions) into classify_window. (4) The only agreement test, tests/test_classify_series.py:61-85 (test_classify_series_agrees_with_pointwise_classify), uses start_date==end_date==date(2024,1,10), a single-session window, so len(window_sessions)==1 and BOTH paths run lookback_days=1 — the assertion passes trivially and never exercises the N>1 path. (5) The divergence risk is real and material: timeline.py:163-166 sizes the required slice as v2_min_history + lookback_days - 1 + trailing_component_lookback, and market_context.py:177-181 (slice_context_to_recent_sessions) keeps end_date=context.end_date for the whole window. So in a multi-day classify_series window the feature store and trainable v2 models (HMM/GMM, fit over the end-anchored trailing window per timeline.py:651-680) are built once over a window ending at `end`, whereas pointwise classify(d) for an interior day d anchors at d. For trainable evidence layers this can change interior-day labels — exactly the byte-identity guarantee that is untested. (6) No other test covers it: classify_series appears only in tests/test_classify_series.py; the classify_window tests in tests/test_schema_and_timeline.py:367-402 only assert error-raising/output-count, and test_classify_matches_last_output (442-454) checks only the last output and only that an error is raised. The finding holds.

#### F-026 — Replay payload-contract drift (v2_dependency_payload_contracts-only) breaks the window via replay_mismatch but is untested
- **Spec:** SR-029 (§5 L128-131) — "It is part of replay equality: if the model output is byte-stable but dependency payload semantics drift, replay must report a mismatch."
- **Code evidence:** run_shadow_replay_check.py:164-166 injects v2_dependency_payload_contracts into replayed_payload and :176 diffs it; a drift yields matches=False. But :187 breaks_qualification=_diff_touches_classification_fields(diff), and :86-100 only flags keys named state/label/*_state/*_label — so a pure v2_dependency_payload_contracts drift records the incident with breaks_qualification=0. No test exercises a v2_dependency_payload_contracts-only drift.
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec requires payload-semantic drift to 'report a mismatch', which the code does (matches=0, caught by shadow_qualification._replay_mismatch_dates so the window IS broken via replay_mismatch). The spec text is satisfied, but the behavior is subtle and load-bearing (a contracts-only drift breaks the window through the replay_mismatch path, not breaks_qualification) and has zero test coverage; the only mismatch test tampers transition_risk.state.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add explicit coverage (and optionally a comment) that v2_dependency_payload_contracts drift produces matches=False and is caught by the qualification replay_mismatch path even though breaks_qualification stays 0.
- **Test to add/update:** A replay test mutating only the stored v2_dependency_payload_contracts block (no state/label change) asserting matches=False, an incident is recorded, and evaluate_shadow_qualification reports blocking_reason 'replay_mismatch' for that session.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified all cited code and the spec. run_shadow_replay_check.py:164-166 injects v2_dependency_payload_contracts into replayed_payload; :176 builds the diff and :177 sets matches=(diff is None); :187 sets breaks_qualification=_diff_touches_classification_fields(diff); :86-100 only flags keys named state/label/*_state/*_label. shadow_qualification.py:36-50 (_replay_mismatch_dates) selects replay_checks.matches=0, and :102-104 breaks the window via the 'replay_mismatch' reason independent of breaks_qualification. The spec quote at shadow_runner_spec.md §5 L127-131 is accurate verbatim. The only mismatch test (test_shadow_replay_check.py:111-161) tampers transition_risk.state (line 124, a classification field); no test anywhere exercises a v2_dependency_payload_contracts-only drift (only assertions found are a static contracts-equality check at line 93 and a column-presence check in test_historical_walkforward.py:120). So the spec text IS satisfied (matches=0 breaks the window via replay_mismatch), but the load-bearing contracts-only path has zero test coverage — a genuine test_gap, as claimed. One minor imprecision in the finding: dependency_payload_contracts.py returns nested keys including breadth_state/volatility_state/volume_liquidity_state which DO end with '_state', so a drift in those subkeys would set breaks_qualification=1 (contrary to the finding's blanket 'breaks_qualification=0'); a drift in non-matching keys like credit_funding_effective/event_calendar yields breaks_qualification=0. This nuance does not refute the core claim, since the window is broken via replay_mismatch regardless and the test gap is real.

#### F-027 — Walk-forward 'no silent skips of required NYSE sessions' gate has no failure-path test
- **Spec:** historical_walkforward_spec.md §6 — "no silent skips of required NYSE sessions;"
- **Code evidence:** scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:131-135 _missing_sessions computes expected NYSE schedule minus actual rows; :510-511 appends failure reason 'missing_sessions'. tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py:240 only asserts the empty case payload['missing_sessions'] == []. No test removes an interior NYSE session and asserts the failure reason fires.
- **Why it violates the spec:** Detecting silently-skipped sessions is an explicit mandatory pass/fail criterion. The detection logic (nyse_calendar().schedule over [min,max] minus present dates) is non-trivial and never exercised on a gap. A regression in _missing_sessions (e.g. wrong calendar or off-by-one window) would silently let a walk-forward with missing sessions pass.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add a test that builds 252 sessions, drops one interior NYSE session from both the summary CSV and the runs table, and asserts status=='fail' with 'missing_sessions' in failure_reasons and the dropped date in payload['missing_sessions'].
- **Test to add/update:** test_build_walkforward_report_detects_skipped_nyse_session: omit sessions[100] from rows; assert 'missing_sessions' in failure_reasons and sessions[100].isoformat() in result['missing_sessions'].
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Confirmed. Code: scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:131-135 (_missing_sessions = expected NYSE schedule from _expected_sessions:124-128 minus actual as_of dates) and :510-511 (appends 'missing_sessions' failure reason), wired into _failure_reasons at :655/:669-679 driving status='fail' at :682 — all as cited. Spec: docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:113 lists 'no silent skips of required NYSE sessions' as an explicit §6 mandatory pass/fail criterion (reinforced at :120). Test gap: in tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py the ONLY reference to missing_sessions is line 240 (payload['missing_sessions'] == [], the empty case in the no-gates test). No test removes an interior NYSE session and asserts the 'missing_sessions' reason fires. All fixtures (_session_rows:22-63 and the default contiguous 3-row block) use contiguous NYSE sessions, so _missing_sessions always returns []. Asymmetry confirms it: every other §6/§7 gate has a dedicated failure-path rejects_* test (replay_mismatch:315, short_oos:355, mixed_frozen:392, unknown_baseline:414, red_flags:451, golden:509/543/565, nan_leakage:586/606, unknown_stretch:634, flip_flops:659) — missing_sessions is the lone exception. A regression in the non-trivial detection logic (wrong calendar / off-by-one window / wrong set difference) would let a walk-forward with skipped sessions silently pass, uncaught. Finding evidence is accurate; severity medium / confidence high are appropriate (isolated test gap on a mandatory gate, not a live code bug).

#### F-028 — Walk-forward 'no engine crashes' gate (status='failure' rows) has no failure-path test
- **Spec:** historical_walkforward_spec.md §6 — "no engine crashes across the entire qualifying window;"
- **Code evidence:** scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:508-509 `if summary_df["status"].eq("failure").any(): reasons.append("run_failures_present")`. No test constructs a summary row with status=='failure' and asserts 'run_failures_present' (grep returns no test hits)
- **Why it violates the spec:** A failed/crashed classification session inside the qualifying window must fail the gate.
