- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified at scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:508-509 (`if summary_df["status"].eq("failure").any(): reasons.append("run_failures_present")`), which is wired into build_walkforward_report (line 669) and drives status="fail" (line 682). Spec docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:112 lists "no engine crashes across the entire qualifying window;" as a §6 pass/fail criterion. In tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py, every constructed row hardcodes status="success" (_session_rows lines 45-46, _prepare_walkforward_root lines 78,93,108) — no test sets status="failure" for the report builder. Grep for run_failures_present across tests/ returns zero hits. Two tests in tests/test_historical_walkforward.py (lines 158, 207) do produce failure rows but exercise only the runner (run_walkforward): line 203 asserts the DB runs row equals "failure" and line 233-239 asserts summary columns persist; neither calls build_walkforward_report (grep returns no matches in that file) nor asserts run_failures_present in failure_reasons. The report-builder gate's failure branch is never executed by any test.

#### F-029 — Shadow qualification counter: present-but-failed run (status != 'success') reset path is untested
- **Spec:** shadow_runner_spec.md §1 — "The runner executes for 252 consecutive NYSE trading sessions. ... Each session emits exactly one immutable output for the tuple (as_of_date, engine_version, config_version)."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/shadow_qualification.py:110-112 `if status != "success": blocking_reasons.append("non_success_run"); break`. tests/test_shadow_qualification.py tests 252-pass, missing_session_gap, breaking_incident, off-session incident, and replay_mismatch resets, but never inserts a run with status='failure'/'in_progress' inside the window to assert the 'non_success_run' reset
- **Why it violates the spec:** A session that ran but did not succeed must reset the consecutive-clean counter just like a missing session. Only the missing-session reset is tested. A regression that treats non-success statuses as clean (e.g. counting any present row) would inflate the qualification counter toward 252 on a window containing failed sessions — the exact silent-skip failure the spec forbids.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add a shadow-qualification test that inserts 252 sessions where one interior session has status='failure' and asserts qualifies is False, current_consecutive_sessions equals the count after that session, and 'non_success_run' in blocking_reasons.
- **Test to add/update:** test_shadow_qualification_resets_after_non_success_run: insert 252 success runs, then UPDATE runs SET status='failure' for sessions[120]; assert current_consecutive_sessions==131 and 'non_success_run' in blocking_reasons.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against source and spec. shadow_qualification.py:110-112 contains exactly the cited branch: `if status != "success": blocking_reasons.append("non_success_run"); break`. In tests/test_shadow_qualification.py the only run-insert helper (_insert_success_runs, lines 24-49) hardcodes status="success"; the 5 tests cover 252-pass, missing_session_gap, breaking_incident, off-session incident, and replay_mismatch — none inserts a status='failure'/'in_progress' run inside the window to exercise the non_success_run reset. Grepping the whole tests/ tree confirms only test_shadow_runner.py (lines 290-298) and test_shadow_storage.py (line 170) insert non-success run rows, and neither imports/calls evaluate_shadow_qualification, so the branch is untested anywhere. Spec basis is accurate: shadow_runner_spec.md §1 line 27 requires 252 consecutive sessions, §0 line 12 explicitly lists 'silent failures' as a target, and §5 lines 119-123 define in_progress/failure as real run statuses — so a present-but-failed session must reset the counter. The finding holds.

#### F-030 — Walk-forward required-summary-columns gate (§5 artifact contract) has no failure-path test
- **Spec:** historical_walkforward_spec.md §5 — "one machine-readable summary table ... The machine-readable summary must also include v2_dependency_payload_contracts. This records the cross-axis payload shape used by the run ... so operator review can catch semantic drift between walk-forward runs."
- **Code evidence:** scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:44-56 REQUIRED_SUMMARY_COLUMNS; :107-108 _missing_summary_columns; :514-515 appends 'missing_report_columns'. tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py always writes the full column set; no test omits a required column and asserts 'missing_report_columns' fires
- **Why it violates the spec:** The §5 contract requires the summary to carry the transition-risk provenance columns so operators can detect semantic drift; the report builder enforces this via missing_report_columns, but that enforcement branch is never tested. A regression dropping a required column, or a real run that omits one, would not be caught. (REQUIRED_SUMMARY_COLUMNS does not itself include v2_dependency_payload_contracts, only the transition_risk_* columns — a separate scope question.)
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add a test that writes a summary CSV missing one REQUIRED_SUMMARY_COLUMNS entry and asserts status=='fail' with 'missing_report_columns' in failure_reasons and the missing column listed in payload['missing_summary_columns'].
- **Test to add/update:** test_build_walkforward_report_rejects_missing_required_columns: drop transition_risk_primary_drivers from the summary; assert 'missing_report_columns' in failure_reasons.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified the finding holds. CODE: scripts/build_walkforward_report.py defines the gate exactly as cited — REQUIRED_SUMMARY_COLUMNS (lines 44-56, including the transition_risk_* columns), _missing_summary_columns (lines 107-108), and _failure_reasons appends "missing_report_columns" when missing_summary_columns is non-empty (lines 514-515). It is wired in at line 657 and surfaced in the analysis payload at line 689. SPEC: docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md §5 (lines 94-106) requires the machine-readable summary to preserve provenance and include drift-detection payload contracts so operators can catch semantic drift — the gate is a legitimate spec-grounded enforcement. TEST GAP CONFIRMED: grep across the entire repo shows "missing_report_columns", "missing_summary_columns", and "REQUIRED_SUMMARY_COLUMNS" appear ONLY in scripts/build_walkforward_report.py and in ZERO test files. In tests/test_build_walkforward_report.py, the row builders (_session_rows and the default rows in _prepare_walkforward_root) always write the full required column set, and every failure-path test asserts a DIFFERENT reason (missing_golden_results, replay_mismatch_detected, insufficient_oos_sessions, mixed_frozen_versions, nan_leakage_detected, red_flags_detected, golden_results_* variants). No test omits a required column and asserts missing_report_columns fires. A regression dropping a required column would not be caught by the suite. The finding's own caveat (that REQUIRED_SUMMARY_COLUMNS does not literally include v2_dependency_payload_contracts) is accurate and does not weaken the core test-gap claim. All cited evidence line numbers are correct.

#### F-031 — §9.4 'sequence' golden-date assertion is registered but never verified by any test
- **Spec:** §9.4 — "\| 2018-10-10 \| tests bull→narrowing_breadth→bear_stress sequence \|"
- **Code evidence:** tests/test_fixture_verification.py:247-248 (`if field_name == "sequence": continue`); fixture row tests/fixtures/derived/golden_dates_v2.yaml:28-31 (`sequence: bull_to_narrowing_breadth_to_bear_stress`)
- **Why it violates the spec:** The 2018-10-10 §9.4 date's whole reason for existing is to exercise the bull→narrowing_breadth→bear_stress sequence, but the only test that iterates the V2 golden fixture (test_v2_golden_dates_classify_expected_fields) explicitly `continue`s past the `sequence` field, asserting nothing. The classify call for 2018-10-10 happens, but no part of the asserted sequence (bull, narrowing_breadth, bear_stress across the window) is checked. The §9.4 behavior this date is meant to protect has zero test coverage.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Replace the `continue` with a real assertion: classify the trailing window ending 2018-10-10 and assert the trend/breadth/transition labels pass through bull → narrowing_breadth → bear_stress in order (or at minimum that the terminal session's breadth_state and transition_risk match the tail of the sequence).
- **Test to add/update:** In test_v2_golden_dates_classify_expected_fields, for the q4_2018_breadth_stress row, classify the window and assert the ordered label progression bull→narrowing_breadth→bear_stress is observed across the sessions leading into 2018-10-10.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Confirmed by reading the actual code and spec. Spec docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md:4656 states the 2018-10-10 §9.4 row exists to "test bull→narrowing_breadth→bear_stress sequence". Fixture tests/fixtures/derived/golden_dates_v2.yaml:28-31 registers it with the sole expected field `sequence: bull_to_narrowing_breadth_to_bear_stress`. The only test iterating expected_v2_fields, test_v2_golden_dates_classify_expected_fields (tests/test_fixture_verification.py:246), hits `if field_name == "sequence": continue` (lines 247-248) and asserts nothing — and since `sequence` is the ONLY key for this date, every other assertion branch is unreachable for 2018-10-10. The string bull_to_narrowing_breadth_to_bear_stress appears only in the YAML, never in any .py test (grep confirmed). test_v2_section_9_4_golden_dates_are_registered only checks registration (non-empty fields), not behavior. The narrowing_breadth/bear_stress tests in test_transition_and_strategy.py:538 and test_breadth_state_v2_labels.py use synthetic single-axis inputs to unit-test rule mappings; none classifies 2018-10-10 or asserts the multi-day sequence. The §9.4 sequence behavior this date protects has zero behavioral coverage.

#### F-032 — No test asserts the V1 trend_direction risk-rank dict against spec §3.6
- **Spec:** V1L1AB-006 / §3.6 — "trend_direction_risk_rank:   bull: 0   sideways: 1   transition: 2   bear: 3   unknown: 2"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/trend_direction.py:35-43 (_RISK_RANK literal); no test in tests/ references trend_direction._RISK_RANK
- **Why it violates the spec:** The code's _RISK_RANK matches §3.6 exactly, but unlike volatility_state, network_fragility, volume_liquidity and inflation_growth — all of which have explicit risk-rank contract tests — the trend_direction risk-rank has NO test pinning it to the spec values. The dict carries an added 'euphoria': 4 V2 key; a silent edit to any of the five V1 values (e.g. bear→2) would change hysteresis decay ordering and ship without a failing test.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add a unit test in tests/test_trend_direction.py asserting {k: _RISK_RANK[k] for k in ('bull','sideways','transition','bear','unknown')} == {'bull':0,'sideways':1,'transition':2,'bear':3,'unknown':2}, mirroring tests/test_volatility_state.py:32.
- **Test to add/update:** test_v1_trend_direction_risk_rank_matches_spec_3_6: import _RISK_RANK from regime_detection.trend_direction and assert the five V1 labels map to the spec §3.6 YAML values exactly.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified all claims against actual code and spec. (1) `_RISK_RANK` literal at src/regime_detection/trend_direction.py:35-43 matches §3.6 V1 values exactly (bull:0, sideways:1, transition:2, bear:3, unknown:2) plus added euphoria:4 and recovery:1 V2 keys. (2) Spec quote is verbatim at docs/regime_engine_v1_final_spec.md:447-452. (3) tests/test_trend_direction.py contains NO assertion on _RISK_RANK, and no test in tests/ asserts the trend_direction risk-rank values (grep for TREND_DIRECTION_RISK_RANK assertions returned no matches; test_per_label_hysteresis.py imports it but only tests the hysteresis mechanism using NETWORK_FRAGILITY constants). (4) Sibling components DO have explicit contract tests: network_fragility test_network_fragility_risk_rank_matches_v2_spec_3_6 asserts the full dict verbatim (test_network_fragility_classifier.py:319-333); volatility_state pins crisis_vol (test_volatility_state.py:32-33); volume_liquidity/inflation_growth reference their RISK_RANK constants. (5) Harm is real: _RISK_RANK flows into hysteresis via axis_builders/trend_direction.py:48 (risk_rank=TREND_DIRECTION_RISK_RANK passed to _build_axis_outputs), so a silent edit to a V1 value would change hysteresis decay ordering and ship with no failing unit test. Genuine, unprotected test gap; no current live bug.

#### F-033 — ADX_14 Wilder ewm pin is only verified by a spec-text string match, not by computing _compute_adx_14
- **Spec:** V1L1AB-011 — "# Implementation pin: ADX_14 uses pandas ewm(alpha=1/14, adjust=False, min_periods=14) # for ATR, +DM, -DM, and DX smoothing."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/trend_character.py:82-106 (_wilder_ewm + _compute_adx_14 apply ewm(alpha=1/14, adjust=False, min_periods=14) to tr, plus_dm, minus_dm, dx); tests/test_trend_character.py:235-240 test_v1_spec_pins_adx_ewm_seeding_convention only asserts the spec FILE contains the pin string; tests/test_reconciliation_contracts.py:137 only asserts adx_14.iloc[13] is NaN
- **Why it violates the spec:** The implementation pin is a load-bearing numeric contract (it fixes ATR/+DM/-DM/DX smoothing to pandas recursive ewm rather than classic Wilder running-sum seeding — the two differ in the warm-up region). The only test of the pin asserts the spec markdown contains the text; it does NOT run _compute_adx_14, so a code change from ewm(adjust=False) to a true-Wilder running-sum (or adjust=True) would not fail it. The actual numeric ADX values are only checked via frozen golden fixtures captured from engine output, which self-bless the current implementation rather than verifying against an independent Wilder reference.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add a unit test that builds a small known high/low/close series, computes _compute_adx_14, and compares against ADX recomputed inline with ewm(alpha=1/14, adjust=False, min_periods=14) on TR/+DM/-DM/DX (and asserts the first 13 values are NaN), so the pin is verified at the code level not just the spec text.
- **Test to add/update:** test_compute_adx_14_uses_wilder_ewm_pin: assert _compute_adx_14 output equals an inline reference that applies ewm(alpha=1/14, adjust=False, min_periods=14) to TR, +DM, -DM and DX, and that index 0..12 are NaN.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified all citations. (1) Spec docs/regime_engine_v1_final_spec.md:491-493 contains the load-bearing pin ("ADX_14 standard Wilder formula" + "Implementation pin: ADX_14 uses pandas ewm(alpha=1/14, adjust=False, min_periods=14) for ATR, +DM, -DM, and DX smoothing"). (2) Code trend_character.py:82-106: _wilder_ewm applies ewm(alpha=1/n, adjust=False, min_periods=n) to tr, plus_dm, minus_dm, and dx exactly as the finding states; adjust=False recursive seeding genuinely differs from classic Wilder running-sum seeding in the warm-up region. (3) tests/test_trend_character.py:235-240 test_v1_spec_pins_adx_ewm_seeding_convention only reads the spec markdown and asserts the pin STRING is present — it never imports or calls _compute_adx_14. (4) tests/test_reconciliation_contracts.py:123-137 only asserts features.adx_14.iloc[13] is NaN, a cold-start property that holds for BOTH ewm(adjust=False) and running-sum Wilder, so it cannot discriminate the conventions. (5) The only test that actually runs compute_features (-> _compute_adx_14), tests/test_trend_character.py:103-124, asserts sma_50/return_63d against inline reference formulas but never asserts adx_14. (6) The sole numeric ADX checks are frozen golden fixtures (tests/fixtures/v1_frozen_outputs/*.json, e.g. adx_14: 30.89310564) replayed by tests/test_v1_frozen_replay.py:68 against the SAME engine that produced them — self-blessing, not an independent Wilder reference. A switch to adjust=True or running-sum seeding would not fail the pin test or the NaN test. The test_gap is real.

#### F-034 — No test exercises §10.3 precedence when sideways_chop co-fires with a transition_risk scenario (position-size loosening)
- **Spec:** §10.3 Scenario Precedence — "Apply modifiers in increasing priority order, layered on `default_neutral`. Highest-priority match wins on conflicting fields."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/strategy_response.py:144-156 (sideways_chop sets position_size_multiplier=0.75 by assignment at line 147; bull_fragile at 151-156 runs after and re-lowers to 0.5)
- **Why it violates the spec:** sideways_chop fires on trend_character/volatility axes while recovery_attempt/bull_fragile/bear_stress/crisis fire on transition_risk_state, so they can co-fire on the same session. sideways_chop's position_size_multiplier is set by unconditional assignment (=0.75), not min(), so when sideways_chop co-fires with recovery_attempt (which sets 0.5) the result is loosened to 0.75. Per §10.3 sideways_chop > recovery_attempt so 0.75 winning is spec-correct — but this conflict-resolution path has no test. A future reorder of the if-blocks would silently flip the winner with no failing test.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / medium / high
- **Minimal fix:** No code change; add coverage. Optionally make the precedence explicit by ordering blocks strictly by §10.3 rank with comments referencing the precedence list.
- **Test to add/update:** test_strategy_response_sideways_chop_outranks_recovery_attempt: call build_strategy_response with trend_character='chop', volatility_state='normal_vol' AND transition_risk_state='recovery_attempt', and assert position_size_multiplier==0.75 and modifiers_applied==['recovery_attempt','sideways_chop']. Also add a bull_fragile+chop case asserting psm==0.5.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Confirmed by reading the code and spec. strategy_response.py:135-142 (recovery_attempt) sets position_size_multiplier=0.5 by unconditional assignment, and lines 144-149 (sideways_chop, fires when trend_character=="chop" and volatility!="crisis_vol") later overwrites it to 0.75 by unconditional assignment at line 147. Because sideways_chop's if-block runs AFTER recovery_attempt's, when both co-fire the result is 0.75. Spec §10.3 (regime_engine_v1_final_spec.md:1048-1054) defines precedence "crisis > bear_stress > bull_fragile > sideways_chop > recovery_attempt > ... Highest-priority match wins on conflicting fields", so 0.75 winning is spec-correct — but it is enforced solely by source-line ORDER, not by min()/explicit priority. The co-firing is reachable: transition_risk_series.py:504-508 shows recovery_attempt fires on prior_bear/close/breadth conditions independent of trend_character, so trend_character=="chop" can coexist with transition_risk_state=="recovery_attempt". Test verification: grep across tests shows NO call to build_strategy_response passes trend_character_active="chop"; the only sideways_chop-named test (test_transition_and_strategy.py:185) uses "volatile_chop" which deliberately does NOT trigger the modifier (asserts modifiers_applied == []); no test asserts "sideways_chop" in modifiers_applied; and no test exercises the sideways_chop+recovery_attempt precedence conflict. The cited evidence and reasoning are accurate; the test gap is real, and a future reorder of the if-blocks would silently flip the winner with no failing test.

### LOW (21)

#### F-035 — Emitted engine_version is regime-engine-v2.0.0, contradicting the §2.4/§11 V1 literal regime-engine-v1.0.0; frozen-replay test strips engine_version from byte-identity
- **Spec:** §2.4 Output Versioning / §11 / §11.1 — "Every top-level output includes: { "engine_version": "regime-engine-v1.0.0", "config_version": "core3-v1.0.0", ... }. ... V1 byte-identity is mechanically enforced by `tests/test_v1_frozen_replay.py`."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/__init__.py:5 (__version__ = "2.0.0"); src/regime_detection/versioning.py:8-9 (engine_version() returns "regime-engine-v2.0.0"); tests/fixtures/v1_frozen_outputs/2024-04-15.json:2 ("engine_version": "regime-engine-v2.0.0"); tests/test_v1_frozen_replay.py:56-65,90-97 compare with the engine_version key removed
- **Why it violates the spec:** The §11/§2.4 canonical V1 wire pins engine_version to regime-engine-v1.0.0 for config_version core3-v1.0.0. Live emission is regime-engine-v2.0.0 because the unified package version is 2.0.0, and the frozen-replay 'byte-identity' test deliberately strips engine_version from both sides before comparing, so byte-identity is NOT enforced on that field. §14.1/§14.3 authorize the unified state and the test docstring records the v2.0.0 bump, so this is a sanctioned divergence — but the §11 literal value and the emitted value differ, and the strongest replay guarantee explicitly excludes this field.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** conflict / low / high
- **Minimal fix:** No code change needed if §14's v2.0.0 authorization governs; otherwise add an explicit note to §2.4/§11 that under the unified branch engine_version is regime-engine-v<package-version> and byte-identity is enforced modulo engine_version. Keep test_version_coupling_pyproject_matches_engine_version as the binding check.
- **Test to add/update:** Add a test asserting the V1 frozen fixtures' engine_version equals f"regime-engine-v{package_version}" so the excluded field is still pinned to the package version rather than silently free-floating (and, if strict V1 conformance is wanted, that the legacy-V1-wire projection emits regime-engine-v1.0.0 under config core3-v1.0.0).

#### F-036 — Default config path resolves to core3-v2.0.0.yaml, not the V1 spec's mandated configs/core3-v1.0.0.yaml
- **Spec:** §2.4.1 Config Loading — "V1 ships with configs/core3-v1.0.0.yaml. ... Default config path is configs/core3-v1.0.0.yaml."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/config.py:182-216 (_default_config_resource_name_for_version dispatches on __version__ major: major==2 -> configs/core3-v2.0.0.yaml); src/regime_detection/__init__.py:5 (__version__="2.0.0") so load_default_regime_config() returns the V2 config
- **Why it violates the spec:** RegimeEngine() with no config_path now loads core3-v2.0.0.yaml (config_version core3-v2.0.0), whereas the V1 spec fixes the default to core3-v1.0.0.yaml. A caller invoking RegimeEngine().classify(...) without an explicit V1 config gets V2 behavior and a V2 config_version. This is the intended V2 default but diverges from the literal V1 §2.4.1 default-path requirement.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** conflict / low / high
- **Minimal fix:** No code change recommended (intended V2 default). To honor strict V1 §2.4.1, either keep __version__ at 1.x for V1 distributions, or update the V1 spec to record that the default config follows the package major version.
- **Test to add/update:** A regression test pinning load_default_regime_config().config_version to the expected default for the shipped __version__ major, so future major bumps are caught.

#### F-037 — window_days row override in the load_event_calendar path is not validated for start<=end ordering; a reversed window silently never fires
- **Spec:** V1L23-019 / §7.2 Per-event window_days Override — "The value must be a 2-element `[start_offset, end_offset]` pair in NYSE trading days; absence falls back to the type's default window from §7.2 above."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/loaders.py:669-707 (_parse_window_days only checks 2-item integers, no ordering); src/regime_detection/event_calendar.py:193-197 (start_idx=event_idx+start_offset, end_idx=event_idx+end_offset; if start_offset>end_offset then the slice is empty). Contrast tests/test_event_label_resolution.py:84-93 which proves the SEPARATE load_scheduled_events path DOES reject reversed window_days.
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec phrases the override as an ordered [start_offset, end_offset] pair. The load_event_calendar/_validate_event_df path accepts a reversed pair like [3,-3] without error; compute_event_calendar_outputs then paints an empty trading-day slice, so the event window silently never fires for that row — a label is dropped with no warning. The asymmetry with the validated load_scheduled_events path shows the ordering check was intended but is missing on this path.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** edge_case / low / high
- **Minimal fix:** In loaders.py _parse_window_days (or _validate_event_df), after parsing both ints raise ValueError when parsed[0] > parsed[1], mirroring the 'window_days lower bound' check already used in the load_scheduled_events path.
- **Test to add/update:** Add a test in tests/test_event_calendar.py passing an event row with window_days=[3,-3] through load_event_calendar and asserting it raises ValueError (rather than silently producing normal_calendar).

#### F-038 — V2 request-input contract validation runs after build_market_context, so a missing configured V2 input may surface a context-builder error before the dedicated ClassifyRequest contract error
- **Spec:** V1 final spec §2.1 (boundary validation belongs on the request path) — "`classify` and `classify_window` are wrappers over `classify_request`; all boundary validation belongs on the request path."
- **Code evidence:** engine.py:474-503 classify_request calls build_market_context (line 483-499) BEFORE _validate_v2_request_input_contracts (line 500); the latter raises `ClassifyRequest missing configured V2 inputs: ...` (engine.py:282-287)
- **Why it violates the spec:** For a V2 config that declares a required seam, build_market_context runs first. If it raises on the same missing input it produces a different, less request-scoped error than the V2RequestInputContract diagnostic; if it tolerates the absence the dedicated check still fires afterward. The spec says all boundary validation belongs on the request path; the request-path V2 contract validation is present but ordered after context construction, so its specific diagnostic may be pre-empted. The spec does not mandate exact ordering, so this is a diagnostic-clarity concern.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** edge_case / low / low
- **Minimal fix:** Move _validate_v2_request_input_contracts(request, cfg) ahead of build_market_context in classify_request so the request-boundary contract error is raised first and deterministically.
- **Test to add/update:** test_classify_request_reports_missing_v2_input_before_context_build: with a V2 config that configures monetary_pressure_state but omits macro_series, assert the raised ValueError message is the 'ClassifyRequest missing configured V2 inputs' contract error.

#### F-039 — HMM state-mean drift alert (>20%) and transition-prob review flag (>30%) are computed but never surfaced/emitted to any operator-visible surface
- **Spec:** V2L56-019 / §6.1 Training — "Compare new model parameters to prior version; alert when state-mean parameter drift exceeds 20%. ... a separate review-flag fires when transition-probability shifts exceed 30% but does not block deployment."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/hmm_state.py:361 stores parameter_drift on HMMFeatures; src/regime_detection/timeline.py:211-241 reads hmm_features.state_probabilities/.top_state_prob/.n_states but never reads .parameter_drift; grep for parameter_drift in src/ shows zero consumers outside hmm_state.py
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec requires the engine to 'alert' when state-mean drift exceeds 20% and to fire a review-flag when transition-prob shift exceeds 30%. compute_hmm_parameter_drift correctly computes parameter_drift, state_mean_drift_alert, max_transition_prob_shift, and transition_prob_review_flag, and attaches the result to HMMFeatures.parameter_drift. But that field is never read by any output builder, logger, manifest, or wire model — the alert/flag booleans are silently discarded. No 'alert' is ever emitted to an operator-visible surface.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / high
- **Minimal fix:** Emit the drift alert when set: in compute_hmm_features (or the timeline HMM output builder) log a WARNING when latest_drift.state_mean_drift_alert or transition_prob_review_flag is True, and/or surface the drift booleans on HmmOutput / a manifest artifact so the operator-side quarterly review actually receives the alert.
- **Test to add/update:** A test that runs compute_hmm_features over a window engineered to drift >20% across two refit checkpoints and asserts an operator-visible alert is produced (e.g. caplog WARNING containing 'state-mean drift' or a non-None drift field on the emitted HmmOutput), not merely that HMMFeatures.parameter_drift.state_mean_drift_alert is True.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified: the drift alert/flag booleans are computed correctly (src/regime_detection/hmm_state.py:467-478 in compute_hmm_parameter_drift) and attached to HMMFeatures.parameter_drift (hmm_state.py:355-362), but no operator-visible surface ever reads them. A grep across all of src/regime_detection for .parameter_drift / state_mean_drift_alert / transition_prob_review_flag / max_transition_prob_shift / HMMParameterDrift returns ONLY hmm_state.py (plus tests). timeline.py:209-241 reads hmm_features.state_probabilities/.top_state_prob/.n_states but never .parameter_drift. feature_store.py:732 stores the full HMMFeatures on feature_store.hmm, but no manifest serializer, output builder, logger, or wire model reads the .parameter_drift attribute, so the boolean is dropped when the object is discarded. The spec (docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md:4434 'alert when state-mean parameter drift exceeds 20%' and :4468 'a separate review-flag fires when transition-probability shifts exceed 30%') uses the verbs 'alert' and 'review-flag fires', which require the signal to reach an operator — storing a boolean on an in-memory dataclass field that nothing reads does not satisfy that. I attempted to refute via ADR 0020 (docs/decisions/0020-v2-prerequisite-and-shadow-scope.md:36-56 / F-025), but the ADR corroborates rather than refutes: it claims the result is 'surfaced on HMMFeatures.parameter_drift', yet that attribute is never serialized/logged/emitted, so no alert actually reaches an operator. Finding holds. Severity corrected to low because the spec itself marks this as non-blocking, advisory calibration-review tooling (ADR F-025: fail-open observability that 'never blocks the fit and never feeds the runtime transition score'); no classification output or capital-protection path depends on it, so the operational impact of the un-surfaced alert is low rather than medium.

#### F-040 — NetworkFragilityOutput does not pin the closed §3.3 label set as a Literal, unlike all four sibling V2 axes
- **Spec:** V2 §3.3 Labels — "### 3.3 Labels ```text diversified_normal decorrelated_calm rotation_watch stock_picker_dispersion idiosyncratic_crisis rising_fragility correlation_concentration correlation_to_one systemic_stress_unconfirmed systemic_stress unknown ```"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/axis_output_models.py:69-79 (NetworkFragilityOutput inherits raw_label/stable_label/active_label as bare `str` from AxisOutput:26-28). Contrast InflationGrowthOutput (114-118), CreditFundingOutput (144-148), MonetaryPressureV2Output (171-175), VolumeLiquidityStateOutput (240-244), which each override the triple to their closed Literal. The closed 11-label NetworkFragilityLabel exists (network_fragility_rules.py:56-68) but is never applied to the wire model.
- **Why it violates the spec:** §3.3 defines network fragility as a closed 11-label set, and the V2 axis contract pins the raw/stable/active triple as Pydantic. Every other V2 label axis enforces its closed set at the output boundary via a Literal override, so an out-of-set label is rejected by type validation. NetworkFragilityOutput leaves the triple as open str, so the §3.3 closed set is not enforced at the output model — a producer bug emitting e.g. 'systemic_crisis' or a stale/renamed label would serialize silently rather than failing validation. The set is enforced upstream in the rule engine, so this is a missing defense-in-depth/contract pin at the model layer.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / high
- **Minimal fix:** In axis_output_models.py, import NetworkFragilityLabel from regime_detection.network_fragility_rules and override raw_label/stable_label/active_label on NetworkFragilityOutput to NetworkFragilityLabel (mirroring InflationGrowthOutput), with the same reportIncompatibleVariableOverride pyright ignores the siblings use.
- **Test to add/update:** Add a test that constructs NetworkFragilityOutput(raw_label='systemic_crisis', stable_label='diversified_normal', active_label='diversified_normal', ...) using real models and asserts pydantic.ValidationError, plus a positive case asserting all 11 §3.3 labels (from NetworkFragilityLabel.__args__) are accepted.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: Verified against actual code and spec. NetworkFragilityOutput (axis_output_models.py:69-79) extends AxisOutput and overrides ONLY `mode` (line 78) and `evidence` (line 79); it inherits the bare `str` label triple from AxisOutput:26-28 and never re-types it. The four sibling V2 axes each override the raw/stable/active triple to their closed Literal: InflationGrowthOutput:115-117, CreditFundingOutput:145-147, MonetaryPressureV2Output:172-174, VolumeLiquidityStateOutput:241-243. The closed 11-label NetworkFragilityLabel Literal exists at network_fragility_rules.py:56-68 and matches spec §3.3 (spec lines ~3489+: diversified_normal, decorrelated_calm, rotation_watch, stock_picker_dispersion, idiosyncratic_crisis, rising_fragility, correlation_concentration, correlation_to_one, systemic_stress_unconfirmed, systemic_stress, unknown) but is never applied to the wire model — it is used only for the rule layer and the raw_labels list in axis_builders/network_fragility.py:20,112. The shared build_per_label_axis_outputs helper (per_label.py:18-23,74-80) passes labels as bare str, so no narrowing happens outside the Pydantic model. No test enforces out-of-set rejection at the NetworkFragilityOutput boundary (test_models.py constructs it only with valid labels). The finding's evidence is accurate in every particular; this is a genuine missing contract-pin/defense-in-depth inconsistency relative to its four siblings.

#### F-041 — §3 timestamp/temporal columns declared TEXT instead of the spec §3 TIMESTAMP/DATE affinity, contradicting the shadow_storage 'verbatim implementation' docstring
- **Spec:** SR-010 (§3 L63-64) / Shadow Runner Spec §3 SQLite Schema — "run_timestamp TIMESTAMP NOT NULL, as_of_date DATE NOT NULL, ... incident_date DATE NOT NULL, ... breaks_qualification BOOLEAN NOT NULL"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/shadow_storage.py:45-79 declares run_timestamp TEXT, as_of_date TEXT, check_timestamp TEXT, incident_date TEXT (vs spec TIMESTAMP/DATE); utc_iso_now writes ISO-8601 strings; module docstring shadow_storage.py:1-10 claims 'verbatim implementation' of §§1-7
- **Why it violates the spec:** SQLite has no native TIMESTAMP type — declared TIMESTAMP/DATE get NUMERIC affinity, while the code declares TEXT and stores ISO-8601. This is functionally fine (ISO strings round-trip identically and ORDER BY sorts correctly; the mandatory UNIQUE constraint is preserved). The gap is the docstring's 'verbatim implementation' claim being literally false for column types, which can mislead an auditor diffing schema against the spec. Low-severity cosmetic deviation noted for completeness.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / high
- **Minimal fix:** Either (a) change the column declarations to TIMESTAMP/DATE/BOOLEAN to match spec §3 verbatim (storing the same ISO strings; SQLite ignores the affinity difference), or (b) soften the docstring to note temporal columns use TEXT storage of ISO-8601 values with identical round-trip semantics, so the 'verbatim' claim is accurate.
- **Test to add/update:** Add a test that opens a fresh shadow DB, queries PRAGMA table_info for runs/replay_checks/incidents, and asserts each temporal column either matches the spec §3 type or (if TEXT) round-trips ISO-8601 values, documenting the intentional choice.

#### F-042 — config= override is not enforced to be a RegimeConfig instance at the request boundary
- **Spec:** §2.4.1 Config Loading — "classify(..., config=...) may override the engine default only with a validated RegimeConfig object."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/engine.py:52,65 (ClassifyRequest is a plain frozen @dataclass; config: RegimeConfig \| None has no runtime validation); engine.py:482 (cfg = request.config if request.config is not None else self._config passes config through unchecked); coercion only happens later in MarketContext (market_context.py:23,116-117)
- **Why it violates the spec:** Because ClassifyRequest is a dataclass (not Pydantic), a caller can pass a non-RegimeConfig object (a dict or wrong model) as config and no boundary check rejects it at classify/classify_request. A dict satisfying RegimeConfig's schema would be silently coerced by MarketContext's Pydantic validation; a malformed one fails deep inside build_market_context with a less direct error. The spec wants the override accepted ONLY as an already-validated RegimeConfig object. In practice Pydantic validation provides equivalent data safety, so the risk is a slightly later/less-targeted error.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / medium
- **Minimal fix:** Add an isinstance(request.config, RegimeConfig) guard in classify_request (raising TypeError with a clear message) before build_market_context, so a non-RegimeConfig override fails loudly at the boundary as the spec requires.
- **Test to add/update:** test_classify_rejects_non_regimeconfig_override: classify(..., config={...dict...}) raises TypeError at the request boundary rather than failing inside build_market_context.

#### F-043 — Strategy response emits modifier names outside the §10.4 V1 scenario set (transition_weakening, transition_warning, high_transition_risk, sideways_stress)
- **Spec:** §10.4 Scenario Modifiers (V1 set) / §10.3 precedence list — "crisis > bear_stress > bull_fragile > sideways_chop > recovery_attempt > bull_healthy_low_vol > default_neutral"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/strategy_response.py:158-186 appends 'transition_weakening', 'transition_warning', 'high_transition_risk', and 'sideways_stress' to modifiers_applied
- **Why it violates the spec:** §10.3 enumerates exactly seven scenario names and §10.4 defines exactly six modifiers. The code emits four additional modifier names that appear nowhere in §10.3/§10.4. These are V2-owned score-band states plus the sideways_stress→watch mapping which the V2 spec §4 defines, and §10.4 says strategy response consumes the V2-owned transition_risk.state. So this is governed by V2 — but a reader auditing strictly against the V1 §10.3 precedence list finds modifier names with no V1 precedence rank, leaving their conflict-resolution order against the six V1 scenarios spec-undefined in V1 text.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / medium
- **Minimal fix:** No code change required if V2 ownership is accepted; otherwise add a V1 spec note (or cross-reference) enumerating the V2-owned modifier names and their precedence rank relative to the six §10.4 scenarios so the emitted modifiers_applied vocabulary is fully specified.
- **Test to add/update:** Add a test asserting the full closed set of possible modifier names emitted by build_strategy_response is exactly the documented union of V1 §10.4 names plus the V2-owned names, so any new/renamed modifier is caught.

#### F-044 — §11 canonical data_quality includes "reason": null, but the emitted V1 wire omits the reason key entirely (exclude_none)
- **Spec:** §11 — ""data_quality": { "status": "ok", "freshness_days": 0, "completeness": 1.0, "reason": null }"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/wire_models.py:72-81 (model_dump defaults exclude_none=True); tests/fixtures/v1_frozen_outputs/2024-04-15.json:31-35 (data_quality has no "reason" key); src/regime_detection/classification_status.py:18-24 (reason: str \| None = None)
- **Why it violates the spec:** The §11 canonical block shows data_quality with an explicit "reason": null member on every axis. The live wire serializes with exclude_none=True, so when reason is None the key is dropped rather than emitted as null; the archived frozen fixtures confirm the key is absent. §11.1 documents exclude_none for V2 optional top-level fields but does not explicitly extend that omission rule to the nested data_quality.reason shown as null in the §11 example. The result is a shape divergence between the §11 canonical JSON and the actual wire — cosmetic and self-consistent against the archived fixtures.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / medium
- **Minimal fix:** Either (a) document in §11/§11.1 that null-valued data_quality.reason is omitted from the wire via exclude_none (preferred — matches existing behavior), or (b) if literal §11 shape is normative, stop excluding data_quality.reason.
- **Test to add/update:** Add an assertion in the frozen-replay suite that for ok-status axes data_quality contains exactly {status, freshness_days, completeness} and never a null reason, codifying the omission contract.

#### F-045 — Ambiguity Log #9 cites axis_series.py but the pinned KeyError/None logic actually lives in axis_builders/network_fragility.py (stale citation)
- **Spec:** V2AMBA-009 / Ambiguity Log #9 (§ lines 535-544) — "V1↔V2 axis date alignment (`axis_series.py` v2 classifier). ... Resolution: when the v1 dict is supplied (non-None), a missing session raises `KeyError` (loud failure). The "unknown" fallback is reachable only when the caller explicitly passes `None` for the v1 dict (unit-test path)."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/axis_builders/network_fragility.py:155-172 (KeyError on missing day when dict supplied; "unknown" only when dict is None). axis_series.py:658-662 only forwards the dicts; the pinned logic was relocated.
- **Why it violates the spec:** The named code symbol (axis_series.py v2 classifier) no longer contains the pinned alignment logic — it moved into axis_builders/network_fragility.py::build_network_fragility_axis_series. The BEHAVIOR matches the pin exactly (v1 dict supplied → KeyError on missing session; None → "unknown"), so this is a stale citation, not a behavioral drift. The append-only log was not updated when the function was extracted.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / high
- **Minimal fix:** Update Ambiguity Log #9 to cite regime_detection.axis_builders.network_fragility.build_network_fragility_axis_series (the current home of the KeyError vs None-fallback logic) instead of axis_series.py.
- **Test to add/update:** Optionally add a docstring/citation lint that asserts every Ambiguity Log 'Pinned in <symbol>' string resolves to an importable symbol, so relocations surface.

#### F-046 — BOCPD library pinned to a dev pre-release (0.2.dev1) rather than a stable release
- **Spec:** V2 Ambiguity Log #62 (§4.6/§6.3) — "The Adams-MacKay 2007 online BOCPD algorithm is implemented in `bayesian_changepoint_detection` (PyPI package, last release 2023, pure-Python, MIT-licensed) ... Pinned in `regime_detection.change_point` and declared as `bayesian-changepoint-detection` in pyproject.toml."
- **Code evidence:** pyproject.toml:26 `"bayesian-changepoint-detection==0.2.dev1",`
- **Why it violates the spec:** The dependency is declared and imported exactly as the entry requires (change_point.py:39-43 imports the right symbols; method string stays "BOCPD"). The only deviation is the pinned version is a development pre-release (0.2.dev1) rather than the stable 2023 release the entry describes. The substitution is correct and reproducible; this is a supply-chain/reproducibility hygiene note, not a behavioral gap.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / high
- **Minimal fix:** Confirm 0.2.dev1 is the intended/only PyPI artifact carrying the Adams-MacKay online implementation; if a non-dev release exists, pin to it. Otherwise document in pyproject why a .dev version is the production pin (vendoring or a hash-pinned lock would be stronger).
- **Test to add/update:** A tests/test_source_hygiene.py assertion (or CI check) that the installed online_changepoint_detection symbol is importable and returns a posterior matrix of expected shape, guarding against a future version yanking or reshaping the API.

#### F-047 — §9.1 performance-gate / §10 strategy-improvement: HMM calibration drift compares consecutive in-call refit checkpoints, not the persisted 'prior version'
- **Spec:** V2L56-018 / §6.1 Training — "Compare new model parameters to prior version; alert when state-mean parameter drift exceeds 20%."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/hmm_state.py:319-327 compares each checkpoint's de-standardized means/transmat to previous_raw_means/previous_transmat from the immediately preceding checkpoint in the SAME compute_hmm_features sweep; only latest_drift is retained at :361
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec says to compare new parameters to the 'prior version' — the previously deployed/versioned model artifact — and alert on >20% drift. The implementation compares adjacent PIT refit checkpoints within a single classify_window call and keeps only the most recent pair's drift. Given the engine is stateless and refits per call, an in-call checkpoint-to-checkpoint comparison is a reasonable operationalization, but it is not the same as comparing against the last persisted/versioned model, so a drift between the deployed version and the current fit would not be measured. The field is advisory only (never feeds the runtime score), so impact is low.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / low
- **Minimal fix:** Document (in the module/ADR the spec references) that 'prior version' is operationalized as the previous in-call refit checkpoint; OR, if the persisted-version comparison is intended, load the prior versioned state-mean/transmat artifact and compare the freshest fit against it.
- **Test to add/update:** A test asserting the documented comparison semantics (consecutive-checkpoint vs persisted-prior-version) so the 'prior version' interpretation is locked and cannot silently change.

#### F-048 — profile_manifest provenance gate hardcodes event_calendar as the required manifest input, which the spec text does not state
- **Spec:** V1 final spec §2.1 (manifest provenance bullet) — "Profile-runner calls must set `request_source="profile_manifest"` and pass manifest provenance through `manifest_resolved_inputs` / `manifest_cli_overrides`. Direct calls must not carry manifest metadata."
- **Code evidence:** engine.py:34 `_PROFILE_MANIFEST_REQUIRED_INPUTS = frozenset({"event_calendar"})` and engine.py:250-257 raises `profile_manifest request missing manifest-backed required inputs: event_calendar` when event_calendar is absent
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec requires profile_manifest calls to 'pass manifest provenance' but never enumerates which input names must appear, nor singles out event_calendar. The code elevates a single hardcoded name into a mandatory provenance key, so a runner that legitimately resolved event_calendar via a different manifest channel (or named it differently) would be rejected even though it did pass provenance. The 'direct must not carry manifest metadata' half matches the spec exactly; the profile_manifest half adds a constraint the spec does not state.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / low
- **Minimal fix:** Either (a) document/justify the event_calendar provenance requirement in §2.1 so code and spec agree, or (b) relax the gate to require non-empty manifest provenance for profile_manifest rather than the specific literal 'event_calendar'.
- **Test to add/update:** test_profile_manifest_requires_only_nonempty_provenance: pass request_source='profile_manifest' with manifest_resolved_inputs={'event_calendar'} succeeds and with frozenset() raises, pinning the intended contract.

#### F-049 — V1 config path still runs the full legacy transition-risk state machine then discards the V2-only fields
- **Spec:** V1OUT-029 (V1 transition_risk output contract; V1 frozen-output shape) — "transition_risk output for V1 carries only state and evidence (V1 frozen fixture transition_risk keys = ['evidence','state'])."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/transition_risk_series.py:108-140 (transition_score_config is None branch builds legacy TransitionScoreInputs and calls build_transition_risk_outputs_by_date) and 650-657 (output.model_copy strips score/score_components/primary_drivers to None)
- **Why it violates the spec:** On the V1 path the engine still computes the legacy transition-risk state machine (hard-override flags, debounce) before zeroing out the V2-only fields. This is a simplicity/scope observation, not a correctness defect: the V1 wire output is byte-correct (score fields suppressed via model_copy + exclude_none, and byte-identity replay passes). The spec does not forbid computing-then-suppressing. Flagged only because the legacy machine is dead-weight computation on the V1 path.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / low
- **Minimal fix:** No behavior change is safe or required — the V1 output is byte-identical to the frozen fixtures. Optionally document in transition_risk_series.py that the V1 branch's state-machine result is intentionally discarded except for state/evidence, to prevent a future reader from wiring the suppressed fields back into the V1 wire.
- **Test to add/update:** If documenting, add an assertion in a V1-path unit test that build_transition_risk_series(...) output rows have score is None and score_components is None when transition_score config is None.

#### F-050 — Section 8 red-flag detection omits 'crisis labels missing during obvious crash windows'
- **Spec:** WF-023 (§8 Defensible Label Distribution) — "Red flags that fail review unless explicitly justified: ... crisis labels missing during obvious crash windows;"
- **Code evidence:** scripts/build_walkforward_report.py:425-492 (_red_flags detects label_dominance, long_unknown_run, repeated_one_day_flip_flops, transition_risk_never_fires, transition_risk_almost_always_fires only)
- **Why it violates the spec:** Four of the five §8 red flags are auto-detected and fail the gate, but the spec also lists missing crisis labels during obvious crash windows as a red flag. _red_flags has no crash-window reference set, so an engine that never emits crisis/crash labels during a known stress window (e.g. 2020-03) is not flagged. SHOULD-level gap; cannot be derived from summary distributions alone without a crash-window date list.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / high
- **Minimal fix:** Add a configured crash-window date set (e.g. the §9.4 stress dates) and a red flag 'crisis_label_missing_in_crash_window' that fires when no crisis/crash-equivalent label appears in transition_risk_state/volatility_state within any configured crash window present in the OOS range.
- **Test to add/update:** Add a test building a 252-row summary that spans a known crash window with no crisis label and assert a 'crisis_label_missing_in_crash_window' red flag is produced and the gate fails.

#### F-051 — SOFR/IORB Unknown-Gate uses min-of-three-proxy-pairs, so SOFR/IORB staleness alone does not force unknown when FEDFUNDS-IOER is fresh
- **Spec:** V2L2B-025 / §2C Unknown Gate line 3306 — "SOFR or IORB stale beyond data_quality.max_freshness_days"
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/axis_builders/credit_funding.py:167-186 (funding_spread_staleness_by_date = np.minimum.reduce over sofr_iorb / sofr_ioer / fedfunds_ioer pair staleness) and :220-221 (funding_spread_stale = funding_spread_staleness_days > max_freshness_days)
- **Why it violates the spec:** The Unknown Gate literally lists 'SOFR or IORB stale beyond max_freshness_days' as a forcing condition. The code computes the freshest of three funding-proxy pairs and only forces unknown when ALL of {SOFR-IORB, SOFR-IOER, FEDFUNDS-IOER} are stale. A session where SOFR and IORB are both stale but the FEDFUNDS-IOER legacy proxy is fresh classifies (does not force unknown). This is the intentional ADR 0009 pre-SOFR/IORB splice and the adjacent 'stale carried values still force unknown' clause is satisfied because FEDFUNDS-IOER is a real fresh observation. But it is in literal tension with the line-3306 wording naming SOFR/IORB specifically.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / low
- **Minimal fix:** Either (a) update the §2C Unknown Gate wording to 'funding-spread inputs stale beyond max_freshness_days (SOFR-IORB, or its ADR 0009 SOFR-IOER / FEDFUNDS-IOER fallbacks)', or (b) if SOFR/IORB freshness must be enforced independently post-2021, gate on sofr_iorb_pair_staleness directly when the date is within the SOFR/IORB era. No code change recommended without spec clarification.
- **Test to add/update:** test_unknown_gate_when_sofr_and_iorb_stale_but_fedfunds_ioer_fresh — assert the resulting label (classify vs unknown) so the chosen interpretation is pinned and cannot silently drift.

#### F-052 — Spec defines the 30% transition-prob review flag ambiguously; code uses absolute (percentage-point) change without spec backing
- **Spec:** V2L56-020 / §6.1 Training — "a separate review-flag fires when transition-probability shifts exceed 30% but does not block deployment."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/hmm_state.py:470 max_transition_prob_shift = float(np.abs(aligned_trans - prev_trans).max()); :477 transition_prob_review_flag = max_transition_prob_shift > 0.30
- **Why it violates the spec:** The §6.1 operational-definition code block only defines the relative-change formula for STATE-MEAN drift. For the transition-probability 30% review flag the spec gives no formula. The implementation measures it as the maximum ABSOLUTE change in transition entries (a 30 percentage-point move). The spec phrase 'shifts exceed 30%' could equally mean a relative 30% change. Because the metric drives the review flag, the interpretation is load-bearing. The code's choice is defensible (relative change is unstable near zero probabilities) but is not pinned by the spec.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** partial / low / low
- **Minimal fix:** No code change required if the absolute-shift reading is ratified; instead pin the chosen definition in the spec (or an ADR the spec references). If a relative definition is intended, change line 470 accordingly.
- **Test to add/update:** A documentation/ADR cross-check test (or a parametrized unit test) asserting the exact transition-prob shift definition (absolute percentage-point) the operator review relies on.

#### F-053 — Network-fragility §3.5 rule inputs (21d slope/stability/drawdown) are encoded twice; the scalar path is dead on production yet its docstring claims it ships, and parity is held only by a sparse approximate test
- **Spec:** v1 §0 / v2 §12 First Principle (fast debugging) — "Optimize for capital protection, strategy routing, replayability, and fast debugging."
- **Code evidence:** Scalar encoding: network_fragility_rules.py:174 _trailing_slope (np.polyfit), :193 _trailing_stability, :208 _trailing_drawdown, consumed by :224 build_rule_inputs_for_date. Vectorized encoding of the SAME predicates: :274 _rolling_ols_slope_series, :294 _rolling_stability_series, :315 _rolling_drawdown_series, consumed by :322 build_rule_inputs_by_date. Production imports ONLY the vectorized one (axis_builders/network_fragility.py:21,115); build_rule_inputs_for_date has no production caller. The docstring axis_builders/network_fragility.py:60 wrongly states production uses build_rule_inputs_for_date. Equivalence asserted only by tests/test_network_fragility_rules_precedence_series.py:374-386 over index[20::15] using pytest.approx(nan_ok=True)
- **Why it violates the spec:** The same spec predicates are computed two ways (polyfit vs hand-rolled OLS; tail-window NaN guards vs sliding_window_view). Only the _by_date path ships, yet the production docstring names the scalar one. A future edit to one §3.5 threshold/window can silently diverge the two encodings (the scalar .loc[:dt].tail(window) is index-order dependent; the vectorized path is positional), and the sparse approx test would not necessarily catch it — defeating the §0 single-source-of-truth/fast-debugging intent.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / low / high
- **Minimal fix:** Make build_rule_inputs_for_date delegate to (or be deleted in favor of) the vectorized helpers so the 21d slope/stability/drawdown predicate is encoded once; or, if the scalar form must stay for unit tests, have it call the same _rolling_*_series reducers. Also correct the stale axis_builders/network_fragility.py:60 docstring to name build_rule_inputs_by_date.
- **Test to add/update:** Strengthen the parity test to compare build_rule_inputs_for_date vs build_rule_inputs_by_date on EVERY session date (not index[20::15]) and across an unsorted/duplicated-index DataFrame, asserting exact (not approx) agreement of avg_pairwise_corr_slope_21d, effective_rank_stability_21d, and drawdown_21d.
- **Verifier notes:** CONFIRM: All cited evidence verified accurate. (1) Two encodings of the same §3.5 predicates coexist: scalar _trailing_slope/_trailing_stability/_trailing_drawdown feeding build_rule_inputs_for_date (network_fragility_rules.py:174,193,208,224) and vectorized _rolling_ols_slope_series/_rolling_stability_series/_rolling_drawdown_series feeding build_rule_inputs_by_date (:274,294,315,322). (2) grep confirms production (axis_builders/network_fragility.py:21,115) imports and calls ONLY build_rule_inputs_by_date; build_rule_inputs_for_date in this module has NO production caller (only tests/test_network_fragility_rules_precedence_series.py imports it). (3) The production docstring at axis_builders/network_fragility.py:60 says "materialize the per-day scalar rule inputs (build_rule_inputs_for_date)" but the actual call at :115 is build_rule_inputs_by_date — a genuine factual inaccuracy in the shipping docstring, defeating the §0/§12 "fast debugging" intent. (4) Parity is asserted only by tests/test_network_fragility_rules_precedence_series.py:374-386 over index[20::15] (4 of 80 dates) with pytest.approx(nan_ok=True). (5) Notably, the stronger AST source-hygiene guard test_source_hygiene.py:99-119 (test_bulk_rule_input_builders_do_not_scalar_loc_per_session) protects credit_funding and inflation_growth but EXCLUDES network_fragility, so this axis relies solely on the sparse approximate test. (6) Spec quote verbatim correct at v1 §0 line 13 and v2 §12 line 4759. The finding holds.

#### F-054 — §10.1 increasing-priority modifiers_applied ordering is asserted only for bull_healthy_low_vol pairings, not for the full precedence chain
- **Spec:** §10.1 modifiers_applied ordering — "`modifiers_applied` contains the scenario names that fired in increasing priority order. If multiple scenarios fire, the highest-priority scenario is last and wins conflicts."
- **Code evidence:** src/regime_detection/strategy_response.py:123-202 append order; tests/test_transition_and_strategy.py:145-148,166-169,217-221 only assert ordering for bull_healthy_low_vol + one transition/event modifier
- **Why it violates the spec:** The spec mandates modifiers_applied be ordered by increasing priority with the highest-priority scenario last. The code's append order encodes this, but the only multi-modifier ordering tests pair bull_healthy_low_vol (lowest non-default rank) with exactly one higher modifier. No test fixes the relative order of sideways_chop vs bull_fragile, or sideways_chop vs recovery_attempt, in modifiers_applied. A reorder of the if-blocks could produce a non-increasing-priority list and ship undetected.
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / low / high
- **Minimal fix:** No code change; add ordering coverage for a co-firing pair where both members rank between default_neutral and crisis.
- **Test to add/update:** test_strategy_response_modifiers_applied_increasing_priority: construct an input where sideways_chop and bull_fragile both fire (trend_character='chop', volatility='normal_vol', transition_risk_state='fragile_bull') and assert modifiers_applied==['sideways_chop','bull_fragile'].

#### F-055 — followthrough_rate breakout_level tie-break (20d-preferred) is deterministic but unpinned by spec and untested
- **Spec:** V2L1-007 / §1A followthrough_rate — "`breakout_level` = the max-of-prior-window that close[b] crossed at b."
- **Code evidence:** trend_character.py:191-194: prefers the 20d prior-window max (m20) when close[b]>m20, else falls back to m50, in _compute_followthrough_rate
- **Why it violates the spec:** When close[b] crosses both the 20d and 50d prior-window maxima, the spec phrase does not uniquely select which level to use (the two crossed levels differ; the 50d max >= the 20d max). The code deterministically picks the 20d level (the more lenient hold test), slightly inflating held_count vs choosing the 50d level. Defensible but the spec does not pin it, so the followthrough_rate value (and breakout_expansion firing) depends on an unstated tie-break, with no fixture locking it. (A regression-locking test is captured as a separate finding.)
- **Category / Severity / Confidence:** test_gap / low / low
- **Minimal fix:** No code change strictly required; document the tie-break and add a fixture that locks it against regression.
- **Test to add/update:** Add a deterministic fixture where a session b crosses both its 20d and 50d prior-window maxima, with the subsequent 5 closes between the 20d and 50d levels; assert the documented breakout_level choice (currently 20d → held=True).

### 2a. Confirmed findings — summary table

## 4. Ambiguous Requirements

1. **§7.1 vs §11 (V1L23-003)** — §7.1 directs the engine to OUTPUT a {state:unknown, reason:not_implemented_v1} object for inflation/growth and credit/funding, but the canonical V1 wire schema in §11 (lines 1235-1251) and the StructuralCausalState model emit no such keys at all. The implementation follows §11 (no keys); StructuralCausalState has only event_calendar + monetary_pressure, and the frozen V1 fixtures contain no inflation_growth/credit_funding key.
   - Why ambiguous: The two spec sections directly conflict: §7.1 mandates placeholder objects while §11's authoritative wire contract (enforced by byte-identity replay) omits them. The code cannot satisfy both; it follows the byte-identity-enforced §11.
   - Resolution options: Amend §7.1 to state these axes are simply absent from the V1 wire (matching §11), OR add inflation_growth/credit_funding placeholder objects to the V1 wire and re-freeze fixtures. Lowest-risk option preserving frozen byte-identity is the §7.1 doc amendment. Pin the resolution with a test asserting the V1 structural_causal_state key set is exactly {event_calendar, monetary_pressure}.
2. **§2B Rules / Precedence (V2L2A-050) — risk_off_mild** — risk_off_mild appears in §2B Labels, Precedence (rank-2, directly after recession_scare), Risk Rank, and Hysteresis, but has NO entry in the §2B 'Rules (operational definitions)' block (lines 2982-3071). inflation_growth_rules.py:265-299 evaluate_risk_off_mild invents predicates (credit in {spread_widening,credit_stress}, spy_21d_return in [threshold,0), at least one of cyc/def slope<0 / treasury slope<0 / pmi<50) with no spec anchor; because risk_off_mild outranks goldilocks/recovery_growth, the invented predicate can shadow benign labels.
   - Why ambiguous: The spec lists the label in every table except the operational-definition block, so its firing condition is genuinely undefined; the code's predicate is unverifiable against the spec.
   - Resolution options: Add an operational risk_off_mild rule to §2B (or an ADR) pinning the exact predicate/thresholds the code uses, OR if risk_off_mild is meant to be inactive/deferred, remove it from the precedence walker so it cannot pre-empt spec-defined labels. Until pinned, cite the governing ADR in evaluate_risk_off_mild's docstring and add a precedence test.
3. **§2B Features — CPI trend (V2L2A-051)** — The spec writes cpi_3m_change_pct / cpi_6m_change_pct with a calendar offset (cpi[t - 3_months]/cpi[t - 6_months]), but inflation_growth.py:347-352 substitutes a fixed 63-/126-trading-session shift on a daily forward-filled CPI series (_config_layer2.py:161-162). 63≈3 months and 126≈6, but a fixed session shift does not land on a clean month boundary and can span 2/4 or 5/7 underlying CPI prints depending on as_of_date position.
   - Why ambiguous: The spec formula names a calendar-month offset; the code uses a session-count approximation. Whether the calendar-month or session approximation is normative is not stated, and both are defensible for a monthly forward-filled series.
   - Resolution options: Either document in §2B that the 3m/6m CPI change is a 63/126 trading-session approximation of the calendar-month offset (acceptable for monthly forward-filled CPI), or compute the change against the CPI observation exactly 3/6 calendar months prior (DateOffset(months=3/6)) before forward-filling. Pin the chosen semantics with a synthetic-CPI test.
4. **§1A followthrough_rate breakout_level (V2L1-007)** — When close[b] crosses both the 20d and 50d prior-window maxima, the spec phrase 'the max-of-prior-window that close[b] crossed' does not uniquely select which level to use (the two crossed levels differ; the 50d max >= the 20d max). trend_character.py:191-194 deterministically picks the 20d level (more lenient hold test), slightly inflating held_count vs the 50d choice.
   - Why ambiguous: The spec text admits both interpretations when both windows are crossed; no tie-break is stated, so the followthrough_rate value (and breakout_expansion firing) depends on an unspecified choice.
   - Resolution options: Document the tie-break (20d-preferred) explicitly in the spec, or if the intended semantics is the strictest hold, switch to max(m20,m50) when both are crossed. Either way pin it so the value is reproducible against the spec text. (A regression-locking test is captured as a separate finding.)
5. **§11.1 vs §2A — structural_causal_state.monetary_pressure shape** — §11.1's V2-extended output snippet shows monetary_pressure keyed on `state` ({state, evidence, data_quality}), but the authoritative §2A axis definition (lines 2829-2845) defines monetary_pressure as a normal V2 axis with the raw/stable/active label triple and precedence, and the V2 axis contract pins that triple. The §11.1 example is terminated with `...` (a sketch). The code follows §2A (MonetaryPressureV2Output exposes raw_label/stable_label/active_label, no `state`).
   - Why ambiguous: The two spec clauses disagree on the nested wire key (`state` vs the label triple); §11.1 is likely a stale carry-over of the V1 placeholder shape, but it is not marked non-normative.
   - Resolution options: Reconcile the spec, not the code: amend §11.1's reshaped-fields JSON so monetary_pressure shows the raw_label/stable_label/active_label triple consistent with §2A. If a `state` projection is actually intended for the nested slot, it must be added explicitly and documented (but that contradicts §2A). The shipped §2A shape should be pinned by a regression test (captured as a finding).

## Appendix A — Regression Delta vs Prior Review

Each prior spec_review.md finding re-verified against CURRENT code (code is ground truth, not the prior "resolved" labels).

| Prior ID | Group | Current status | Evidence | Note |

## Appendix B — Refuted / Dropped Findings (transparency)

13 candidate findings were dropped because adversarial verifiers refuted them (majority refute for high/crit; single refute for medium).

| Severity | Category | Spec ref | Title | Why dropped |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| high | edge_case | §3 / WF-008 | event_calendar is passed whole to every session instead of being sliced as-of, risking future-event leakage in the walk-forward runner | REFUTE: The finding's factual code claims are correct (runner passes whole event_df at scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:278-283 while slicing market data at :233-237), but its conclusion of future-event leakage is refuted by the engine's design. The finding self-scopes the leak as conditional on the engine not clipping events as-of; the engine DOES clip, correctly by publication_date rather than event date: event_calendar.py:198 (`if day < publication_date: continue`) gates every painted window day, and event_calendar.py:361 applies the same guard in compute_event_window_just_passed. publication_date is populated in loaders.py:618-650 (scheduled types default to date-90d per the ADR 0002 contract; ad-hoc defaults to date). build_market_context (market_context.py:102-106) deliberately stores the FULL normalized calendar because scheduled-event windows (e.g. fed_week [-2,+2] around FOMC) must fire BEFORE the event date, so the engine must see forward-dated scheduled rows; slicing event_df to date<=as_of_date as the finding implies would be wrong and would suppress spec-required pre-event windows. The economic as-of gate (publication_date <= firing session) is enforced per-row, so no future-information leak occurs. Evidence note: the finding's spec_ref §3/WF-008 is mismatched — in spec_review.md WF-008 is the Minimum-Coverage criterion; the §3 Data Discipline no-leak invariant quoted is WF-005, whose evidence already cites event_calendar and is marked partial. \|\| REFUTE: The finding's own deciding condition resolves against it: "Whether this leaks depends on engine-side as-of filtering of event rows; if the engine does not itself clip events to as_of_date, this is a future-information leak." The engine DOES clip events to as-of, via a publication_date guard, so there is no leak.  Trace of the actual path (runner -> engine): scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:281 passes the whole event_df to engine.classify with lookback_days=1. classify -> classify_request (src/regime_detection/engine.py:474-503) -> build_market_context, which stores the full normalized calendar (src/regime_detection/market_context.py:102-106, 123) without slicing. BUT the only event-label consumer, compute_event_calendar_outputs (src/regime_detection/event_calendar.py:122-253), applies the as-of filter at the point of use: line 198 `if day < publication_date: continue` skips any window day before the event's publication_date, and line 200-202 only writes a label bit for sessions present in session_pos (= context.sessions, which are sliced to <= as_of_date because spy_ohlcv is sliced at market_context.py:343). The vol_crush path compute_event_window_just_passed has the identical guard (event_calendar.py:361-362).  publication_date semantics make this point-in-time-correct: for scheduled types (FOMC/CPI/NFP/ECB/...) publication_date defaults to event_date - 90 days (loaders.py:628-636, ADR 0002 §52 / ADR 0014 R3), modeling the real-world fact that meeting schedules are published ~90 days ahead. So a FOMC dated T+1 painting fed_week onto session T uses only information publicly available at T (the meeting was already announced) and only the scheduled DATE, never the outcome -- so neither "future event outcomes" nor "data not available as of that date" leaks (docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:48-49).  Two dedicated tests prove the intended behavior: tests/test_event_calendar.py:270-306 (forward-dated FOMC 2024-01-19 with publication_date 2023-12-01 correctly labels as_of 2024-01-17 as fed_week -- exactly the scenario the finding flags, and it is intended PIT lead-up), and tests/test_event_calendar.py:309-329 (forward-dated FOMC whose publication_date 2024-01-25 is AFTER as_of 2024-01-17 is BLOCKED -> primary_label expiry_week only). Slicing event_df to date<=as_of_date in the runner (as the finding implies should happen) would be WRONG: it would strip legitimately-published forward-scheduled events and break the designed fed_week/cpi_week lead-up labeling.  Spec-ref note: the finding cites WF-008, but in spec_review.md:482 WF-008 is the §4 "Minimum Coverage" criterion, not the leakage invariant. The actual data-discipline invariant is WF-005 (spec_review.md:479, status "partial"), whose evidence cell already pairs the runner slices with src/regime_detection/eve...(event_calendar.py) -- i.e. the reviewers already attribute event as-of handling to the engine. The spec_quote itself (docs/historical_walkforward_spec.md:49) is verbatim correct and the §3 requirement is a real in-force MUST; it is simply not violated. \|\| REFUTE: The runner passing the whole event_df to every session is the intended, leak-free contract — the engine gates each event's window-painting by publication_date, which ADR 0002 establishes as the correct point-in-time lookahead boundary (NOT event_date). Trace: scripts/run_historical_walkforward.py:281 passes the full event_df -> engine.classify -> classify_request (engine.py:481-499) -> build_market_context stores the whole calendar as normalized_event_calendar (market_context.py:102-123, NOT sliced by as_of_date) -> build_event_calendar_series (axis_series.py:549-553) -> compute_event_calendar_outputs (event_calendar.py:122). Two independent guards prevent any future-event leak: (1) sessions=context.sessions is clipped to date<=as_of_date because spy_ohlcv is sliced at market_context.py:343 (s[s['date'].dt.date <= as_of_date]) and sessions=tuple(spy_ohlcv.index.date) at :119, so output is only produced for sessions <= as_of_date; (2) the publication_date gate at event_calendar.py:198 (`if day < publication_date: continue`) blocks any window-day from being painted before the event was publicly known. The same publication_date gate also protects compute_event_window_just_passed (event_calendar.py:361). For scheduled FOMC/CPI/NFP rows missing publication_date, the loader defaults it to event_date - 90 days (loaders.py:628-636 / ADR 0002 §52), matching the real-world ~90-day advance schedule release. ADR 0002 §10/§19 explicitly states: 'Scheduled event dates may be used even when event_date > as_of_date, but only when publication_date <= as_of_date ... publication date is the real lookahead boundary, not event date.' The finding's implied fix (slice events by event_date <= as_of_date like market rows) would actually BREAK the design by discarding legitimately-known forward schedule information. This exact no-leak property is directly unit-tested: tests/test_event_calendar.py:309-331 (test_event_calendar_blocks_unpublished_future_scheduled_event) proves a future FOMC dated 2024-01-31 with publication_date 2024-01-25 does NOT produce fed_week when classifying as_of 2024-01-17, while :270-307 proves an already-published future FOMC correctly does. The finding's premise — that contrast with sliced market_slice implies a missing as-of filter — is wrong because the as-of filter for events is publication_date-based, not event_date-based, by deliberate spec design. |
| medium | incorrect | v2 §3.7 (Hysteresis) | max_unknown_freeze_days flat floor over-holds benign (deescalation_days=0) stable labels across data-quality gaps, beyond the per-label de-escalation threshold the spec ties the hold to | REFUTE: Code behavior is accurately described but the spec-violation claim does not hold. At hysteresis.py:164-179, for a benign label with deescalation_days=0 the `if threshold > 0` branch is skipped, so hold_limit stays at max_unknown_freeze_days (2 in prod), and the last-known benign label (normal_vol/low_vol) is indeed held frozen for up to 2 unknown sessions before flipping to `unknown`. core3-v2.0.0.yaml:63-67 confirms low_vol:0/normal_vol:0 with max_unknown_freeze_days:2. However, this is NOT a §3.7 violation. The spec quote "It clears immediately once a valid classified label appears" (spec line 3635) refers to `unknown` not being sticky in the RECOVERY direction — proven by spec line 2873 ("unknown: 0 # data-quality absence; clear immediately ON RECOVERY") and spec lines 1066-1068 ("absence-of-signal must clear immediately ONCE A VALID volume/liquidity RULE FIRES"). That requirement is satisfied by deescalation_days_by_label[unknown]=0, not by the freeze window. The spec nowhere requires a valid stable label to flip to `unknown` instantly when a data-quality gap appears; carry-forward/freeze across short gaps is a sanctioned engine construct (hysteresis.py docstring 113-122; golden test test_data_quality_gap_freezes_prior_hysteresis_state_within_window at tests/test_per_label_hysteresis.py:305-361; v2 config pins max_unknown_freeze_days:2 on all 9 axes). The §3.7 second sentence establishes a per-label FLOOR for high-risk states (correlation_to_one:5), and the code takes max(flat_floor, threshold-1) precisely so that floor is never under-honored — it does not forbid a small uniform freeze of benign states. The finding even concedes max_unknown_freeze_days is not a spec construct, but an out-of-spec engine convention that is documented and tested is not a spec violation. Note: the cited spec_review.md F-038 finding is the OPPOSITE concern (premature exit from high-risk states), which the current max(hold_limit, threshold-1) logic already remediates. The finding mis-reads "clears immediately on recovery" as "flips to unknown immediately on a data gap." |

"unknown" is a real CreditFundingLabel (network_fragility_rules.py:113-122) distinct from None. The dependency contract codifies this: absent_policy="pass_none_to_falsify_predicate" vs unknown_policy="pass_unknown_label" (axis_series.py:236-238). So None occurs ONLY when the whole dict is omitted (axis unwired = per-deployment); a wired axis never yields None for a session. The two cases are NOT conflated — they are distinct in the data. The behavior the finding labels a violation (systemic episodes → systemic_stress_unconfirmed when the credit axis is unwired) is the explicitly intended, tested (test_network_fragility_rules.py:292-312), evidence-reasoned ("credit_funding_unavailable") fail-closed path, which the finding itself concedes is "the correct fail-closed direction."
