| medium | partial | SR-005 (§1 L30, §7 L158-159) | Replay verification compares parsed-JSON dicts, not byte-identity / stored output_sha256 | REFUTE: The finding misreads the spec's "exactly" as a byte-identity requirement; the spec actually defines replay equality as SEMANTIC equality, which the code correctly implements.  Code (confirmed accurate): scripts/run_shadow_replay_check.py:161 parses the replayed output via json.loads(replayed_output.model_dump_json(indent=2)); :173-174 parses the stored JSON via json.loads(Path(output_path).read_text()); :176 compares structurally with _diff_values. The stored output_sha256 (written at shadow_storage.py:250-256 via sha256_file) is indeed never read in the replay path. So the finding's code description is factually correct.  But the spec does NOT require byte-identity or sha256-based replay verification: - shadow_runner_spec.md §7 L159 says literally "Compare the replayed output to the stored JSON output" — comparing to the JSON output (what the code does), not to a byte hash. - shadow_runner_spec.md §3 L127-131 is decisive: "v2_dependency_payload_contracts ... is part of replay equality: if the model output is byte-stable but dependency payload semantics drift, replay must report a mismatch." This explicitly frames replay equality as SEMANTIC, not byte, and demands catching drift that a byte/sha256 hash CANNOT catch. The code directly implements this by injecting v2_dependency_payload_contracts (:164) and rule_provenance (:172) into the structural comparison. - §1 L30 "reproduce the stored output exactly" must be read against §3 L130, i.e. exact VALUE equality of the JSON, which _diff_values provides. - output_sha256 is stored per §3 L122 as part of the immutable run ledger (integrity/immutability), never designated by the spec as the replay oracle.  Moreover, the finding's premise that byte-identity "incidentally holds because both sides use canonical json.dumps" is itself wrong: the writer serializes via model_dump(mode="json") + json.dumps(indent=2, sort_keys=True) + trailing "\n" (run_shadow_regime.py:188,196-199), while the replay serializes via model_dump_json(indent=2) with no sort_keys and no trailing newline (run_shadow_replay_check.py:161). These are NOT byte-identical (key ordering and trailing newline differ), so a byte/sha256 comparison would FALSELY flag every replay as a mismatch. Structural comparison is therefore not merely acceptable — it is the correct and necessary design under this spec.  The cited code lines are accurate, but the spec interpretation underpinning the finding is wrong, so the finding does not hold. |

| low | conflict | v1 §2.7 (NaN Handling Rule / Cold Start) | Data-quality freeze emits a real regime label for stable_label/active_label on insufficient/stale sessions, contradicting §2.7's hard rule that all three labels be "unknown" | REFUTE: The code behavior is described accurately but the spec-violation characterization is wrong. The finding frames this as a §2.7 "hard rule" violation, but §2.7 and §3.7 operate at different pipeline layers and do not conflict.  VERIFIED CODE: axis_series.py:607-617 — on quality_forces_unknown(dq), raw_label="unknown" always, while stable_label/active_label = the frozen prior known label only when is_frozen. hysteresis.py:161-188 holds last_known_stable/last_known_active when data_gap_count <= hold_limit, where hold_limit = max(max_unknown_freeze_days, threshold-1) (lines 164-170). The frozen-label emission is real.  WHY THE §2.7 CONFLICT CLAIM FAILS: 1. §2.7 (v1 spec lines 225-254) is the PER-CLASSIFIER cold-start contract. Its implementation pattern (lines 250-254: "return unknown, then evaluate rules only on non-NaN data") governs the RAW rule-evaluation layer. The code honors §2.7 in full: raw_label is forced to "unknown" on every DQ-forced-unknown session (axis_series.py:609). 2. §3.7 (v2 spec lines 3634-3638) is a SEPARATE, deliberate post-classification hysteresis layer that explicitly states: "Data-quality flickers away from high-risk classified states are still held by the threshold of the stable label being left, for example correlation_to_one: 5." This directly AUTHORIZES holding the label across DQ flickers. It is not silent and does not defer to §2.7 — it was written for exactly this scenario. 3. The codebase's own governance ratifies the hold as REQUIRED, not forbidden: V2L34-022 (spec_review.md:382) maps §3.7's DQ-flicker hold to an "acceptance_criteria \| MUST"; ADR 0010 (lines 64-68) confirms "transient drops from high-risk classified labels remain debounced by the high-risk label's own threshold." So holding stable/active labels is a deliberate capital-protection feature, not a §2.7 breach. 4. The finding's sub-claim that holding active_label is unauthorized is weak: active_label is derived as max(raw, stable) by risk-rank (hysteresis.py:235-238), so holding active follows mechanically from holding stable, which §3.7 permits.  THE GENUINE RESIDUAL CONCERN IS ALREADY CAPTURED ELSEWHERE: The finding's only factually-correct novel point is that benign states are also held via the flat max_unknown_freeze_days:2 floor (hold_limit=max(2, threshold-1) holds even when deescalation=0). But that is precisely F-038 in the codebase's own spec-compliance review (spec_review.md:543, 654) — classified as a §3.7 HYSTERESIS-MECHANISM defect ("flat freeze window vs per-label threshold; key the hold on the label being left"), NOT a §2.7 hard-rule conflict. So the real issue is (a) already known and (b) mis-categorized by this finding as a §2.7 conflict.  There is no spec governing max_unknown_freeze_days by name (grep of docs/ and ADRs found zero references), but §3.7's DQ-flicker-hold language is the operative authorization, and the codebase review treats the hold as spec-mandated. The "§2.7 vs §3.7 conflict shipping non-unknown labels on NaN sessions" framing is therefore not supported: the two specs are layered, not contradictory, and raw_label (the §2.7-governed output) is correctly unknown. \|\| REFUTE: The finding misreads §2.7's scope. §2.7 (v1 spec lines 225-255) is a hard rule on the CLASSIFIER'S per-session output at cold-start ("insufficient history at the start of a backtest"; reason=insufficient_history/required_feature_is_nan). The freeze code DOES satisfy it: axis_series.py:609 sets raw_label="unknown" on every quality-forced-unknown session, and at true cold-start (no warm-up) hysteresis.py:180-188 emits unknown for all three labels because last_known_stable is None. The freeze only holds a prior label MID-SERIES after warm-up (hysteresis.py:171-179, gated on last_known_stable/last_known_active not None) — i.e. the data-quality flicker scenario, not §2.7's cold-start scenario. That mid-series hold is EXPLICITLY authorized by the in-force V2 spec §3.7 (docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md:3636-3638): "Data-quality flickers away from high-risk classified states are still held by the threshold of the stable label being left, for example correlation_to_one: 5." The active_label hold is not an independent violation — it falls out of the standard hysteresis active_label formula (active=stable when raw is not riskier) applied to the held stable, which the spec defines (§2.10) and §3.7 endorses. The V2 spec repeatedly affirms it inherits §2.7 verbatim (v2 lines 231, 379, 882) but every reference is to the raw/cold-start classifier output, never to the cross-session debounce layer. Decisively, the repo's own authoritative spec_review.md already covers this exact seam as F-038 (spec_review.md:543, 766), which treats the hold-during-DQ-flicker as REQUIRED behavior per §V2L34-021/ADR 0010 and prescribes holding for the per-label de-escalation threshold (up to 5 days on high-risk labels). The finding's premise that ANY non-unknown label during a DQ-forced unknown violates §2.7 is incoherent with that accepted fix. The only genuine residual issue — the flat max_unknown_freeze_days:2 floor holding benign 0-day-threshold labels for up to 2 sessions — is precisely F-038, already tracked, and is a mis-keying of a sanctioned mechanism, not a §2.7 hard-rule violation. \|\| REFUTE: The freeze does not violate §2.7 as claimed. (1) Scope: V1 §2.7 (docs/regime_engine_v1_final_spec.md:225-255) is titled "NaN Handling Rule (Cold Start)" and its example is "insufficient history at the start of a backtest." The genuine cold-start path is honored — in hysteresis.py the freeze branch (161-179) only fires when last_known_stable/last_known_active are non-None, i.e. AFTER a valid label has been produced; during true cold start they are None and the code returns all-three-unknown (180-188). So §2.7's literal cold-start scenario is NOT violated. (2) Authorization: the mid-series transient-gap hold is a deliberately ratified V2 design, documented in V2 §3.7 (docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md:3634-3638: "Data-quality flickers away from high-risk classified states are still held by the threshold of the stable label being left") AND ADR 0010 (docs/decisions/0010-...md:64-68: de-escalation keyed on the stable label being left so transient drops from high-risk classified labels stay debounced). V2 inherits §2.7 in 20+ places but defines the hold-across-gaps behavior here. (3) The active_label/benign-state sub-claims are weak: the spec's hysteresis model couples active to the held stable label, and max_unknown_freeze_days:2 is an intentionally-shipped config knob (src/regime_detection/configs/core3-v2.0.0.yaml:43,56,67,77) with a pinning test (tests/test_axis_series.py:213-216 asserts stable=active=bear, data_quality_freeze=True). The behavior is designed, config-driven, and tested — governed/satisfied by the later V2 spec, not an accidental violation. At most this is a V1-doc cross-reference nit (low), not a high-severity shipped conflict. |
| low | missing | V2L56-023 / §6.2 Model + §6 registry | GMM clustering has no K-Means fallback when GMM convergence is unstable; unstable fits return None and become a hard RuntimeError instead of the spec-authorized fallback | REFUTE: The spec does NOT mandate the K-Means fallback. §6.2 line 4499 (docs/regime_engine_v2_spec.md) says "K-Means is an *acceptable* fallback when GMM convergence is unstable" — permissive ("acceptable"), not MUST/SHALL. The registry line 4356 says "GMM by default; K-Means *only* as fallback," which constrains K-Means to a fallback role, not a mandate that the fallback must exist. The actual spec_review requirement covering the §6.2 Model clause (V2L56-028, spec_review.md:442) is already marked "implemented" by shipping GMM via sklearn; reviewers treated K-Means fallback as optional, consistent with the clustering.py:9-11 docstring ("K-Means fallback is a future option for a follow-up slice") and the single K-Means/GMM slice in docs/v2_slice_gate_checklist.md:5. The mechanical chain the finding describes is real: clustering.py:154-164 catches the GMM fit exception and continues, :179-180 returns None when no checkpoint succeeds, and transition_risk_series.py:157-162 raises RuntimeError when feature_store.clustering is None. But that RuntimeError is the spec-INTENDED behavior: §6 lines 4345-4349 explicitly state that once transition_score is enabled, "missing HMM, cluster/GMM, or change-point evidence is a hard data-quality failure, not an optional omitted component." The spec WANTS missing mandatory evidence to fail loud (consistent with AGENTS.md:33 "Deterministic errors... propagate loud"). The finding inverts this — treating the spec-prescribed hard failure as the violation. Evidence inaccuracy: the finding cites spec_ref V2L56-023, but that row (spec_review.md:437) is §6.1 HMM State-to-Label Mapping, unrelated to GMM K-Means fallback; the correct row is V2L56-028. No MUST requirement obligates implementing K-Means, so this is not a spec-compliance violation. |
| low | partial | §2A Release Timestamp Handling (V2L2A-018) | §2A first-release/latest-revision vintage storage not implemented for DGS2/DGS10/broad_usd monetary series; macro replays with latest-revision (lookahead) values | REFUTE: Code reading is accurate (monetary_pressure.py:157-227 + feature_store.py:1054-1059 pass single dgs2/dgs10/broad_usd series with no first-release/latest-revision seam, while inflation_growth.py:218-239 implements a CPI first-release path), but the finding mischaracterizes this as an unaddressed §2A spec violation. The spec's own implementation log entry #73 (regime_engine_v2_spec.md:2598-2650) binds the exact `value_first_release`/`value_latest_revision` clause specifically to CPI ("no V2 metric consumed vintages — inflation_growth read only the latest-revision CPIAUCSL series"), and resolves it with a CPI-only first-release loader + engine substitution. Accepted ADR 0020 F-045 (docs/decisions/0020-v2-prerequisite-and-shadow-scope.md:63-69, dated 2026-05-31) states explicitly: "The V2 §2A dual-vintage implementation is a CPI-only dual-vintage store for first-release historical replay... There is no generic all-macro vintage store in this slice." Thus the §2A clause, as interpreted and resolved by the project's own governing documents, does NOT require first-release storage for DGS2/DGS10/broad_usd. Data reality confirms the scope: DGS2/DGS10 are daily Treasury constant-maturity yields (effectively un-revised, conceded by the finding) and broad_usd is FRED DTWEXBGS (negligible revision), so the replay/lookahead impact is near-zero. The asymmetry is an accepted, documented scope decision, not an unhandled bug. |
| low | test_gap | §5.7 Hysteresis | No dedicated unit test for §5.7 volatility 2-day de-escalation (crisis_vol/high_vol) | REFUTE: The finding's load-bearing justification is inaccurate. It claims "A regression that changed core3-v1.0.0.yaml volatility de-escalation ... would not be caught by any volatility-named test." But tests/test_v2_config.py:410 (test_v1_yaml_still_loads_with_v1_config_version) explicitly asserts `cfg.volatility_state.deescalation_days_by_label["crisis_vol"] == 2` for the V1 yaml — exactly the §5.7-named label and value. A regression of crisis_vol/high_vol de-escalation in core3-v1.0.0.yaml would fail that assertion. Verified: core3-v1.0.0.yaml:39-48 sets all volatility deescalation days (incl. explicit crisis_vol:2, high_vol:2 keys) and default to 2; spec §5.7 at docs/regime_engine_v1_final_spec.md:618 reads "Escalation to high_vol or crisis_vol: immediate ... De-escalation: 2 stable days required" (quote accurate). The hysteresis engine (hysteresis.py:51-99) is label-agnostic and IS unit-tested for both immediate escalation and N-day de-escalation counting in tests/test_per_label_hysteresis.py (e.g. test_escalation_is_immediate..., test_systemic_stress_requires_five_days_to_deescalate) — generic, so volatility labels exercise the identical code path. The §5.7 contract is therefore covered by: (a) generic engine logic tests, (b) the V1 config-value assertion at test_v2_config.py:410, and (c) golden replay in test_volatility_state.py:19-29. The narrow gap that remains (no test literally named for volatility asserts the 2-day count through the engine with crisis_vol/high_vol) is cosmetic given the engine is generic and the config value is pinned, not the medium-severity capital-protection regression risk the finding asserts. |

## Appendix C — Methodology & Agent Census

- Phase 1 Audit: 17/17 section auditors returned.
- Phase 2 Dimensions: 6/6 dimension reviewers + 5/5 regression workers returned.
- Phase 3 Triage: 83 raw → 68 distinct (+ 5 ambiguities).
- Phase 4 Verify: 68 findings adjudicated; 55 confirmed, 13 refuted.
- Phase 5 Synthesis: executive summary + 6 milestones.
- Dedup notes: 83 raw findings -> 70 distinct canonical findings. 13 raw findings were merged into 6 canonical entries: (1) r32+r42+r66 -> per-session model_instability renormalized away (same transition_score.py:248-258 code, three reviewers, kept the strongest §4.2/§4.0/§10 quote); (2) r37+r57+r68+r77 -> data_outage_specialist 10th-cohort closed-set violation (same cohort_routing.py:35/83-90; the prior crisis-pre-emption framing is resolved, closed-set invention remains); (3) r8+r76 -> breadth_state.py:70 min_periods=63 vs 50; (4) r1+r16 -> engine_version v2.0.0 vs §2.4/§11 literal v1.0.0; (5) r55+r63 -> shadow_storage TEXT vs §3 TIMESTAMP/DATE schema; (6) r40+r70 -> §9.4 golden-date value-vs-presence test gap (r40's transition_evidence is a subset of r70's broader value-check), and r47+r82 -> §5 per-artifact run_timestamp/archive-path provenance (same WF-018/WF-010 root across CSV+JSON+report). Note: r39 (§9.4 'sequence' field skip) was NOT merged into the r40/r70 golden cluster because it is a distinct field/mechanism (an explicit `continue` past the sequence assertion). r44+r79 merged -> walk-forward replay verification path (wrong DB + trusted-external-JSON, same WF-024/WF-016 root); r43 (macro not archived) kept separate as a distinct artifact gap. r49 (no materiality threshold / tie escapes gate, code-logic) and r71 (no failure-path test for the same gate) kept separate because category differs (partial vs test_gap). 6 raw findings were reclassified OUT of findings into the ambiguities list because the spec is genuinely self-contradictory or silent: r10 (§7.1 vs §11), r26 (risk_off_mild undefined operational rule), r27 (CPI calendar vs session offset), r22 (followthrough breakout_level tie-break — the spec-ambiguity half), and r62 (§11.1 vs §2A monetary_pressure shape). r22 and r62 each also retain a residual test_gap/regression-pin finding (locking the shipped behavior) since a concrete code-pinning action exists independent of the spec reconciliation. Severity normalized per rubric: r43/r44+r79 elevated/kept critical (replayability/reproducibility failure that ships unverifiable macro-dependent labels); r56, r30, r19, r64, r45, r70, r71, r46 are high (correctness/capital-protection/unenforced mandatory gate/missing MUST). Findings sorted by severity then category.
